Exception of Quantity vs. Description in Confessions
Ruling that exception of quantity is valid if joined, exception of description is not

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between istithna of quantity and istithna of description in confessions and state the Hanafi ruling on each, including the condition of joining.

Core Idea
Exception of quantity in confessions is valid only if joined; exception of description is invalid even if joined.

When a person confesses to a debt and then makes an exception, the Hanafi school distinguishes between excepting part of the amount (quantity) and excepting a quality (description). The ruling depends on whether the exception is joined to the confession. This passage explains the rule and its rationale, including an exception for involuntary separation and an application to ghasb of a defective cloth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of exception
Determine if the exception refers to a quantity (e.g., a portion of the amount) or a description (e.g., a quality like counterfeitness).
Quantity examples: 'except 100 dirhams'; description: 'except that they are counterfeit'.
2
Check if the exception is joined (mawsulan)
An exception is joined if it is said in the same utterance without a significant pause. If separated, it is not accepted for quantity exceptions.
Involuntary separation due to breath is considered joined.
3
Apply the rule for quantity exceptions
If the exception is of quantity and joined, the exception is accepted and the confession is modified accordingly. If separated, the confession stands as originally stated.
The word 'thousand' covers quantity, and the exception is a verbal act that must be part of the same utterance.
4
Apply the rule for description exceptions
Exception of description is invalid even if joined. The description is not part of the quantity, so the exception does not affect the confession.
Describing the dirhams as counterfeit is a description, not a quantity, so the exception fails.
5
Apply the principle to the ghasb example
If someone confesses to usurping a cloth and then brings a defective cloth, his word is accepted because ghasb is not limited to sound items. This is consistent with the principle that the confession is about the property, not its quality.
The ghasb case illustrates that description (soundness) is not inherent to the act of ghasb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ قَالَ فِي هَذَا كُلُّهُ أَلْفًا ثُمَّ قَالَ إِلَّا إِنَّهُ يَنْقُصُ كَذَا لَمْ يُصَدَّقْ وَإِنْ وَصَلَ صُدَقَ لِاَنَّ هَذَا إِسْتِشَاءَ الْمِقْدَارِ وَالْإِسْتِشَاءُ يَصِحُ مَوْصُولًا بِخِلَافِ الزِّيَافَةِ لِأَنَّهَا وَصَفَ وَاسْتَنَاءُ الْأَوْصَافِ لَا يَصِحُ وَاللَّفْظُ يَتَنَاوَلُ الْمِقْدَارَ دُونَ الْوَصْفِ وَهُوَ تَصَرُّفُ لَفْظِيَ كَمَا بَيَّنَا وَلَوْ كَانَ الْفَضْلُ ضُرُورَةَ انْقِطَاعِ الْكَلَامِ بِانْقِطَاعِ نَفْسِهِ فَهُوَ وَاصْل لِعَدَمِ إِمْكَانِ الْإِحْتِرَازِ عَنْهُ وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِغَضَبٍ ثَوْبٍ ثُمَّ جَاءَ بِثَوْبٍ مُعِيْبٍ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهُ لاَنَّ الْغَصَبَ لَا يَخْتَصُّ بِالسَّلِيمِ
And if he says in all these cases 'a thousand' then says 'except that it is short by so much', he is not believed, but if he said it joined then he is believed, because this is an exception of quantity, and exception is valid when joined, unlike counterfeitness because it is a description, and exception of descriptions is not valid. And the word (thousand) covers the quantity, not the description, and it is a verbal disposition as we explained. And if the separation was due to the necessity of the speech stopping due to breath, then it is connected because avoidance is impossible. And whoever confessed to usurping a cloth then brought a defective cloth, his word is accepted because usurpation is not specific to sound items.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage clarifies the rule of istithna (exception) in confessions. When a person confesses to an amount (e.g., a thousand dirhams) and then says 'except that it is short by such an amount' (i.e., exclusive of a deficit), the exception is only valid if it was said immediately (mawsulan). If said later (mafsūlan), it is not accepted. The reason is that this is an exception of quantity (istithna' al-miqdar), which is valid when joined because the word 'thousand' covers the quantity, and the exception is a verbal modification that must be part of the same utterance. In contrast, describing the dirhams as counterfeit (zyuf) is an exception of description (istithna' al-wasf), which is not valid even if joined because the description is not part of the quantity and would be a change of the subject matter. The text adds that if the separation was involuntary (e.g., due to running out of breath), then it is still considered connected. Additionally, the passage brings in the rule for ghasb of a cloth: if someone confesses to usurping a cloth and then brings a defective cloth, he is believed because ghasb is not limited to sound items.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnā'): An exception or exclusion from a general statement; in iqrar, it modifies the confessed amount or description.
موصول (mawsulan): Said in the same utterance without a gap; connected.
معیب (mu'īb): Defective or flawed; an item with a fault.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a confession of a thousand dirhams, if the confessor says 'except that it is short by 100', but says it separately (mafsūlan), is he believed?
A) Yes, because it is an exception of quantity.
B) No, because exception of quantity must be joined.
C) Yes, because exception of description is valid.
D) No, because exception of quantity is never valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, exception of quantity in confessions is accepted only if joined, while exception of description is never accepted, preserving the integrity of verbal acknowledgments.

Ghasb vs Wadi'ah: Liability Based on Confession
Resolving conflicting claims about whether property was taken as deposit or usurped

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a possessor who admits taking a property is liable for its loss, even if he claims it was a deposit, unless the owner confirms permission.

Core Idea
Confession of taking triggers liability; a later claim of permission is not accepted when denied.

This passage from al-Hidayah tackles a frequent dispute: the owner says the property was taken by force (ghasb), while the possessor says it was given as a deposit (wadi'ah). The ruling turns on which of the two admitted to the taking. By mastering this distinction, you will see how the Hanafi school protects property rights while honouring the evidentiary weight of confessions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the first scenario: possessor says 'I took as deposit' and owner says 'you took as ghasb'. Then the second: possessor says 'you gave as deposit' and owner says 'you took as ghasb'. Note the outcome: liability in the first, no liability in the second.
2
Analyse the confession pattern
In the first scenario, the possessor confessed to taking (a cause of liability) and then claimed permission (idhn). Since the owner denies permission, the possessor's later claim is not credited; his own confession binds him. In the second, the possessor did not confess to taking; he attributed the action to the owner.
3
Apply the burden of proof rule
Whoever asserts a cause of liability against another must prove it. If the possessor admits taking, the cause is established; his claim of permission is a defence that he must prove. If he does not admit taking, the owner must prove ghasb.
4
Compare with the loan (qard) variant
The text contrasts with a case where both agree the taking was with permission, but differ on whether it was deposit or loan. Here the possessor's word is accepted because the cause of liability (loan) is claimed by the owner, who must prove it.
This highlights that the rule is not about the label but about admission of taking.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قَالَ لِأخَرَ أَخَذْتُ مِنْكَ اَلْفَ دِرْهَم وَدِيْعَةً فَهَلَكَتْ فَقَالَ لَا بَلْ اَخَذْتُهَا غَصْبًا فَهُوَ ضَامِنٌ وَإِنْ قَالَ أعْطَيْتَنِيْها وَدِيْعَةً فَقَالَ لَا بَلْ غَصَبْتَنِيهَا لَمْ يَضْمَنْ وَالْفَرْقُ اَنَّ فِى الْفَضل حوَّل أَقَرَّ بِسَبَبٍ الصَّمَانِ وَهُوَ الأخذُ ثُمَّ ادَّعَى مَا هُبْرِنُه وَهُوَ الْاِذْنُ وَالْآخَرُ يُنْكِرُهُ فَيَكُونُ الْقَوْلُ لَهُ مَعَ الْيَمِينِ وَفِي الثَّانِي أَضَافَ الْفِعَلَ إِلَى غَيْرِهِ وَذَالِكَ يَدَّعِي عَلَيْهِ سَيَبَ الصَّمَانِ وَهُوَ الْغَصَبُ فَكَانَ الْقَوْلُ لِمُنْكِرِهِ مَعَ الْيَمِيْنِ وَالْقَبْضُ فِي هَذَا كَالَا خُذِ وَالدَّفْعُ كَالْإِعْطَاءِ فَإِنْ قَالَ قَائِلُ الْأَعْطَاء وَالدَّفْعُ إِلَيْهِ لَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا بِقَبْضِهِ فَتَقُولُ قَدْ يَكُونُ بِالتَّخْلِيَةِ وَالْوَضْعِ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ وَلَوِ اقْتَضَى ذَالِكَ فَالْمُقْتَضِى ثَابِتٌ ضُرُورَةً فَلَا يَظْهَرُ فِي الْعِقَادِهِ سَبَبَ الضَّمَانِ وَهَلَمَا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَالَ اَخَذْتَهَا مِنْكَ وَدِيْعَةً وَقَالَ الْآخَرُ لَا بَلْ قَرْضًا حَيْثُ يَكُونُ الْقَوْلُ لِلْمُقِرِ وَإِن أَقَرَّ بِالْأَحْدِ لأَنَّهُمَا تَوَافَقَا هُنَاكَ عَلَى أن الأخذَ كَانَ بِالْإِذَن إِلَّا أَنَّ الْمُقَرَّ لَهُ يَدَّعِى سَبَبَ الصَّمَانِ وَهُوَ الْقَرْضُ وَالْآخَرُ اَنَّ يُنْكِرُهُ فَافْتَرَقَا
And whoever says to another: 'I took from you a thousand dirhams as a deposit and they perished', and the other says 'No, rather you took them as a usurpation', then he is liable. And if he says 'You gave them to me as a deposit', and the other says 'No, rather you usurped them from me', then he is not liable. The difference is that in the first, he confessed to a cause of liability (taking) and then claimed what absolves him (permission), and the other denies that, so his word is accepted with his oath. In the second, he attributed the act to someone else, and that other claims a cause of liability against him (usurpation), so the word of the denier is accepted with his oath. And taking (qabd) here is like taking (akhdh), and giving (daf') is like giving (i'ta'). If someone says that giving and handing over cannot be without his taking, we say it can be by relinquishing and placing before him. And even if it requires that, the requirement is established by necessity, so it does not appear in the contract as a cause of liability. And this contrasts with the case where he says 'I took them from you as a deposit' and the other says 'No, rather as a loan', where the word is of the confessor, because they agree that the taking was with permission, but the confessed-to claims a cause of liability (loan) and the other denies it, so they differ.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute between two parties over whether property was held as a deposit (wadi'ah) or usurped (ghasb). The text presents two scenarios. In the first scenario, the person in possession says: 'I took from you a thousand dirhams as a deposit, and they were destroyed.' The owner responds: 'No, you took them by usurpation.' In this case, the possessor is liable (damin). The reasoning is that the possessor confessed to taking (a cause of liability) and then claimed that the owner gave permission (idhn) for the deposit, but the owner denies that permission. Since the possessor admitted the taking (which is the cause of daman), his later claim of permission is not accepted without proof; thus the owner's statement that it was ghasb is given weight, and the possessor must pay. In the second scenario, the possessor says: 'You gave them to me as a deposit.' The owner says: 'No, I did not give; rather you usurped them from me.' Here the possessor is not liable. The difference is that the possessor did not admit to taking; he attributed the act of giving to the owner. So the onus is on the owner to prove the usurpation, and the possessor's denial is accepted with oath. The text also clarifies that the terms 'taking' and 'giving' can include constructive delivery (takhliya). It contrasts this with a similar dispute between deposit and loan (qard): if the possessor says he took as deposit and the owner claims it was a loan, the possessor is believed, because both agree the taking was with permission, but the owner asserts a stronger cause (loan) which he must prove. This shows the nuanced rules of burden of proof and claim in Hanafi fiqh regarding confessions and property disputes.

Key Terms
ضامن (dāmin): Legally liable to compensate or pay damages.
اقرار (iqrār): A legal confession or acknowledgment that creates rights and obligations against the confessor.
اذن (idhn): Permission; in this context, the owner's consent to the deposit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when the possessor says 'I took from you a thousand dirhams as a deposit' and the owner says 'No, you took them as ghasb', what is the ruling?
A) The possessor is liable.
B) The owner is liable.
C) Neither is liable until proof.
D) The judge will ask for witnesses.

Key Takeaway
Confession of taking creates a presumption of liability; the possessor must prove permission to avoid compensation.

Acknowledgment of Possession: Lessor vs. Lessee
Dispute on whose claim is accepted in possession-based contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on acknowledgment of possession in lease/loan vs. deposit and apply the rule of istiḥsān to resolve evidentiary disputes.

Core Idea
In a dispute over possession from lease or loan, Abu Hanifa accepts the lessor's statement because possession is incidental, not intended for ownership.

This lesson explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about whose statement is accepted when one party claims to have leased or loaned an item and the other claims ownership. The source passage from the Hidayah contrasts the deposit case with lease/loan, highlighting the distinction between incidental possession (ḍarūriyya) and intended possession (maqṣūda). You will learn how Abu Hanifa's application of istiḥsān overrides the qiyās preferred by the Sahibayn, and why this ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline deposit case
The passage begins with a deposit scenario: someone acknowledges taking a deposit and then claims it as his own; the depositee denies. Here, the depositee's statement is accepted because the taker acknowledged his possession.
This is the qiyās baseline for the dispute.
2
Recognize the disputed cases: lease, loan, dwelling
The text then presents the main dispute: if someone claims to have leased (or loaned) an animal or garment to another, and the other claims ownership. Abu Hanifa says the lessor's statement is accepted; the Sahibayn say the lessee's statement is accepted.
This difference extends to lending (ʿāriya) and providing dwelling (iskān).
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's istiḥsān reasoning
Abu Hanifa distinguishes lease/loan from deposit: in lease/loan, possession is necessary (ḍarūriyya) only to derive benefit (usufruct), so it does not imply ownership acknowledgment. The lessor acknowledges possession from his own side, so his description of the nature of that possession should be trusted.
Istiḥsān is the juristic preference that departs from the analogy (qiyās) due to this distinction.
4
Understand the Sahibayn's qiyās reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad analogize lease/loan to deposit: since the taker admitted taking the item, that admission is akin to deposit, where the depositee's statement is accepted. They argue that the lessee/borrower should be believed over the alleged lessor/lender.
The Sahibayn's view is the qiyās, but Abu Hanifa's istiḥsān is given preference in Hanafi usul.
5
Apply the distinction to new scenarios (tailoring, debt)
The passage extends the dispute to a tailoring contract: the tailor claims he stitched the garment for a fee and returned it; the owner claims the garment is his. The same difference applies. A contrast is made with debt repayment: if someone claims to have collected a debt, the debtor's statement is accepted because debts are fungible.
This reinforces that the specific identity of the item (not fungible) triggers the istiḥsān ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قَالَ هَذِهِ الْأَلْفُ كَانَتْ وَدِيْعَةً لِى عِنْدَ فَلَان فَاخَذْتُهَا مِنْهُ فَقَالَ فُلَانٌ هِيَ لِى فَإِنَّهُ يَأْخُذْهَا لأَنَّهُ أَقَرَّ بِالْيَدِ لَهُ. وَادَّعَى اِسْتِحْقَاقَهَا عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ يُنْكِرُ فَالْقَوْلُ لِلْمُنْكَرٍ وَلَوْ قَالَ اجَرْتُ دَابَّتِي هَذِهِ فُلَانًا فَرِكَبَهَا وَرَدَّهَا أَوْ قَالَ اجَرْتُ تَوبِي هَذَا فَلَانًا فَلَبِسَهُ وَرَدَّهُ وَقَالَ فُلَانٌ كَذَّبَتَ وَهُمَا لِي فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهُ وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ وَقَالَ ابويُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلُ الَّذِى أُخِذَ مِنْهُ الدَّابَّةَ وَالتَّوْبَ وَهُوَ الْقِيَاسُ وَعَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ الْإِعَارَةُ وَالْإِسْكَانُ وَلَوْ قَالَ خَاطَ فُلَانٌ تَوبِى هَذَا بِنِصْفِ دِرْهَمٍ ثُمَّ قَبَضْتُهُ وَقَالَ فُلَانٌ الثَّوْبُ ثَوْبِي فَهُوَ عَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ فِي الصَّحِيحِ
ترجمہ: اگر کہا کہ یہ ہزار فلاں کے پاس میرے ودیعت تھے۔ میں نے اس سے لے لئے۔ فلاں نے کہا وہ تو میرے ہیں تو فلاں لے لے گا۔ کیونکہ مقر نے اس کے لئے قبضہ کا اقرار کیا ہے اور اس پر ہزار کے استحقاق کا دعوی کیا ہے اور وہ منکر ہے۔ پس منکر کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ اور اگر یہ کہا کہ میں نے فلاں کو اپنا یہ چوپا یہ اجارہ پر دیا تھا۔ اور وہ اس پر سوار ہوا پھر واپس کر گیا یا کہا کہ میں نے اپنا یہ کپڑ افلاں کو اجرت پر دیا تھا اس نے پہن کر واپس کر دیا اور فلاں نے کہا کہ تو جھوٹا ہے وہ تو میرے ہیں ۔ قول مقر کا ہو گا۔ اور یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ قول اس کا ہو گا جس سے چوپایہ یا کپڑا لیا گیا ہے اور قیاس بھی یہی ہے اور اسی اختلاف پر ہے عاریت دینا اور مکان میں بسانا۔ اور اگر کہا کہ فلاں نے میرا یہ کپڑا انصف درہم کے عوض سیا۔ پھر میں نے اس کو اپنے قبضہ میں لے لیا اور فلاں نے کہا کہ کپڑا تو میرا ہے۔ تو صحیح قول میں یہ بھی اسی اختلاف پر ہے۔
وَجْهُ الْقِيَاسِ مَا بَيَّنَّاهُ فِي الْوَدِيْعَةِ وَجْهُ الْإِسْتِحْسَانِ وَهُوَ الْفَرْقُ اَنَّ الْيَدُ فِي الْإِجَارَةِ وَالْإِعَارَةِ ضُرُورِيَّةٌ تَثْبُتُ ضُرُورَةُ إِسْتِفَاءِ الْمَعْقُودِ عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ الْمَنَافِعُ فَيَكُونُ عَبْدَ مَا فِيمَا وَرَاءَ الضُّرُورَةِ فَلَا يَكُونُ إِقْرَارًا لَهُ بِالْيَدِ بِالْيَدِ مطلق بخلا فِي الْوَدِيعَةِ لِاَنَّ الْيَدَ فِيهَا مَقْصُودَةٌ وَالْإِبْدَاعُ إِثْبَاتُ الْيَدِ قصد لِلْمُودَع وَوَجْهُ اخَرَ اَنَّ فِي الْإِجَارَةِ وَالْإِعَارَةِ وَالْإِسْكَان أَقَرَّ بِيَدِ ثَابِتَةٍ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ فَيَكُونُ الْقَوْلُ كَيْفِيَّتِهِ وَلَا كَذَالِكَ فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الْوَدِيْعَةِ لِأَنَّهُ قَالَ فِيْهَا كَانَتْ وَدِيْعَةً وَقَدْ تَكُونَ مِنْ غَيْرِ صُنْعِهِ حَتَّى لَوْ قَالَ أَوْ دَعْتُهَا كَانَ عَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ وَلَيْسَ مَدَارُ الْفَرْقِ عَلَى ذِكْرِ الْاَحْدِ فِى طَرَفِ الْوَدِيْعَةِ وَعَدَمِهِ فِي الطَّرَفِ الْآخَرِ وَهُوَ الْإِجَارَةُ وَاخْتَاهَا لِأَنَّهُ ذَكَرَ الْأَخْذَ فِي وَضْعِ الطَّرَفِ الْآخَرِ وَهُوَ الْإِجَارَةُ فِي كِتَابِ الْإِقْرَارِ أَيْضًا وَهَذَا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَالَ اقْتَضَيْتُ مِنْ فُلَانِ اَلْفَ دِرْهَم كَانَتْ لِى عَلَيْهِ أَوْ أَقْرَضْتُهُ أَلْفًا ثُمَّ اَخَذْتُهَا مِنْهُ وَانْكَرَ الْمُقَرَّ لَهُ حَيْثُ يَكُونُ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهُ لِاَنَّ الدُّيُونَ تُقْضَى بِأَمْثَالِهَا وَذَالِكَ إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ بِقَبْضِ مَضْمُونِ فَإِذَا أَقَرَّ بالْإِقْتِضَاءِ فَقَدْ أَقَرَّ بِسَبَبٍ الصَّمَانِ ثُمَّ اَدَّعَى تَمْلِكُه عَلَيْهِ بِمَا يَدْعَيْهِ عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الدَّيْنِ مُقَاصَّةً وَالْآخَرُ يُنْكِرُهُ أَمَّا هَهُنَا الْمَقْبُوضُ عَيْنُ مَا ادَّعَى فِيْهِ الْإِجَارَةَ وَمَا أَشْبَهَهَا فَافْتَرَقَا
If he says: 'This thousand was a deposit with me at so-and-so, then I took it from him,' and so-and-so says: 'It is mine,' then he will take it because he acknowledged possession for him and claimed entitlement over him, and he denies; so the statement is for the denier. And if he says: 'I leased this animal of mine to so-and-so, and he rode it and returned it,' or he says: 'I leased this garment of mine to so-and-so, and he wore it and returned it,' and so-and-so says: 'You lie, they are mine,' then his statement is his statement, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The statement is of the one from whom the animal and garment were taken, and that is the analogy. And on this difference are lending and providing dwelling. And if he says: 'So-and-so stitched this garment of mine for half a dirham, then I took possession of it,' and so-and-so says: 'The garment is my garment,' then it is on this difference in the correct view. The basis of analogy is what we explained in the deposit. The basis of juristic preference is the distinction: that possession in lease and lending is necessary, established by necessity of deriving the contracted benefit, which is the usufruct, so it is as non-existent beyond the necessity, so it is not an acknowledgment of possession for him, unlike in the deposit, because possession therein is intended, and depositing is establishing possession intentionally for the depositee. And another basis: that in lease, lending, and providing dwelling, he acknowledged a possession established from his own side, so his statement is accepted about its modality, not so in the case of deposit because he said therein it was a deposit, and it may be without his action; even if he said 'I deposited it,' it would be on this difference. And the pivot of the distinction is not on mentioning the taking in one side (deposit) and not in the other side (lease and its like), because he mentioned the taking in the other side, i.e., lease, in the Book of Acknowledgment as well. And this is contrary to the case when he says: 'I collected from so-and-so a thousand dirhams that were owed to me' or 'I lent him a thousand then took it from him,' and the acknowledged one denies, where his statement is his statement, because debts are paid with their equivalents, and that is only with possession of a guaranteed thing. So when he acknowledges collection, he has acknowledged a cause of guarantee, then he claims ownership over it by way of set-off for the debt he claims against him, and the other denies it. As for here, the taken thing is the very thing he claimed the lease and the like in, so they differ.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah deals with disputes arising from acknowledgment (iqrār) of possession. It begins with a clear case: if someone admits taking a deposit from another and then claims ownership, but the depositee denies, the depositee's statement is accepted because the taker acknowledged his possession. The central dispute concerns lease (ijāra), loan (ʿāriya), and providing dwelling (iskān). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the statement of the person who claims to have leased out the item is accepted (the lessor), due to istiḥsān (juristic preference). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the statement of the person from whom the item was taken (the alleged lessee) is accepted, which is the ruling by qiyās (analogy) based on the deposit case. The same difference applies to ʿāriya and iskān. The text then extends this to a tailoring contract. The commentary explains the reasoning: in lease/loan, possession is incidental and necessary only for deriving benefit, so it does not imply ownership acknowledgment; in deposit, possession is the primary purpose. Another distinction: in lease/loan, the person acknowledges possession that originates from his own action (he gave it on lease), so his statement about the nature of that possession prevails. In deposit, the acknowledgment does not necessarily imply his own action. Finally, a contrast is made with debt cases: if someone acknowledges receiving money but claims it was repayment of a debt, the denier's statement is accepted because debts are satisfied by equivalents; here the item is specific, not fungible. This lesson illustrates the Hanafi method of combining qiyās and istiḥsān to reach nuanced rulings.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrār): Legal acknowledgment of a right or liability; here specifically acknowledging possession or a contract.
اليد (al-yad): Possession or control over an item; the fact of having physical custody.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that departs from qiyās due to a stronger consideration; used here to prefer lessor's statement.
مقر (muqirr): The person who makes the acknowledgment (the one claiming to have leased or deposited).
مقر له (muqarr lahu): The person in whose favor the acknowledgment is allegedly made (the lessee/depositee).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, whose statement is accepted when a lessor claims he leased an animal and the alleged lessee claims ownership?
A) The lessor's statement is accepted.
B) The lessee's statement is accepted.
C) Both statements are rejected and the case is dismissed.
D) The animal is divided equally.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when a lessor/lender claims the item was leased/loaned and the lessee/borrower claims ownership, the lessor/lender's statement is accepted because possession in such contracts is incidental, not indicative of ownership.

intermediate
10 min
The Basis for Distinction Between Wadi‘ah and Ijarah in Acknowledgment
Explaining that the ruling difference hinges on possession, not wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school distinguishes acknowledgment of deposit from acknowledgment of ijarah based on the nature of possession, and evaluate the refutation of the wording-based distinction.

Core Idea
The ruling difference in acknowledgment hinges on whether full or limited possession is acknowledged, not on the phrasing used.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a person acknowledges that another held an item as a deposit, the depositee must return it. But when the acknowledgment concerns a hire or loan, the hirer or borrower is not obliged to return immediately. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this distinction, showing that it rests on the type of possession (qabd) acknowledged, not on the specific words uttered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acknowledgment scenarios
Note the two contexts: acknowledgment of a deposit (wadi‘ah) and acknowledgment of ijarah/‘ariyah. In deposit, returning is wajib; in ijarah, it is not wajib.
The ruling difference is the central issue.
2
Understand the initial objection
The passage raises an objection: a deposit can occur without the owner's action (e.g., a finder holds a lost item). Why then is return wajib upon acknowledgment? The answer is that the depositee's possession is still full, even if not given by the owner.
This clarifies that 'action' refers to the acknowledger's action.
3
Examine the wording-based distinction
‘Ali ibn Musa al-Tammi argued that the difference is due to the word 'akhadha' (he took) used in deposit, implying a consequence of return, versus 'radda' (he returned) in ijarah.
This view is presented before being refuted.
4
Analyze the refutation and the correct criterion
The author refutes the wording-based view by citing Imam al-Mahamili, who used 'akhadha' in both contexts yet the ruling differs. The real basis is the type of possession: full possession in deposit, limited possession in ijarah.
Possession (qabd) is the decisive factor.
5
Contrast with loan (qard)
Acknowledgment of a loan implies a guarantee to return the like, because possession in a loan is guaranteed (madhmun). In ijarah, the same item is returned, not a substitute.
This further illustrates the importance of possession type.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولا كذالك ....اور مسئلہ ودیعت میں یہ بات نہیں ہے کیونکہ ودیعت کی صورت میں تو مقر نے یہ کہا ہے کہ میرے وہ ہزار درہم فلاں کے پاس ودیعت تھے۔ اور اس سے یہ ثابت نہیں ہوتا کہ اسکو قبضہ مقر کی جانب سے ملا تھا۔ اس لئے کہ ودیعت بھی اس کے فعل کے بغیر بھی ہوتی ہے جیسے لفظہ کہ وہ ملتقط کے پاس ودیعت ہوتا ہے۔ اگر چہ لقطہ کے مالک نے اس کو نہیں دیا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کے قول " وقد يَكُونُ من غير صنعه" پر یہ اعتراض کیا گیا ہے کہ یہ قول سابق الايداع اثبات اليد قصدا کے منافی کیونکہ قصد اقبضہ کا اثبات مقتضی صنع ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ دیا گیا ہے کہ مصنع سے مراد منع مقر ہے نہ کہ منع مودع اور قصد اقبضہ کا اثبات صنع مودع کا مقتضی ہے فلا منافاة قوله وليس مدار الفرق .. شیخ محمد بن شجاع بلخی کے شاگردعلی بن موسیٰ تمی عراقی نے فرق واضح کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے کہ ودیعت کے مسئلے میں واپس کرنا اس لئے واجب ہے کہ اس میں مقر نے اخذ تھا منہ" کہا ہے تو اس کی جزاء واجب ہے اور اخذ کی جزاء یہی ہے کہ واپس کرے۔ بخلاف اجارہ واعادہ کے کہ ان میں اس نے فردّھا علی کہا ہے۔ فكان الافتراق في الحكم للافتراق في الرضع صاحب ہدایہ اس فرق کی تردید کر رہے ہیں۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ فرق کا مدار اس بات پر نہیں ہے کہ مقر نے جانب ودیعت میں لفظ اخذ بولا ہے اور جانب اجارہ واعارہ میں یہ لفظ نہیں کیا بلکہ لفظ ردلایا ہے اس واسطہ کہ امام محمل نے کتاب الاقرار میں اجارہ اور اعادہ کی جانب میں بھی لفظ اخذہ ہی ذکر کیا ہے اور حکم وہی بیان کیا ہے جو سابق میں مذکور ہوا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فرق کا مدار لفظ اخذ پر نہیں ہے بلکہ مدار قبضہ پر ہے کہ ودیعت کی صورت میں مقر کی طرف سے دوسرے کے لئے پورے قبضہ کا اقرار اگر چہ وہ مقر کے دینے سے حاصل نہ ہوا ہو اور اجارہ واعادہ کی صورت میں ایک تو صرف بقدر ضرورت قبضہ کا اقرار ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ قبضہ بھی اپنی ہی جانب سے دینے کا اقرار ہے۔ قوله وهذا بخلاف ما یعنی اجاره و غیرہ کا حکم مذکور حکم قرض کے خلاف ہے۔ اس لئے کہ قرضے تو مثل دے کر ادا کئے جاتے ہیں اور یہ اسی وقت ہو گا جب اس کا قبضہ مضمون ہو۔ پس وصولی قرض کا اقرار اپنے اوپر سبب ضمان کا اقرار ہو گا اور اجارہ وغیرہ میں شئی مقبوض مثل نہیں ہوتی بلکہ بعینہ وہی چیز ہوتی ہے۔ جس میں اجارہ کا دعویٰ کیا ہے۔
He said: 'And not likewise...' and the issue of deposit (wadi‘ah) is not like that, because in the case of deposit, the acknowledger said: 'My thousand dirhams were deposited with so-and-so.' And from this it is not established that he received possession from the acknowledger. Because a deposit can also occur without his action, like the word that it is deposited with the finder, even if the owner of the lost article did not give it. An objection was raised against the author of al-Hidayah's statement 'And sometimes it is without his action' that this statement contradicts the earlier mention of establishing intentional possession, because the intention to give possession necessitates action. The answer is that by 'action' is meant the action of the acknowledger, not the action of the depositee, and establishing intention to give possession necessitates the action of the depositee, so there is no contradiction. He said: 'And the point of difference is not...' The student of Shaykh Muhammad ibn Shuja‘ al-Balkhi, ‘Ali ibn Musa al-Tammi al-‘Iraqi, clarified the difference by saying that in the case of deposit, returning is obligatory because the acknowledger said 'he took from me', so its consequence is obligatory, and the consequence of taking is to return. Unlike ijarah and ‘ariyah, where he said 'he returned it to me'. So the difference in ruling is due to the difference in utterance. The author of al-Hidayah refutes this distinction, saying that the point of difference is not that the acknowledger used the word 'akhadha' in the case of deposit and did not use it in ijarah and ‘ariyah but used the word 'radda', because Imam al-Mahamili mentioned in Kitab al-Iqrar in the case of ijarah and ‘ariyah also the word 'akhadha', and the ruling is the same as previously mentioned. From this it is known that the point of difference is not the word 'akhadha', but rather possession (qabd). In the case of deposit, the acknowledger acknowledges complete possession for the other, even if it was not obtained by the acknowledger's giving. In the case of ijarah and ‘ariyah, first, he acknowledges possession only to the extent necessary, and second, he acknowledges that he himself gave possession. He said: 'And this is contrary to what...' meaning the ruling mentioned for ijarah and other is contrary to the ruling of loan (qard). Because loans are repaid with the like, and that only happens when the possession is guaranteed. So acknowledging receipt of a loan is an acknowledgment of a cause of guarantee on oneself. In ijarah etc., the possessed thing is not a like, but rather it is the very thing concerning which the claim of ijarah is made.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah on the difference between acknowledgment of a deposit (wadi‘ah) and acknowledgment of hiring or lending (ijarah/‘ariyah). The core issue is why the depositee must return the deposit upon acknowledgment, while the hirer or borrower is not obliged to return. The commentary clarifies that the distinction is not based on whether the word 'akhadha' (he took) is used, as some argued, but on the nature of possession acknowledged. In deposit, the acknowledger admits that the other party had full possession of the item, even if it was not physically delivered by the acknowledger. In ijarah/‘ariyah, the acknowledger only admits that the other party had possession to the extent needed for use, and that possession was given by the acknowledger himself. The author refutes the earlier distinction based on wording by citing that Imam al-Mahamili used 'akhadha' in both contexts, yet the ruling differs. The passage also contrasts with loan (qard), where acknowledgment of receipt implies a debt of replacement, unlike ijarah where the same item is to be returned.

Key Terms
ودیعت (wadi‘ah): A deposit: one person entrusts property to another for safekeeping without compensation.
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract of hire: one gives the usufruct of an asset in exchange for rent.
قبضہ (qabd): Possession: physical control or constructive control over an item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is returning wajib in acknowledgment of a deposit but not in acknowledgment of ijarah/‘ariyah?
A) Because the word 'akhadha' is used in deposit but not in ijarah
B) Because deposit involves full possession acknowledged, while ijarah involves only limited possession
C) Because deposits are always in cash while ijarah involves property
D) Because the depositee is a trustee while the hirer is a guarantor

Key Takeaway
The distinction between acknowledging a deposit and acknowledging a hire/loan lies in the nature of possession acknowledged, not in the specific wording used.

Acknowledgment of an Act vs. Possession: The Hanafi Rule
Hanafi ruling on acknowledgment of an act without possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that acknowledgment of an act does not imply acknowledgment of possession, and apply it to scenarios of cultivation, construction, or planting on another's property.

Core Idea
Acknowledging an act on property does not acknowledge possession — the act may be done by a hired worker.

In disputes over property, a person may acknowledge that another performed an act—like cultivating land or building a house—on property currently in the first person's possession. The critical legal question is whether this acknowledgment implies that the performer also had possession or ownership of the property. The Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction: acknowledging the act alone does not entail acknowledging possession, and the original possessor's word is accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Parties
Recognize that the muqir (acknowledger) acknowledges an act (e.g., cultivation, building, planting) performed by the muqarr lahu (beneficiary) on property that is currently in the muqir's physical possession.
The property is in the muqir's yad (hand/possession).
2
Examine the Acknowledgment
The muqir only says that the muqarr lahu performed an act—he does not say 'I took possession from him' or 'the property is his.' This is a mere act acknowledgment, not a possession acknowledgment.
The wording is crucial: 'you cultivated this land' vs. 'you owned this land.'
3
Understand the Legal Reasoning
An act can be performed by a hired worker or an assistant while the property remains in the owner's possession. Therefore, acknowledging the act does not logically imply that the performer had possession or ownership.
The act alone is neutral regarding possession.
4
Apply the Analogy
The passage compares to a tailor sewing a shirt: if the owner says 'the tailor sewed my shirt' without saying 'I took it from him,' it does not acknowledge the tailor's possession. Similarly, the muqir's statement is taken as true.
The analogy reinforces the distinction between act and possession.

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on acknowledgment of an act without acknowledgment of possession. The scenario: A person (muqir) acknowledges that another person (muqarr lahu) performed an act (cultivating, building, planting) on property that is currently in the muqir's own possession. When the muqarr lahu claims ownership of the property based on that acknowledgment, the muqir denies and says he only hired the person or sought assistance. The ruling is that the muqir's statement is believed because he only acknowledged the other's act, not his possession or ownership. The analogy given is a tailor sewing a garment while it is still in the owner's possession; acknowledging that the tailor sewed does not imply the tailor had possession of the garment. This principle is important in disputes over property where the claim is based on an act of cultivation, construction, or planting.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): An acknowledgment by a person of a right due to another, which creates a legal obligation.
قبضہ (qabd): Possession; physical control.
ید (yad): Hand; metaphorically possession or control.

Priority of Health Debts Over Terminal Illness Acknowledgments
Establishing the priority of health debts over terminal illness acknowledgments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule giving precedence to debts from health and known causes over debts acknowledged in terminal illness, and contrast it with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Health debts and known-cause debts are stronger because they are proven by external evidence; mere acknowledgment in terminal illness is suspect of defrauding heirs.

When a person in terminal illness acknowledges debts, the Hanafi school does not treat all debts equally. Debts from health and debts incurred with known causes (like purchases or loans) take priority over debts merely acknowledged during terminal illness. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this Hanafi position and the Shafi'i counter-argument, revealing a fundamental difference in how each school views the reliability of acknowledgment in illness.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the exact ruling: Debts from health (diyun al-sihha) and debts due to known causes during illness (diyun ma'rufat al-asbab) are given precedence (muqaddam) over debts merely acknowledged in terminal illness.
The ruling applies when the estate is insufficient to cover all debts.
2
Identify the Shafi'i contrary position
State that Imam al-Shafi'i holds all debts equal, regardless of when they were incurred or how they arose, because the acknowledgment proceeds from a sane, religious person and the dhimma (conscience) can bear all obligations.
The Shafi'i view treats acknowledgment in illness like any other acknowledgment.
3
Analyze the basis of each argument
Hanafi: The acknowledgment in terminal illness is suspect because it could be a stratagem to defraud heirs; debts from health and known causes are proven by external evidence. Shafi'i: The acknowledgment is a rational act from a competent person, so it should be honored equally.
Both schools agree on the capacity of the dying person, but differ on the potential for fraud.
4
Derive the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the estate is insufficient, Hanafi pays health debts and known-cause debts first; Shafi'i distributes all debts proportionally, treating all debts equally.
This difference can significantly affect how much heirs receive.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that health debts and known-cause debts take precedence. This is the position for fatwa.
The text does not provide a Hanafi rebuttal to Shafi'i's argument, but the ruling itself is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ یہ باب بیمار کے اقرار کے بیان میں ہے۔
مریض نے مرض الموت میں دیوان کا اقرار کیا ، اس پر حالت صحت کے دیون اور اس پر حالت مرض اور حالت صحت کے دیون معلومۃ الاسباب ہیں تو حالت صحت اور معلوتہ الاسباب کے دیون مقدم ہوں گے

ترجمہ ... جب اقرار کیا کسی نے اپنے مرض الموت میں قرضوں کا اور حال یہ کہ اس پر کچھ قرضے اس کی تندرستی کے ہیں اور کچھ قرضے ایسے ہیں جو اس کو اس کے مرض الموت میں اسباب معلومہ سے لازم ہوئے ہیں تو تندرستی والے اور اسباب معلومہ والے قرضے مقدم ہوں گے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ بیماری اور تندرستی کے قرضے برابر ہیں ان کا سبب برابر ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ اقرار ہے جو عقل و دین سے صادر ہوا ہے۔ اور وجوب کا محل وہ ذمہ ہے جو قابل حقوق ہے تو یہ با ہمی بیع و نکاح کے انشاء تصرف کی طرح ہو گیا۔
Chapter on the Acknowledgment of the Sick.
Translation: This chapter is about the acknowledgment of the sick person.
If a person in terminal illness acknowledges debts, and upon him are debts from his health and debts that became due upon him in his illness with known causes, then the debts from health and the debts with known causes are given precedence. Imam al-Shafi‘i says: The debts of illness and debts of health are equal because their cause is equal, and that cause is the acknowledgment emanating from intellect and religion, and the place of obligation is the conscience which is capable of rights, so it becomes like initiating a transaction of sale or marriage.
Translation: When a person acknowledges in his terminal illness debts, and upon him are some debts from his health and some debts that became due upon him in his illness with known causes, then the health debts and the known-cause debts are given precedence. Imam al-Shafi‘i says that illness and health debts are equal because their cause is equal – and that cause is the acknowledgment emanating from intellect and religion, and the place of obligation is the conscience which is capable of rights, so it becomes like initiating a transaction of sale or marriage.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on the acknowledgment of a sick person (bab iqrar al-marid). It presents a ruling from the Hanafi school: When a person in terminal illness (marad al-mawt) acknowledges debts, and he also has debts from his period of health and debts incurred during his illness through known causes (like purchases or loans), then the health debts and the known-cause illness debts take precedence over the debts merely acknowledged in terminal illness. This is because debts from health and those with known causes are established with stronger evidence, while the acknowledgment in terminal illness is suspect as it may be an attempt to defraud heirs. Imam al-Shafi‘i disagrees, arguing that all debts are equal because the acknowledgment is a rational act coming from a competent person, and the conscience (dhimma) is capable of receiving rights, similar to initiating a sale or marriage. The Shafi‘i view treats all debts equally. The text does not provide the Hanafi response here, but the Hanafi ruling is that health debts and known-cause debts are preferred.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness: an illness from which the person is expected to die and actually dies.
دين (dayn): Debt: a financial obligation owed by a person.
ذمة (dhimma): Legal personality or conscience; the capacity of a person to have rights and obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) All debts are equally prioritized
D) Debts incurred during illness without known causes

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, debts from health and with known causes are given priority over debts merely acknowledged in terminal illness because the latter are subject to suspicion of fraud.

Prohibition of Gratuitous Transfers During Terminal Illness and Validity of Acknowledgment
Explanation of prohibition and validity with rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why gratuitous transfers (tabarru' and muhabah) are prohibited during terminal illness and distinguish the validity of acknowledgment (iqrar) from heir's right.

Core Idea
Gratuitous transfers harm creditors; acknowledgment creates its own obligation, independent of death.

In this passage, the commentator explains two key rulings regarding the actions of a person in marad al-mawt (terminal illness). First, why gratuitous transfers and below-market sales are prohibited: because creditors' rights are attached to the estate, and these transactions are not essential needs. Second, why an acknowledgment (iqrar) in favor of an heir or of a debt remains valid, even though it may reduce other heirs' shares. The answer lies in the nature of the obligation: inheritance attaches at death, while a debt becomes obligatory by the acknowledgment itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibited acts
Recognize that tabarru' (gift, bequest) and muhabah (favored sale) are both gratuitous transfers. The text says the sick person cannot give away property that is not obligatory, and cannot sell below market value.
Tabarru' includes bequest (wasiyya) and dowry (jahiyya) as mentioned.
2
Understand the rationale: attachment of creditors' rights
The prohibition is due to the rights of creditors (huguq al-ghurama) being attached to the estate. These transactions would deplete the estate needed to pay debts.
This is the core legal reason: creditors have a prior claim.
3
Distinguish the case of acknowledgment (iqrar)
The text asks why acknowledgment in favor of an heir is valid, and why acknowledgment of debt is valid. The answer: the heir's entitlement is based on death, so the acknowledgment is subject to that; debt becomes binding from the moment of acknowledgment.
Thus iqrar is not a gratuitous transfer; it creates a genuine obligation.
4
Analyze the proof: the analogy with witnesses' retraction
The text provides an analogy: witnesses of lineage who testify before death and later retract after death are not liable if the beneficiary took property. This shows that the right (inheritance) attaches at death. For debt, it attaches at the time of acknowledgment, not death.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) clarifying the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولهذا منع ... حق غرماء کی وابستگی ہی کی وجہ سے مریض کو تبرع و محابات کی ممانعت ہے۔ یعنی وہ ترکہ کو نہیں کر سکتا جو اس کے ذمہ واجب نہیں ہیں۔ جیسے وصیت اور جہیہ وغیرہ۔ نیز محابات بھی نہیں کر سکتا کہ مال کو اس کی قیمت سے کم پر کسی کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دے۔ کیونکہ یہ اصلی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ سوال . حالت مرض میں وارث کے لئے اقرار صحیح ہے۔ حالانکہ اس سے دیگر ورثہ کا حق باطل ہوتا ہے۔ پھر مرض کی حالت میں دین کا اقرار کیوں صحیح نہیں ۔ نہ جواب ... وارث جو مال کا مستحق ہوتا ہے وہ نسب اور موت دونوں سے ہوتا ہے تو ان میں سے جو آخر پایا جائے۔ استحقاق اسی کی طرف منسوب ہو گا اور وہ موت ہے۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ قبل از موت نسب کی گواہی دینے والے اگر موت کے بعد گواہی سے رجوع کرلیں اور حال یہ کہ مشہود له مال لے چکا تو گواہ لوگ کسی چیز کے ضامن نہیں ہوتے۔ بخلاف دین کے کہ اس کو وجوب موت کی وجہ سے نہیں بلکہ دین اقرار کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ ( مبسوط، اسرار)
He said: 'And for this reason, [the sick person] is prevented from gratuitous transfers and favored sales because of the attachment of creditors' rights.' Meaning he cannot give away from his estate that which is not obligatory upon him, like bequest and dowry. Also he cannot make a favored sale, selling his property for less than its value, because this is not an essential need. Question: During illness, acknowledgment in favor of an heir is valid, even though it voids the right of other heirs. So why is acknowledgment of debt not valid during illness? Answer: The heir who is entitled to the property has entitlement through both lineage and death; whichever is found last, the entitlement is attributed to that, and that is death. Do you not see that witnesses of lineage before death, if they retract their testimony after death, and the beneficiary has already taken the property, the witnesses are not liable for anything. Unlike debt, which becomes obligatory not due to death but due to the acknowledgment itself.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, from a commentary (shared) on a matn. It addresses the prohibition of two types of transactions during terminal illness (marad al-mawt): tabarru' (gratuitous transfer like gifts or bequests) and muhabah (selling property below market value). The reason given is that creditors' rights (huguq al-ghurama) are attached to the estate, and these transactions are not essential needs. The text then answers a question: why is acknowledgment (iqrar) in favor of an heir valid, even though it harms other heirs, while acknowledgment of a debt is also valid? The key distinction is that the heir's right is established by death, so the acknowledgment is subject to the heir's entitlement; whereas a debt becomes binding due to the acknowledgment itself, not death. Thus both acknowledgments are valid but operate differently. The proof is based on rational analogy: the witnesses' retraction shows the right attaches at death; for debts, the obligation arises from the moment of acknowledgment.

Key Terms
تبرع (tabarru'): A gratuitous transfer of property without compensation, such as a gift or bequest.
محابات (muhabah): Selling property below its market value, a form of concealed gift.
اقرار (iqrar): A confession or acknowledgment of a right or debt, which creates a legal obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is acknowledgment of debt valid during terminal illness?
A) Because it benefits the creditors
B) Because the debt becomes obligatory due to the acknowledgment itself, not due to death
C) Because the sick person is still competent
D) Because it is a gratuitous act

Key Takeaway
Gratuitous transfers during terminal illness are prohibited to protect creditors, but acknowledgment of debt is valid because it creates its own obligation.

Validity of Acknowledgment During Death Illness: The Effect of Prior Debts
Explaining when acknowledgment during illness is valid after paying prior debts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a sick person's acknowledgment of debt during death illness and distinguish between cases with and without prior debts.

Core Idea
A death-illness acknowledgment is valid in itself but suspended until prior debts are cleared; if none, it binds the entire estate.

The Hanafi school holds that an acknowledgment of debt during death illness is inherently valid, but its enforceability depends on the existence of prior debts. The matn of Al-Hidayah presents two scenarios: one where prior debts exist and one where they do not. We will trace the reasoning and the proof from the saying of Umar (RA) that such an acknowledgment is valid against the entire estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two situations
The passage presents two cases: (a) the sick person has prior debts from his health, and (b) he has no such debts. For each, determine the ruling regarding the acknowledgment.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
The acknowledgment itself is valid (sahih), but it was rejected only in consideration of health creditors. Once their right is removed (by payment), the acknowledgment becomes operative. In the absence of prior debts, no right of another is voided, so the acknowledgment is immediately effective.
3
Analyze the proof
The passage cites the saying of Umar (RA): 'When a sick person acknowledges a debt, it is valid against him in all his estate.' This shows that the acknowledgment is not limited to one-third, unlike a bequest. The phrase 'in all his estate' indicates full effect.
4
Consider the broader principle
Paying debt is a primary need (hajah asliyyah). The heirs' right is conditional on the estate being free from such needs. This is why the sick person's need to settle debts takes precedence over heirs' claims, even to the entire estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا قُضِيَتْ يَعْنِي الدُّيُونَ الْمُتَقَدَّمَةَ وَفَضَلَ شَيْءٍ يُصْرَفُ إِلَى مَا أَقَرَّ بِهِ فِي حَالَةِ الْمَرَضِ لِأَنَّ الْإِقْرَارَ فِي ذَاتِهِ صَحِيحٌ وَإِنَّمَا رُدَّ فِي حَقِّ غُرَمَاءِ الصَّحَةِ فَإِذَا لَمْ يَبْقَ حَقُّهُمْ ظَهَرَتْ صِحَّتُهُ قَالَ فَإِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ عَلَيْهِ دُيُونٌ فِي صِحَتِهِ جَازَ إِقْرَارُهُ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَتَضَمَّنْ إِبْطَالَ حَقِّ الْغَيْرِ وَكَانَ الْمُقَرُّ لَهُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْوَرَثَةِ لِقَوْلِ عُمَرَ إِذَا أَقَرَّ الْمَرِيضُ بِدَيْنٍ جَازَ ذَلِكَ عَلَيْهِ فِي جَمِيعِ تَرَكَتِهِ وَلِأَنَّ قَضَاءَ الدَّيْنِ مِنَ الْحَوَائِجِ الْأَصْلِيَّةِ وَحَقُّ الْوَرَثَةِ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالتَّرْكَةِ بِشَرْطِ الْفَرَاغِ وَلِهَذَا تُقَدَّمُ حَاجَتُهُ فِي التَّكْفِينِ
And when the previous debts are paid, and something remains, it is spent on what he acknowledged during his illness, because acknowledgment in itself is valid, but it was only rejected in consideration of the creditors of health. So when their right no longer remains, its validity appears. He said: If he had no debts in his health, his acknowledgment is valid, because it does not entail voiding the right of another, and the acknowledged one is more entitled than the heirs, due to the saying of Umar: 'When a sick person acknowledges a debt, it is valid against him in all his estate.' And because paying debt is among the primary needs, and the right of the heirs attaches to the estate on condition of freedom (from debts), and therefore his need is given precedence in shrouding.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Al-Hidayah presents two related rulings about a sick person's acknowledgment (iqrar) during death illness. First, if the person has prior debts from health or certain causes during illness, those must be paid first; after that, any remaining estate is used to fulfill the acknowledgment he made during illness. The reason is that the acknowledgment itself was valid, but it was suspended due to the rights of health creditors. Once those creditors' rights are cleared, the acknowledgment becomes operative. Second, if the sick person had no debts from his health, his acknowledgment is valid even if it consumes the entire estate. The acknowledged person is preferred over the heirs because acknowledging a debt is a primary need, and the heirs' right is conditional upon the estate being free from such essential needs. The proof is the statement of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that the debt acknowledged by a sick person is valid against his entire estate. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): An acknowledgment of a right or debt owed by the person making the acknowledgment.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A terminal illness that likely leads to death, during which the person's legal capacity is restricted regarding gifts and acknowledgments that harm heirs.
غرماء الصحة (ghurma' al-sihha): Creditors of debts incurred during health, whose claims take precedence over those acknowledged during illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a sick person in death illness acknowledges a debt and has no prior debts from his health, what is the ruling?
A) The acknowledgment is invalid because it may exceed one-third.
B) The acknowledgment is valid but limited to one-third.
C) The acknowledgment is valid even if it consumes the entire estate.
D) The acknowledgment is valid only if the heir confirms.

Key Takeaway
A death-illness acknowledgment is valid in itself, but prior health debts must be paid first; if none exist, the acknowledgment is effective against the entire estate, not limited to one-third.

Acknowledgment for an Heir During Death Illness
Dispute on acknowledgment for an heir during death illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sick person's acknowledgment for an heir and explain why it is invalid unless confirmed by other heirs, using the hadith and the concept of attachment of heirs' rights.

Core Idea
A dying person's acknowledgment for an heir is void unless the other heirs confirm it.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. The issue arises when a person on their deathbed acknowledges a debt or right in favor of one of their heirs. The Hanafi school, relying on a specific hadith and the principle that the heirs' rights attach to the estate during illness, rules such acknowledgment invalid unless the other heirs confirm its truth. Imam al-Shafi'i, in one opinion, considers it valid. Understanding this ruling protects the interests of all heirs and prevents fraud.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the act: acknowledgment (iqrar) for an heir during death illness. State the ruling: it is not valid (batil) unless the rest of the heirs confirm (tasdiq) it.
The default ruling is invalidity; confirmation makes it valid.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i (in one of his two opinions) holds the acknowledgment valid without confirmation.
Shafi'i's reasoning is based on the idea that acknowledgment merely reveals an existing right, and truthfulness should prevail.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
Examine Shafi'i's evidence: he analogizes to acknowledgment for a stranger, for another heir, and for a deposit, arguing that the sick person's word should be accepted.
The analogy suggests that the same principle should apply regardless of the recipient's status.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Study the Hanafi rebuttal: the hadith prohibits both will and acknowledgment for an heir; the heirs' right attaches to the estate during illness, so favoring one heir harms others; transactions with strangers are allowed due to necessity, but transactions with heirs are rare and not essential.
The attachment of rights is a core Hanafi concept: it restricts the sick person's dispositions that could deplete the estate.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf: Under Hanafi, the acknowledgment is invalid unless remaining heirs confirm; under Shafi'i (one view), it is valid without confirmation. This affects how debts are paid from the estate.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (relied upon) and strengthens fairness among heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَوْ أَقَرَّ الْمَرِيضُ لِوَارِثِهِ لَا يَصِحُ إِلَّا أَنْ يُصَدِّقَهُ فِيهِ بَقِيَةُ وَرَثَتِهِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ فِي أَحَدِ قَوْلَيْهِ يَصِحُ لِأَنَّهُ إِظْهَارُ حَقٍّ ثَابِتٍ لِتَرَجُّحِ جَانِبِ الصِّدْقِ وَصَارَ كَالْإِقْرَارِ لِأَجْنَبِيٍّ وَبِوَارِثٍ آخَرَ وَبِوَدِيعَةٍ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا وَصِيَّةَ لِوَارِثٍ وَلَا إِقْرَارَ لَهُ بِالدَّيْنِ وَلِأَنَّهُ تَعَلَّقَ حَقُّ الْوَرَثَةِ بِمَالِهِ فِي مَرَضِهِ وَلِهَذَا يَمْنَعُ مِنَ التَّبَرُّعِ عَلَى الْوَارِثِ أَصْلًا فَفِي تَخْصِيصِ الْبَعْضِ بِهِ إِبْطَالُ حَقِّ الْبَاقِينَ وَلِأَنَّ حَالَةَ الْمَرَضِ حَالَةُ الِاسْتِغْنَاءِ وَالْقَرَابَةُ سَبَبُ التَّعَلُّقِ إِلَّا أَنَّ هَذَا التَّعَلُّقَ لَمْ يَظْهَرْ فِي حَقِّ الْأَجْنَبِيِّ لِحَاجَتِهِ إِلَى الْمُعَامَلَةِ فِي الصِّحَّةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ حُجِرَ عَنِ الْإِقْرَارِ فِي الْمَرَضِ يَمْتَنِعُ النَّاسُ عَنِ الْمُعَامَلَةِ مَعَهُ وَقَلَّمَا يَقَعُ الْمُعَامَلَةُ مَعَ الْوَارِثِ وَلَمْ يَظْهَرْ فِي حَقِّ الْإِقْرَارِ لِوَارِثٍ آخَرَ لِحَاجَتِهِ أَيْضًا ثُمَّ هَذَا التَّعَلُّقُ حَقُّ بَقِيَةِ الْوَرَثَةِ فَإِذَا صَدَّقُوهُ فَقَدْ أَبْطَلُوهُ فَيَصِحُّ إِقْرَارُهُ وَإِنْ أَقَرَّ لِأَجْنَبِيٍّ جَازَ وَإِنْ أَحَاطَ بِمَالِهِ لِمَا بَيَّنَّا وَالْقِيَاسُ أَنْ لَا يَجُوزَ إِلَّا فِي الثُّلُثِ لِأَنَّ الشَّرْعَ قَصَرَ تَصَرُّفَهُ عَلَيْهِ إِلَّا أَنَّا نَقُولُ لَمَّا صَحَّ إِقْرَارُهُ فِي الثُّلُثِ كَانَ لَهُ التَّصَرُّفُ فِي الثُّلُثِ بَاقِيًا لِأَنَّهُ الثُّلُثُ بَعْدَ الدَّيْنِ ثُمَّ وَثُمَّ حَتَّى يَأْتِيَ عَلَى الْكُلِّ
He said: If a sick person acknowledges for his heir, it is not valid unless the rest of his heirs confirm it. Al-Shafi'i said in one of his two opinions: It is valid, because it is the manifestation of an established right, due to the preponderance of truthfulness, and it becomes like acknowledgment for a stranger, for another heir, and for a deposit. Our proof is his statement (peace be upon him): 'No will for an heir and no acknowledgment of debt for him.' And because the right of the heirs has attached to his property during his illness, and therefore he is prevented from making a gift to an heir altogether. So in specifying some of them there is annulment of the right of the remaining. And because the state of illness is a state of need, and kinship is a cause of attachment, except that this attachment does not appear in the case of a stranger due to his need for transactions in health, because if he were prevented from acknowledgment during illness, people would refrain from transacting with him, and transaction with an heir rarely occurs. And it does not appear in the case of acknowledgment for another heir due to his need as well. Then this attachment is the right of the remaining heirs, so if they confirm him, they have annulled it, so his acknowledgment becomes valid. And if he acknowledges for a stranger, it is valid even if it encompasses all his property, for what we have explained. And by analogy it would not be valid except within one-third, because the Law has restricted his disposition to it, but we say: Since his acknowledgment is valid within one-third, his disposition in the one-third remains, because it is one-third after debt, then again and again until it comprises the whole.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding a sick person's acknowledgment for an heir. The Hanafi position is that it is invalid unless the other heirs confirm it, based on the hadith 'No will for an heir and no acknowledgment of debt for him.' The Hanafi reasoning is that during death illness, the right of all heirs attaches to the estate, so an acknowledgment favoring one heir would harm others. This is similar to the prohibition of bequest for an heir. In contrast, Shafi'i in one of his opinions considers it valid because the acknowledgment is simply revealing an existing right, and truthfulness is favored. The Hanafi response is that the attachment of heirs' rights prevents such acknowledgment, and the need for transactions with strangers allows acknowledgment for them, but not for heirs. If other heirs confirm, they waive their right, making it valid. The passage also addresses that acknowledgment for a stranger is valid even if it consumes the entire estate, with the principle that it operates one-third at a time due to legal restrictions, but eventually can cover the whole.

Key Terms
إقرار للوارث (iqrar li-warith): A sick person's acknowledgment of a debt or right in favor of one of his heirs.
تصديق (tasdiq): Confirmation by the other heirs that the acknowledgment is true, which validates the acknowledgment.
تعلق حق الورثة (ta'allaq haqq al-warathah): The attachment of the heirs' right to the estate during the death illness, which restricts the sick person's transactions that harm the heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid automatically.
B) Invalid unless other siblings confirm.
C) Valid only if it does not exceed one-third.
D) Invalid only if the heir is the sole heir.

Key Takeaway
A sick person's acknowledgment for an heir is void unless the other heirs confirm it; this protects the equitable distribution of the estate.

6 min
Ruling on a Sick Person's Acknowledgment in Favor of an Heir
Exposes Hanafi proof for prohibition of iqrār to heir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi prohibition of a terminally ill person's acknowledgment in favor of an heir, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith and rational proofs.

Core Idea
No acknowledgment to an heir without confirmation by other heirs — the rights of all heirs attach during illness.

One of the most debated issues in deathbed law is whether a terminally ill person can acknowledge a debt owed to his own heir. The Hanafi school holds that such an acknowledgment is automatically invalid unless the other heirs consent. This lesson examines the Hanafi proof from the hadith 'No bequest to an heir and no acknowledgment of debt for him' and the rational argument based on the attachment of heirs' rights. We will also critically assess the Shafi'i opinion that treats the acknowledgment as valid by analogy to a stranger's case.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school rules that a terminally ill person's acknowledgment in favor of an heir is not valid unless the other heirs confirm it.
This is the default ruling (batil) without taṣdīq.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi‘i (in one qawl), Abu Thawr, ‘Ata’, and others consider it valid, comparing it to an acknowledgment to a stranger.
They argue it is merely an expression of a pre-existing right.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent argues that iqrār is testimonial, not a disposition, and circumstantial evidence supports truthfulness; thus it should be valid like iqrār to a stranger.
Analogy (qiyas) to stranger's iqrār is their primary proof.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response counters with the explicit hadith and the rational argument that the rights of other heirs are attached during illness, preventing any preferential treatment. The analogy to a stranger fails because dealings with strangers are necessary, while dealings with heirs are rare.
The illa (cause) for allowing stranger's iqrār is necessity (haja), which does not apply to heirs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi law, the iqrār is ineffective without other heirs' consent; under the Shafi‘i view it is effective.
This affects estate distribution in actual cases.

Source Text

وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا وَصِيَّةَ لِوَارِثٍ وَلَا اِقْرَارَ لَهُ بِالدَّيْنِ وَلَانَّهُ تَعَلَّقَ حَقُّ الْوَرَثَةِ بِمَالِهِ فِي مَرَضِهِ وَلِهَذَا يَمْنَعُ مِنَ التَّبَرُع عَلَى الْوَارِثِ أَصْلًا فَفِي تَخْصِيصِ الْبَعْضِ بِهِ إِبْطَالُ حَقِ الْبَاقِيْنَ وَلَاتَ حَالَةَ الْمَرَضِ حَالَةَ الْإِسْتِغْنَاءِ وَالْقَرَابَةُ سَبَبَ التَّعَلَّقَ إِلَّا أَنَّ هَذَا التَّعَلُّقِ لَمْ يَظْهَر فِى حَقِّ الْأَجْنَبِي لِحَاجَتِهِ إِلَى الْمُعَامَلَةِ فِي الصَّحَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ الْحَجَرَ عَنِ الْإِقْرَارِ بِالْمَرَضِ يَمْتَنِعُ النَّاسُ عَنِ الْمُعَامَلَةِ مَعَهُ وَقَلَّمَا يَقَعُ الْمُعَامَلَةُ مَعَ الْوَارِثِ وَلَمْ يَظْهَرُ فِي حَقِ الْإِقْرَارِ لِوَارِثِ أَخَرَ لِحَاجَتِهِ أَيْضًا ثُمَّ هَذَا التَّعَلُّقُ حَقُّ بَقِيَةِ الْوَرَثَةِ فَإِذَا صَدَّقُوْهُ فَقَدْ ابْطَلُوْهُ فَيَصِحُ إِقْرَارُهُ
ترجمہ اگر اقرار کیا مریض نے اپنے وارث کے لئے تو صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ مگر یہ کہ اس میں باقی ورثہ اس کی تصدیق کریں۔ امام شافعی نے اپنے ایک قول میں کہا کہ صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ایک حق ثابت کا اظہار ہے۔ جانب صدق رائج ہونے کی وجہ سے اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اجنبی کے لئے اقرار کرنا یا وارث آخر کا یا وارث کی تلف کردہ ودیعت کا اقرار کرنا۔ ہماری دلیل حضور علیہ السلام کا ارشاد ہے کہ نہ وارث کے لئے وصیت ہے اور نہ اس کے لئے قرض کا اقرار اور اس لئے کہ اس کے مرض میں ورثہ کا حق اس کے مال سے متعلق ہو گیا۔ اسی لئے اس کو وارث پر تبرع کرنے سے بالکل روک دیا گیا۔ پس اقرار میں بعض کی تخصیص سے باقی ورثہ کا حق باطل کرنا ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ حالتِ مرض حالت اسفناء ہے اور قرابت تعلق کا سبب ہے مگر یہ تعلق اجنبی کے حق میں ظاہر نہیں ہوا ۔ صحت کی حالت میں اس کو معاملہ کی ضرورت ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ کیونکہ اگر مرض کی وجہ سے وہ اقرار مجور ہو جائے تو لوگ اس کے ساتھ معاملہ کرنے سے بازرہیں گے۔ اور وارث کے ساتھ معاملہ بہت کم ہوتا ہے۔ اور دوسرے کے وارث ہونے کے اقرار کے حق میں بھی ظاہر نہیں ہوا ۔ کیونکہ اس کو اس کی بھی ضرورت ہے۔ پھر یہ تعلق باقی ورثہ کا حق ہے۔ جب انہوں نے اس کی تصدیق کر دی تو اپنا حق خود ہی باطل کر دیا۔ لہذا مریض کا اقرار صحیح ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح قوله و لو اقر المریض اگر مریض اپنے وارث کے لئے کسی عین یادین کا اقرار کرے تو اقرار صحیح نہیں۔ الا یہ کہ باقی ورثہ اس کی تصدیق کریں۔ امام احمد ابراہیم مخفی سفیان ثوری شمعی حکم قاضی شریح بھی انصاری، قاسم ابن سلام، ابو ہاشم، سالم، این از بینہ اورایک قول میں امام شافعی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ لیکن ان کا اصح قول یہ ہے کہ اقرار صحیح ہے۔ ابو ثور ، عطاء، حسن بصری، اور اسحاق بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ جہاں تہمت کا اندیشہ نہ ہو وہاں صحیح ہے ورنہ باطل ہے۔ جیسے کسی کی ایک لڑکی اور ایک چاز اولر کا ہے ۔ مریض نے اپنی لڑکی کے لئے اقرار کیا تو صیح نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ تہمت کا امکان ہے اور اگر چچاز ادلر کے کے لئے اقرار کیا تو صحیح ہوگا۔ شوافع میں رویانی نے اسی کو اختیار کیا ہے حسن بن صالح سے مروی ہے کہ صرف اپنی بیوی کے مہر کا اقرار حیح ہے باقی باطل ہے۔
قوله لانه اظهار حق ... امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مریں کا اقرار کرنا ایک حق ثابت کا اظہار ہے کیونکہ اس م میں بدلالت حال ہے پس جیسے اجنبی کے لئے اقرار صحیح ہے ایے ہی وارث کے لئے بھی صحیح ہوگا۔ نیز یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے وہ کسی شخص کی نسبت وارث ہونے کا یا کسی وارث کی

كتاب الاقرا
قوله ولنا قوله عليه السلام .... ماری دلیل سنن دار قطنی کی روایت ہے قال رسول الله الاوصية لوارث ولا اقرار له بدين سوال ..... یه روایت مرسل ہے۔ جواب اول تو حافظ ابو نعیم نے تاریخ اصبہان میں اشعث بن شداد، خراسانی کے تحت اس کو مسند کیا ہے۔
وسنده هكذا "حدثنا ابو محمد بن حبان ثنا ابو عبدالرحمن المقدمى ثنا اشعث بن شداد الخراساني ثنا يحى ثنا نوح بن دراج عن ابان تغلب عن جعفر بن محمد عن ابيه عن جابر نے اہ“۔ اور اگر مرسل ہی تسلیم کر لیں جیسا کہ اکثر کی رائے یہی ہے تب بھی مرسل ہمارے یہاں حجت ہے۔ ۔ سوال ... نوح بن دراج کی ابن معین نے تکذیب کی اسے امام ابوداود فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ چھوٹا ہے۔ حدیث گھڑتا تھا۔ ابن حبان اور حاکم کا بیان ہے کہ یہ ثقات سے بھی موضوعات روایت کرتا ہے۔ پھر مرسل مذکور صحیح کہاں ہوئی؟
جواب جعفر فریابی نے محمد بن عبداللہ بن نمیر سے اس کی توثیق نقل کی ہے شیخ ابوزرعہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ کوفہ کا قاضی تھا اور مجھے امید ہے کہ اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ۔ ابن عدی کا قول ہے کہ مکثر فی الحدیث تو نہیں ہے مگر اس کی حدیث لکھی جاسکتی ہے۔ معلوم ہوا کہ نوح بن دراج مختلف فیہ ہے۔ والاختلاف غیر مضر عندنا “۔(اعلاء السنن)
قوله ولا نه تعلق ہماری عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مریض کے مال سے جمیع ورثہ کا حق وابستہ ہو گیا ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے اس کو ورثہ کے حق میں ہبہ یا وصیت وغیرہ کے احسان کرے کی بالکل ممانعت ہے اور کسی ایک کے لئے اقرار کرنے میں باقی ورثہ کا حق باطل کرنا ہے۔ لہذا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ دوسری عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرض کی حالت مال سے بے نیازی کی حالت ہے۔ کیونکہ امارات موت ظاہر ہو جانے سے ساری امیدیں ختم ہو جاتی ہیں اور اس کے مال کے ساتھ تعلق وابستہ ہونے کا سبب قرابت ہے مگر یہ تعلق اجنبی کے حق میں ظاہر نہیں ہوا ، ( بلکہ اس کے لئے اقرار بیح ہے ) اس لئے کہ صحت کی حالت میں اس کو معاملات کی احتیاج ہے اور ورثہ کے ساتھ معاملات کا وقوع بہت کم ہوتا ہے۔ زیادہ تر جانب ہی کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے اگر اجنبی کے لئے اس کا اقرار صحیح نہ مانا جائے تو لوگ اس سے معاملات نہ کریں گے اور اس کی ضروریات کا دروازہ بند ہو کر رہ جائے گا۔ نیز تعلق مذکور دوسرے شخص کی نسبت وارث ہونے کے اقرار کے حق میں بھی ظاہر نہیں ہوا ۔ کیونکہ انسان کو اس کی بھی ضرورت ہے تا کہ اس کی نسل کے سب وارث باقی رہیں۔ پس نسب کا اقرار یا اس کی ضروریات یا اصلیہ میں سے ہوا۔ پھر تعلق مذکور باقی اور ثہ کا حق ہے ۔ اور جب انہوں نے اس کی تصدیق کر دی تو اقرار معتبر ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ اقرار کا معتبر ہونا تو انہیں کے حق کی وجہ سے تھا۔
And we have his statement (peace be upon him): 'No bequest to an heir and no acknowledgment of debt for him.' And because the right of the heirs becomes attached to his property during his illness, for this reason he is prevented from any gratuitous transfer (tabarru‘) in favor of an heir entirely. So in specifying some of them with it (the acknowledgment) lies the invalidation of the right of the others. And because the state of illness is a state of need, and kinship is a cause of attachment, except that this attachment does not appear in the case of a stranger due to his need for transactions in health, because if he were prevented from acknowledging during illness, people would refrain from transacting with him, and transactions with an heir seldom occur. And it does not appear in the case of acknowledgment for another heir due to his need as well. Then this attachment is a right of the remaining heirs, so if they confirm him, they have invalidated it, and his acknowledgment becomes valid.
Translation: If a sick person acknowledges in favor of his heir, it is not valid unless the other heirs confirm it. Imam al-Shafi‘i said in one of his opinions that it is valid because it is an expression of a proven right, due to the preponderance of truthfulness, and it becomes like an acknowledgment for a stranger or another heir or for a lost deposit. Our proof is the Prophet's statement: 'No bequest to an heir and no acknowledgment of debt for him.' And because the heirs' right becomes attached to his property in his illness, for this reason he is prevented from any gift to an heir. So specifying some by acknowledgment invalidates the right of the others. And because illness is a state of need, and kinship is a cause of attachment, but this attachment does not appear for a stranger due to his need for transactions in health, because if he were prevented from acknowledging due to illness, people would stop dealing with him. Transactions with heirs are rare. It also does not appear in the case of acknowledgment for another heir due to his need as well. Then this attachment is the right of the remaining heirs; when they confirm him, they have invalidated their own right, so his acknowledgment becomes valid.
Detail: ... (paraphrasing the commentary).
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of a terminally ill person's acknowledgment (iqrār) in favor of his own heir. The Hanafi position is that such an acknowledgment is invalid unless the other heirs confirm it. The author first presents the Hanafi proof from hadith and rational argument, then the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi‘i (in one of his opinions) and others. The Hanafi response refutes the Shafi‘i analogy to iqrār to a stranger. The text then discusses the hadith chain, addressing criticisms about its reliability, and provides rational proofs based on the attachment of heirs' rights. The ruling: without confirmation, the iqrār is void; with confirmation, it becomes valid.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment of a debt or right against oneself; a unilateral declaration.
وارث (wārith): An heir who is entitled to a share of the estate.
تصدیق (taṣdīq): Confirmation or ratification by the other heirs, making the acknowledgment valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a terminally ill person's acknowledgment of a debt in favor of his own heir if the other heirs do not confirm it?
A) It is valid and binding.
B) It is invalid and void.
C) It is valid only up to one-third of the estate.
D) It is suspended until recovery from illness.

Key Takeaway
A terminally ill person's acknowledgment in favor of an heir is invalid in the Hanafi school unless the remaining heirs confirm it, based on the hadith and the principle that the rights of all heirs are attached to the estate.
