Sick Person's Iqrār to a Stranger: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Explains validity of iqrār to stranger by istihsan and two furū'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a sick person's iqrār to a stranger is valid for the entire estate by istihsan, and distinguish the rulings when lineage or marriage is later claimed.

Core Idea
A sick person's acknowledgment to a stranger is valid for all property by istihsan, overriding qiyas limitation to one-third.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi ruling on a sick person's iqrār (acknowledgment of debt) to a stranger (non-heir). While qiyas suggests it should be limited to one-third like a bequest, the Hanafi school adopts istihsan (juristic preference) to allow full validity because debt repayment is a primary need. The passage also discusses two sub-issues: what happens if the sick person later claims the stranger is his son, or marries the woman he acknowledged for.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that the passage addresses the validity of a sick person's iqrār to a stranger and its scope – whether it is limited to one-third of the estate or can cover the entire property.
The key distinction is between iqrār (debt acknowledgment) and bequest (wasiyya).
2
Understand the qiyas argument
Qiyas would analogize iqrār to a bequest, limiting it to one-third based on the hadith: 'Your bequest is one-third, and one-third is plenty.' This protects heirs' rights.
This is the default analogy (qiyas jaliy).
3
Analyze the istihsan override
Istiḥsān (juristic preference) overrides qiyas because debt repayment is a primary need (ḥājah aṣliyya). The Law does not intend to restrict debt payment to one-third; thus the iqrār is valid for the entire estate.
The illa (cause) for istihsan is the necessity of enabling transactions with the sick.
4
Apply to the first furū': subsequent lineage claim
If the sick person later claims the stranger is his son, lineage (nasab) relates back to conception. The person becomes an heir from the beginning, so the iqrār to an heir is invalid.
This is based on the principle that lineage is retroactive.
5
Apply to the second furū': subsequent marriage
If the sick person later marries the woman he acknowledged for, the marriage does not retroactively change her status. She was a stranger at the time of iqrār, so the acknowledgment remains valid.
Marriage is a future contract, not retroactive like lineage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وان اقر لا جنبی اگر مریض نے کسی اجنبی کے لئے اقرار کیا تو اقرار جائز ہے۔ اگر چہ اس کے تمام مال کو محیط ہو جائے ۔ کیونکہ قرض کی ادائیگی حوائج اصلیہ میں سے ہے۔ گو قیاس یہی چاہتا ہے کہ تہائی کے علاوہ میں جائز نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ شرع نے اس کا تصرف صرف تہائی تک محدود رکھا ہے۔ لیکن ہم استحسانا کہتے ہیں کہ جب اس کا اقرار تہائی میں صحیح ہوا تو باقی نہائی میں اس کا تصرف جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قرضہ کے بعد بھی تہائی ہے اس کے بعد پھر باقی تہائی میں بھی جائز ہوگا۔ وہذا یہاں تک کہ اقرار کل مال پر حاوی ہوگا۔ اجنبی کے لئے اقرار کیا پھر کہا وہ میرا بیٹا ہے۔ نسب ثابت ہوگا اور اقرار باطل ہوگا، اجنبیہ کے لئے اقرار کیا پھر اس سے نکاح کیا اقرار باطل نہ ہو گا وجہ فرق
قَالَ وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ لِاجْنَبِي ثُمَّ قَالَ هُوَ ابْنِى ثَبَتَ نَسَبُهِ مِنْهُ وَبَطَلَ إِقْرَارُهُ لَهُ فَإِنْ أَقَرَّ لِا جُنَبِيَّةِ ثُمَّ تَزَوَّجَهَا لَمْ يَبْطُلْ اقْرَارُهُ لَهَا وَجْهُ الْفَرْقِ اَنَّ دَعْوَةَ النَّسَبِ تَسْتَنِدُ إِلى وَقْتِ الْعُلُوقِ فَتَبَيَّنَ أَنَّهُ أَقَرَّ لِابْنِهِ فَلَا يَصِحُ وَلَا كَذَالِكَ
His statement: 'And if he acknowledges for a stranger' — If a sick person acknowledges for a stranger, the acknowledgment is permissible, even if it covers all his property, because repayment of debt is among primary needs. Although analogy (qiyas) requires that it should not be valid except within one-third, because the Law has restricted his disposition to one-third. But we say by istihsan: when his acknowledgment is valid in one-third, then disposition in the remaining one-third is permissible, because after the debt there is still one-third, then after that the remaining one-third, and so on until it covers all. If he acknowledged for a stranger then said 'he is my son', his lineage is established and the acknowledgment becomes void. If he acknowledged for a stranger woman then married her, his acknowledgment does not become void. The reason for the difference is that the claim of lineage refers back to the time of conception, so it becomes clear that he acknowledged for his son, thus it is not valid; not so in the case of marriage.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on a sick person's iqrār to a stranger. The ruling is that it is valid even if it consumes the entire estate, based on istihsan (juristic preference), overriding the qiyas that would limit it to one-third. The author explains that paying off debts is a primary need, so necessity overrides the general restriction on a sick person's dispositions. Then two furū‘ (sub-issues) are discussed: (1) if the sick person acknowledges for a stranger and then claims the stranger is his son, the lineage is established and the iqrār becomes invalid because it is then an iqrār to an heir. (2) If he acknowledges for a strange woman and then marries her, the iqrār remains valid because marriage does not retroactively change the nature of the acknowledgment. The distinction is based on the principle that lineage relates back to conception, making the person an heir from the beginning.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in favor of a ruling that better serves public interest or necessity.
أجنبي (ajanabī): A person who is not an heir of the sick person.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity; establishing that the acknowledged person is the son of the declarant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sick person acknowledges a debt to a strange man and later claims he is his son, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The acknowledgment remains valid because it was made before the claim.
B) The acknowledgment becomes void because the person now qualifies as an heir.
C) The acknowledgment is valid up to one-third only.
D) The claim of lineage is invalid because it contradicts the earlier acknowledgment.

Key Takeaway
By istihsan, a sick person's iqrār to a stranger is fully valid to meet debt needs; subsequent lineage claim voids it retroactively, but marriage does not.

Conditions for Valid Acknowledgment of Paternity
Ruling on acknowledging a child with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for a valid acknowledgment of paternity (iqrār bi al-nasab) and explain why illness does not invalidate it.

Core Idea
Acknowledgment of paternity is valid only if biologically possible, the child has no known father, and the child confirms.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a man acknowledges a child as his son. The Hanafi school lays down clear conditions to prevent fraud and protect lineage rights. Even if the man is terminally ill, the acknowledgment stands because establishing lineage is a fundamental need. Let's parse the conditions and their rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is iqrār bi al-nasab (acknowledgment of paternity). The ruling is that it is valid (sahīh) and lineage is established (thabata nasabuhu), even if the acknowledger is sick.
The text begins with 'Wa man aqarra...' – this is a conditional ruling.
2
List the three conditions mentioned
The author states three conditions: (1) the child could be born from such a man (yuuladu mithluhu li-mithlihi), (2) the child has no known lineage (laysa lahu nasabun ma‘rūf), (3) the child confirms the acknowledgment (saddaqahu al-ghulām).
These are shurūt for validity.
3
Understand why each condition is required
Condition 1 prevents manifest falsehood (takdhīb ẓāhir). Condition 2 ensures no conflict with an existing father. Condition 3 is needed because the child is a free agent (fī yad nafsihi) who can speak for himself, unlike an infant.
The text gives ta‘līl (reasoning) for each.
4
Analyze the exception for illness
Illness of the acknowledger does not prevent validity because lineage is a primary necessity (ḥawā’ij aṣliyya). This overrides the general rule that an ill person's Iqrār regarding property may be restricted to one-third of the estate.
The text explicitly states 'lā yamtani‘u bi al-maraḍ'.
5
Consider the consequence: inheritance
Once lineage is established, the child becomes a legal heir and participates in inheritance with other heirs, just like any known heir.
The text ends with 'yushāriku al-wuratha'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَضْلٌ وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِغُلَامٍ يُولَدُ مِثْلُهُ لِمِثْلِهِ وَلَيْسَ لَهُ نَسَبٌ مَعْرُوفٌ أَنَّهُ ابْنُهُ وَصَدَّقَهُ الْغُلَامُ ثَبَتَ نَسَبُهُ مِنْهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَرِيضًا لِأَنَّ النَّسَبَ مِمَّا يَلْزَمُهُ خَاصَّةً فَيَصِحُ إِقْرَارُهُ بِهِ وَشَرَطَ أَنْ يُولَدَ مِثْلُهُ لِمِثْلِهِ كَيْلَا يَكُونَ مُكَذَّبًا فِي الظَّاهِرِ وَشَرَطَ أَنْ لَّا يَكُونَ لَهُ نَسَبٌ مَعْرُوفٌ وَلِأَنَّهُ يَمْنَعُ ثُبُوتَهُ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ وَإِنَّمَا شَرَطَ تَصْدِيقَهُ لِأَنَّهُ فِي يَدِ نَفْسِهِ إِذِ الْمَسْأَلَةُ وُضِعَتْ فِي غُلَامٍ يُعَبِّرُ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ بِخِلَافِ الصَّغِيرِ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ مِنْ قَبْلُ وَلَا يَمْتَنِعُ بِالْمَرَضِ لِأَنَّ النَّسَبَ مِنَ الْحَوَائِجِ الْأَصْلِيَّةِ وَيُشَارِكُ الْوَرَثَةَ فِي الْمِيرَاثِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا ثَبَتَ نَسَبُهُ مِنْهُ صَارَ كَالْوَارِثِ الْمَعْرُوفِ فَيُشَارِكُ وَرَثَتَهُ
A chapter: Whoever acknowledges a boy who is of an age that such a boy could be born to such a man, and the boy has no known lineage, that he is his son, and the boy confirms him, his lineage from him is established even if he is sick, because lineage is something that obligates him specifically, so his acknowledgment of it is valid. And he conditioned that a like of him be born to a like of him, so that he not be a liar in appearance. And he conditioned that he should not have a known lineage, because that prevents its establishment from someone else. And he only conditioned his confirmation because he is in his own hand, since the case is placed concerning a boy who can speak for himself, contrary to a young child, as has passed before. And illness does not prevent it because lineage is among the primary needs. And he will participate with the heirs in the inheritance because when his lineage from him is established, he becomes like a known heir, so he will participate with his heirs.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the acknowledgment of paternity (iqrār bi al-nasab). It states that a man may acknowledge a child as his son even if he is terminally ill, provided three conditions are met: (1) The child must be of an age that it is biologically possible for him to have fathered such a child, so that the acknowledgment is not manifestly false. (2) The child must have no known lineage (majhūl al-nasab), because if the child already has a father, his lineage cannot be claimed by another. (3) The child must confirm the acknowledgment, because the child is a free agent (fī yad nafsihi) and can speak for himself, unlike an infant who cannot. The reason the acknowledgment is valid despite the man’s illness is that lineage is a dire necessity (ḥawā’ij aṣliyya). Once the lineage is established, the child becomes a legal heir and shares in the inheritance with other heirs.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment or confession by a person that imposes a legal consequence on themselves.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity; the legal relationship between a father and child, carrying rights of inheritance and support.
مقر (muqir): The person who makes the acknowledgment.
تصديق (tasdiq): Confirmation by the acknowledged person (the child) that the acknowledgment is true.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for a valid acknowledgment of paternity?
A) The child must be a minor.
B) The child must have a known lineage.
C) The child must confirm the acknowledgment.
D) The acknowledger must be healthy.

Key Takeaway
A valid acknowledgment of paternity in Hanafi law requires biological possibility, no existing lineage, and the child's confirmation; illness of the acknowledger does not invalidate it, and the child becomes a full heir.

Acknowledgment of Lineage: Conditions and the Post-Death Confirmation Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on post-death confirmation of lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the validity of a husband's confirmation of a child after the wife's death, and apply the conditions under which a woman's acknowledgment of a child is accepted.

Core Idea
A woman's child acknowledgment requires husband's confirmation or midwife's testimony; after her death, the majority view accepts his confirmation due to inheritance.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the rules of acknowledging lineage relationships. It first lays out general principles for men and women, then delves into a critical exception: a woman cannot independently claim a child without the father's confirmation. The text then reveals an important difference within the Hanafi school—whether the husband's confirmation remains valid after his wife's death.

Guided Path
1
Identify general rules for man and woman
Note that a man's acknowledgment of parents, child, wife, and mawlā is valid. A woman's acknowledgment of parents, husband, and mawlā is valid, but not of a child—because that imposes paternity on the husband.
This distinction rests on the principle that acknowledging lineage does not burden others.
2
Find the exception for woman's child
A woman's acknowledgment of a child becomes accepted only if the husband confirms (tasdiq) or a midwife testifies to the birth. The husband's right is protected, and the midwife's testimony is reliable for birth.
Tasdiq is the confirmation by the acknowledged person (here the husband) that the claim is true.
3
Analyze tasdiq after death
Tasdiq in lineage is valid after the death of the original acknowledger because lineage continues after death. Similarly, a wife's confirmation after her husband's death is valid—marriage's rulings persist.
But what about the husband's confirmation after the wife's death?
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the husband's confirmation after the wife's death is invalid because marriage ends at death. Inheritance does not yet exist at the time of acknowledgment. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue it is valid because inheritance is a remaining effect of the marriage contract.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school, rooted in the nature of marriage's post-death effects.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: the husband's confirmation after death is valid, establishing the child's lineage. This view is preferred to avoid leaving the child without lineage.
Practical consequence (thamarah): under Abu Hanifa's view, the child would not inherit; under the Sahibayn, the child inherits as a legitimate heir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَجُوزُ إِقْرَارُ الرَّجُلِ بِالْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالْوَلَدِ وَالزَّوْجَةِ وَالْمَوْلَى لِأَنَّهُ أَقَرَّ بِمَا يَلْزَمُهُ وَلَيْسَ فِيهِ تَحْمِيلُ النَّسَبِ عَلَى الْغَيْرِ وَيُقْبَلُ إِقْرَارُ الْمَرْأَةِ بِالْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالزَّوْجِ وَالْمَوْلَى لِمَا بَيَّنَّا وَلَا يُقْبَلُ بِالْوَلَدِ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ تَحْمِيلَ النَّسَبِ عَلَى الْغَيْرِ وَهُوَ الزَّوْجُ لِأَنَّ النَّسَبَ مِنْهُ إِلَّا أَنْ يُصَدِّقَهَا الزَّوْجُ لِأَنَّ الْحَقَّ لَهُ أَوْ تَشْهَدَ بِوِلَادَتِهِ قَابِلَةٌ لِأَنَّ قَوْلَ الْقَابِلَةِ فِي هَذَا مَقْبُولٌ وَقَدْ مَرَّ فِي الطَّلَاقِ وَقَدْ ذَكَرْنَا فِي إِقْرَارِ الْمَرْأَةِ تَفْصِيلًا فِي كِتَابِ الدَّعْوَى وَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ تَصْدِيقِ هَؤُلَاءِ وَيَصِحُ التَّصْدِيقُ فِي النَّسَبِ بَعْدَ مَوْتِ الْمُقِرِّ لِأَنَّ النَّسَبَ يَبْقَى بَعْدَ الْمَوْتِ وَكَذَا يَصِحُ تَصْدِيقُ الزَّوْجَةِ لِأَنَّ حُكْمَ النِّكَاحِ بَاقٍ وَكَذَا يَصِحُ تَصْدِيقُ الزَّوْجِ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا لِأَنَّ الْإِرْثَ مِنْ أَحْكَامِهِ وَعِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لَا يَصِحُ لِأَنَّ النِّكَاحَ انْقَطَعَ بِالْمَوْتِ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَحِلُّ لَهُ غَسْلُهَا عِنْدَنَا وَلَا يَصِحُ التَّصْدِيقُ عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ الْإِرْثِ لِأَنَّهُ مَعْدُومٌ حَالَةَ الْإِقْرَارِ وَإِنَّمَا يَثْبُتُ بَعْدَ الْمَوْتِ وَالتَّصْدِيقُ يُسْتَنَدُ إِلَى أَوَّلِ الْإِقْرَارِ
He said: A man's acknowledgment of parents, child, wife, and master is valid because he acknowledged what is binding on him, and there is no imposing of lineage on another. And a woman's acknowledgment of parents, husband, and master is accepted for what we have explained. But her acknowledgment of a child is not accepted because it involves imposing lineage on another, namely the husband, since the lineage is from him, unless the husband confirms her because the right is his, or a midwife testifies to his birth because the midwife's word in this is accepted, and it has passed in the chapter on divorce. And we have mentioned details of a woman's acknowledgment in the Book of Claims (Kitab al-Da'wa). And the confirmation of these individuals is necessary. And confirmation in lineage is valid after the death of the acknowledger because lineage remains after death. Likewise, the wife's confirmation is valid because the ruling of marriage remains. Likewise, the husband's confirmation is valid after her death because inheritance is among its rulings. But according to Abu Hanifa, it is not valid because marriage is severed by death, and for this reason, it is not permissible for him to wash her according to us. And confirmation is not valid on the basis of inheritance because it is non-existent at the time of acknowledgment; it only becomes established after death, and confirmation is traced back to the beginning of the acknowledgment.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage expands on who can be acknowledged and by whom. A man may acknowledge his parents, child, wife, and former master (mawlā al-‘itāqah) because it imposes only a duty on himself, not on others. A woman may acknowledge her parents, husband, and master, but not a child, because claiming a child imposes paternity on the husband. However, if the husband confirms or a midwife testifies to the birth, it is accepted. Confirmation (tasdiq) is required from all these persons. The passage also discusses tasdiq after death: confirmation of lineage remains valid after the acknowledger's death. For the wife's confirmation after the husband's death or vice versa, there is a difference: according to the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is valid because the effect of marriage continues for inheritance. But according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the husband's confirmation after the wife's death is invalid because the marriage tie is severed at death, and therefore he cannot even wash her body. The reason given is that inheritance is not yet established at the time of acknowledgment; it only arises after death, and confirmation should be based on the situation at the time of acknowledgment.

Key Terms
مولى (mawlā): A freed slave (mawlā al-‘itāqah) who has a master-client relationship.
تصديق (tasdiq): Confirmation by the person being acknowledged (e.g., child, husband) that the acknowledgment is true.
قابلة (qābilah): Midwife; her testimony about birth is accepted in matters of lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a woman's acknowledgment of a child not accepted without her husband's confirmation or a midwife's testimony?
A) Because a child cannot be claimed by a woman.
B) Because it imposes lineage on the husband without his consent.
C) Because the midwife must always be present.
D) Because it is not binding.

Key Takeaway
A woman's acknowledgment of a child is accepted only with the husband's confirmation or a midwife's testimony; after death, the majority view accepts the husband's confirmation due to inheritance being a remaining effect of marriage.

Woman's Acknowledgment of Close Relatives
Ruling on the validity of a woman's acknowledgment of close relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman's acknowledgment of her mother, father, husband, and master, and explain the legal proof and the intra-school dispute.

Core Idea
A woman's acknowledgment of close relatives is valid because it binds only herself, not others.

This passage from the Kitab al-Iqrar discusses a specific case: a woman acknowledging someone as her mother, father, husband, or former master. The general rule of iqrar is that it binds only the one who makes it. However, an intra-Hanafi dispute exists regarding the mother, with some earlier scholars considering it invalid due to lineage issues. The preferred position, supported by Durr al-Mukhtar, affirms its validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a woman's acknowledgment (iqrar) of another person as her mother, father, husband, or master. According to the preferred Hanafi view, this acknowledgment is valid (sahih).
The acknowledgment is an admission that creates legal consequences only for the acknowledger.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the general rule of iqrar: a person's acknowledgment is proof against themselves, not against others. The author also cites equality between mother and father in being origins (usul).
The dalil is not a specific text but a principle derived from the Sunnah and legal reasoning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The woman's acknowledgment binds her alone. For example, acknowledging a mother establishes inheritance rights for the mother from the woman, but does not force the woman's father to accept marriage to that mother. Hence, no imposition on a third party occurs.
The key is that the acknowledgment does not establish nasab (lineage) against the father, only rights and obligations for the woman.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some earlier Hanafi sources (Mabsut, Jami' al-Saghir) held that acknowledging a mother is invalid because lineage traces through fathers, and such acknowledgment implies a marriage that is not proven.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; both sides are based on the same general principle but differ on its application.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The author prefers the majority view that all such acknowledgments are valid, citing Durr al-Mukhtar which argues that mother and father are equal as origins. This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
The preference is based on the weight of later authorities and consistency with the general rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاقرار.
نسب کو کسی غیر کی طرف منسوب کرنا بھی نہیں ہے۔ ان مسائل میں قاعدہ کلیہ یہی ہے کہ آدمی کا اقرار خود اپنی ذات پر حجت ہے نہ کہ غیر پر۔ نبیہ مال ہونے کے اقرار کا صحیح ہونا جیسا کہ او پر مذکور ہوا۔ یہی مشہور ہے۔ اکثر علماء اسی پر ہیں۔ اور یہی تحفہ الفقہاء، سراج الدین کی شرح فرائض اور صاحب ہدایہ کی روایت کے موافق ہے۔ لیکن فرائض عقابی بضوء السراج اور مبسوط و ایضاح اورشیخ محبوبی کی جامع صغیر کے عام نسخوں میں اس کے خلاف یہ ہے کہ ماں ہونے کا اقرار صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ نسب آباء سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ امہات سے نیز اس میں غیر شخص یعنی مقر کے باپ پر زوجیت لاگو کرنا ہے لہذا اقرار صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ مگر صاحب در مختار کہتے ہیں کہ اقرار مذکور کی صحت حق ہے۔ کیونکہ اصل ہونے میں ماں اور باپ دونوں برابر ہیں۔ تو ماں باپ کے مانند ہوئی۔ قوله و يقبل اقرار المراء .... اگر کوئی عورت یہ اقرار کرے کہ فلاں عورت میری ماں ہے۔ یا فلاں شخص میرا باپ یا شوہر یا مولاء عتاقہ ہے تو اس کا یہ اقرار ی ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے جو اوپر مذکور ہوئی لانه اقـرعا يلزمه و ليس فيه تحميل النَّسَبَ علی الغیر ، رہا اس کا عورت ہونا سو یہ اس کی ذات پر اس کے اقرار کی صحت سے مانع نہیں ہے۔
The Book of Acknowledgment. Nor is it attributing lineage to someone else. In these issues, the general rule is that a person's acknowledgment is a proof against his own self, not against others. The correctness of acknowledging being a son in wealth is as mentioned above. This is well-known. Most scholars are upon this. And this is in agreement with Tuhfat al-Fuqaha, Saraj al-Din's Sharh al-Fara'id, and the narration of Sahib al-Hidayah. But in the Fara'id 'Uqabi bi Daw' al-Siraj, and the common copies of al-Mabsut, al-Idah, and Shaykh Mahbubi's Jami' al-Saghir, contrary to this is that acknowledgment of being a mother is not correct because lineage is from fathers, not from mothers. Also it involves applying marriage to another person, i.e., the father of the acknowledger, so the acknowledgment would not be correct. However, Sahib al-Durr al-Mukhtar says that the correctness of the mentioned acknowledgment is correct because in being an origin, mother and father are equal, so the mother is like the father. His saying: And the acknowledgment of a woman is accepted. If a woman acknowledges that such a woman is my mother, or such a person is my father, or my husband, or my master (by emancipation), then her acknowledgment is valid. This is the reason mentioned above: because it is an acknowledgment of something that binds her, and there is no imposition of lineage upon others. As for her being a woman, that does not prevent the validity of her acknowledgment against herself.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage begins with the general rule of iqrar (acknowledgment): a person's acknowledgment is binding only upon themselves, not upon others. The author then discusses a specific case: a woman acknowledging someone as her mother, father, husband, or former master. The majority view (including the author's own reliance) is that such acknowledgment is valid because it only establishes rights and obligations upon herself (e.g., inheritance, marital rights) and does not impose lineage on a third party unfairly. However, there is a minority opinion that acknowledging a mother is invalid because lineage (nasab) is traced through fathers, and such acknowledgment would imply marriage between the mother and the woman's father, which is an imposition on the father. The author sides with the stronger view, citing Durr al-Mukhtar, that mother and father are equal in being origins, so the same ruling applies. The key principle here is that as long as the acknowledgment does not involve foisting lineage upon an unwilling third party, it is valid.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): A legal acknowledgment by a person of a right or obligation against themselves.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or parentage, i.e., the relationship of a person to their ancestors.
ولاء (wala'): The bond of patronage between a former master and a freed slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view in this passage, why is a woman's acknowledgment of her mother considered valid?
A) Because the mother is a blood relative and no imposition on others occurs.
B) Because the woman is legally capable of establishing lineage independently.
C) Because mother and father are equal in being an origin, and the acknowledgment does not force lineage on a third party unwillingly.
D) Because the husband's permission is obtained.

Key Takeaway
A woman's acknowledgment of her mother, father, husband, or master is valid in Hanafi fiqh because it binds only herself, not others, and the mother is considered an origin like the father.

6 min
Woman's Acknowledgment of a Child: Husband's Confirmation Required
Ruling with proof based on the nature of lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman's acknowledgment of a child and explain why the husband's confirmation or proof of birth is necessary.

Core Idea
A woman's claim of a child is not accepted for lineage without the husband's confirmation or proof of birth.

At first glance, a mother's acknowledgment of her child might seem straightforward. However, Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between acknowledgment that only affects the acknowledging person and acknowledgment that imposes rights or obligations on another. This passage explains why a woman's claim of a child requires the husband's verification: because the claim establishes paternity, which is primarily attached to the male.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Default Ruling
The act is a woman's acknowledgment (iqrar) that a specific child is her son. The default Hanafi ruling is that this acknowledgment is not accepted (ghayr maqbul).
The ruling is about establishing lineage (nasab), not merely claiming custody.
2
Recognize the Conditions for Acceptance
The acknowledgment becomes accepted only if one of two conditions is met: (1) the husband confirms (tasdiq) the claim, or (2) a midwife or witness testifies that the child was born in the husband's household.
These conditions protect the husband's right to deny paternity.
3
Understand the Legal Cause (Illah)
The ruling is based on the principle that lineage (nasab) fundamentally pertains to the male, not the female. The woman's claim would impose paternity on the husband, so his confirmation is required.
This is a talil (reasoning) from the nature of lineage.
4
Compare with Other Schools
Other madhahib may accept a woman's acknowledgment for maternity without husband's consent, but the Hanafi school requires verification because paternity is at stake.
This is a point of ikhtilaf with practical consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولا يقبل بالولد... اگر کوئی عورت کسی بچہ کی بابت یہ کہے کہ یہ میرا بیٹا ہے تو جب تک اس کا شوہر اس کی تصدیق نہ کر دے یا کوئی دا یہ اس کی شہادت نہ دے کہ یہ بچہ اس کے یہاں پیدا ہوا تھا۔ اس وقت تک عورت کا یہ اقرار مقبول نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس اقرار میں نسب کو دوسرے پر یعنی شوہر پر لاگو کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ نسب کا اصل تعلق مرد کے ساتھ ہے نہ کہ عورت کے ساتھ۔ اس لئے شوہر کی تصدیق ضروری ہے۔
His saying: And it is not accepted regarding a child... If a woman says concerning a child, 'This is my son,' then as long as her husband does not confirm it, or a midwife does not testify that this child was born at her place, her acknowledgment will not be accepted. Because in this acknowledgment, there is an imposition of lineage upon another, namely the husband. Because lineage fundamentally pertains to the male, not the female. Therefore, the husband's confirmation is necessary.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage clarifies a distinction: a woman can acknowledge her own parents or husband because the rights and obligations fall on herself. However, acknowledging a child is different because the child's lineage is primarily linked to the father. The woman's claim would establish paternity for the husband, which requires his confirmation or independent evidence (like testimony from a midwife that the child was born in his household). Without that, the acknowledgment is not accepted to establish the child's lineage. This ruling protects the rights of the husband and prevents false claims of paternity.

Key Terms
تصدیق (tasdiq): Confirmation or verification by the husband of the woman's claim.
بچہ (bachcha): Child; in this context, a biological child whose lineage is being claimed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Hanafi fiqh require the husband's confirmation for a woman's acknowledgment of a child?
A) Because women are unreliable and cannot be trusted.
B) Because lineage is fundamentally linked to the male, and the claim imposes paternity on the husband.
C) Because the child must consent to the acknowledgment.
D) Because a woman's testimony is only half of a man's.

Key Takeaway
A woman's acknowledgment of a child does not establish lineage unless the husband confirms or independent evidence of birth is provided, due to lineage's primary attachment to the male.

The Definition of Sulh and Key Terminology
Defines sulh and its key terms with an example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definition of sulh according to the Hanafi school and identify the three key terms (musalah alayh, musalah anhu, musali).

Core Idea
Sulh is a contract that removes dispute; its linguistic root indicates intrinsic goodness.

The Book of Sulh follows the Book of Iqrar because denial leads to dispute, and dispute is resolved through conciliation. This lesson defines sulh linguistically and legally, and clarifies the roles of the parties involved in a conciliation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the transition
Note the logical sequence: after the book on acknowledgment (iqrar), the author discusses sulh because denial after acknowledgment causes disputes, which sulh resolves.
2
Define sulh linguistically
Sulh is derived from the root salah (rectification), indicating its intrinsic goodness.
3
Define sulh technically (shar’an)
In Shari’ah, sulh is a contract that removes dispute and cuts off litigation.
4
Identify the three key terms
Musalah alayh (subject matter given in settlement), musalah anhu (right or claim dropped), and musali (the party making the settlement).
5
Apply to the example
Zaid claims a house; Khalid offers 100 dirhams to drop the claim. The dirhams are musalah alayh, the house claim is musalah anhu, and Khalid is musali.
In this example, Khalid (defendant) is the musali because he makes the offer.

ترجمہ صلح تین طرح پر ہے۔ صلح مع اقرار صلح مع سکوت اور وہ یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ نہ اقرار کرے نہ انکار۔ اور صلح مع انکار اور یہ تینوں جائز ہیں۔ کیونکہ قول باری " و الصلح خیر مطلق ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ حضور علیہ السلام کا ارشاد ہے کہ مسلمانوں کے درمیان ہر صلح جائز ہے سوائے اس صلح کے جو حرام کو حلال یا حلال کو حرام کرے۔

قَالَ الله تعالى. وَ إِنْ طَائِفَتَانِ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ اقْتَلُوا فَأَصْلِحُوا بَيْنَهُمَا اور اگر دو فریق مسلمان کے آپس میں لڑ پڑین تو ان میں ملاپ کرا دو تیسری نوع و صلح ہے جو اندیشہ شقاق کے وقت زوجین کے درمیان واقع ہو۔
قَالَ الله تعالى ,
Translation: This book is about the explanation of conciliation. Book of Conciliation. Commentary: His statement: 'Book' — after the Book of Acknowledgment, the Book of Conciliation is brought. The reason for appropriateness is clear because the denial of the acknowledger causes dispute, and dispute leads to conciliation. Conciliation linguistically is a noun from the root musalaha, derived from salah, meaning rectification of condition. So its linguistic meaning indicates its intrinsic goodness. In Shari'ah, conciliation is that contract which removes dispute and cuts off litigation. That is, a contract that eliminates contention is called conciliation. That upon which conciliation is made is called musalah alayh, that from which conciliation is made is called musalah anhu, and the one who makes conciliation is called musali. For example, Zaid claims a house from Khalid. Khalid says: 'Take one hundred dirhams from me and drop the claim of the house.' So the hundred dirhams is musalah alayh, the house is musalah anhu, and Khalid is the musali. Types of Conciliation and Their Legal Status: He said: Conciliation is of three types: conciliation with acknowledgment, conciliation with silence—which is when the defendant neither acknowledges nor denies—and conciliation with denial. All of these are permissible because of the absolute nature of Allah's statement 'And conciliation is better' and because of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Every conciliation is permissible except a conciliation that legalizes the unlawful or prohibits the lawful.' Translation: Conciliation is of three types: conciliation with acknowledgment, conciliation with silence—and that is when the defendant neither acknowledges nor denies—and conciliation with denial. All three are permissible because the divine statement 'And conciliation is better' is absolute, and because the Prophet's (peace be upon him) instruction: 'Every conciliation among Muslims is permissible except a conciliation that makes lawful what is unlawful or makes unlawful what is lawful.' Commentary on his statement: 'On three types...' Conciliation, as known above, is that mutual contract through which reconciliation between opponents is achieved. It has various types. One type is conciliation that occurs between Muslims and the people of war. Allah says: 'And if they incline to peace, then incline to it and rely upon Allah.' Second type: conciliation that occurs between the people of justice and the people of rebellion. Allah says: 'And if two parties among the believers fight, then make peace between them.' Third type: conciliation that occurs between spouses during fear of discord. Allah says: '...'
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Sulh (Conciliation) in the Hanafi fiqh text. It begins by explaining the transition from the Book of Acknowledgment (Iqrar) to the Book of Sulh: since denial leads to disputes, and disputes need resolution, the author moves to conciliation. Sulh is defined linguistically as derived from salah (rectification), and technically as a contract that removes dispute and ends litigation. The key terminology is given: musalah alayh (the subject of the settlement), musalah anhu (the matter being waived), and musali (the settling party). An example clarifies: Zaid claims a house from Khalid; Khalid offers 100 dirhams to drop the claim; the money is musalah alayh, the house is musalah anhu. The passage then presents the famous classification of sulh into three types: (1) with acknowledgment (the defendant admits the claim but settles), (2) with silence (the defendant neither admits nor denies), and (3) with denial (the defendant denies the claim but still settles). All three types are declared permissible (ja'iz) based on two primary textual proofs: the Quranic verse 'And conciliation is better' (4:128) and the hadith 'Every conciliation is permissible except one that makes lawful what is unlawful or makes unlawful what is lawful.' The passage then goes on to mention three specific applications of sulh: between Muslims and warring non-Muslims, between two warring Muslim groups, and between spouses fearing discord. For each, appropriate Quranic verses are cited. This establishes the general permissibility of sulh as a dispute resolution mechanism in Islamic law, with the only restriction being that it cannot alter the rulings of halal and haram.

Key Terms
صلح (ṣulḥ): A contract that removes dispute and cuts off litigation; a settlement between parties
مصالح علیہ (muṣālaḥ ʿalayh): The subject matter of the settlement (what is given in exchange)
مصالح عنہ (muṣālaḥ ʿanh): The matter being waived or dropped (the claim or right)
مدعی علیہ (muddaʿā ʿalayh): The defendant; the person against whom a claim is made

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of Zaid and Khalid, what is the musalah alayh?
A) The house
B) The 100 dirhams
C) The dispute itself
D) The acknowledgment

Key Takeaway
Sulh linguistically means rectification and technically is a contract that ends dispute; its key terms are musalah alayh (consideration), musalah anhu (claim dropped), and musali (settlor).

intermediate
10 min
The Three Types of Sulh and Their Permissibility
Presents the three types of sulh and their permissibility with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the three types of sulh (with acknowledgment, with silence, with denial) and state the dalil for their permissibility, applying the hadith exception.

Core Idea
All three types of sulh are permissible unless they make halal into haram or vice versa.

After defining sulh, this passage presents its threefold classification based on the defendant's stance: acknowledgment, silence, or denial. All are declared permissible based on the Quranic verse 'And conciliation is better' and the prophetic hadith, with the sole exception that sulh cannot alter Allah's rulings.

Guided Path
1
Learn the three types
The text classifies sulh based on the defendant's response: (1) with acknowledgment (iqrar), (2) with silence (sukut: neither admit nor deny), (3) with denial (inkar).
In sulh with denial, the defendant denies the claim but still agrees to settle.
2
Note the universal ruling
All three types are declared ja'iz (permissible) without exception, as stated by the author.
3
Identify the primary proofs
Two proofs are cited: the Quranic verse (4:128) 'And conciliation is better' and the hadith 'Every conciliation is permissible except one that makes lawful what is unlawful or makes unlawful what is lawful.'
The verse is general; the hadith specifies the only restriction.
4
Understand the exception
The hadith explicitly excludes any sulh that contradicts Shari'ah by reversing the halal/haram status of something.
This preserves the boundaries set by Allah.
5
Apply to examples
If a defendant denies but offers a payment to drop a claim, that is valid sulh with denial. If the settlement involves interest (riba), it is invalid because it makes haram permissible.
The exception is crucial for modern disputes.

Source Text

Key Terms
صلح مع اقرار (ṣulḥ maʿa iqrār): Settlement where the defendant acknowledges the claim but reaches a compromise on payment.
صلح مع سکوت (ṣulḥ maʿa sukūt): Settlement where the defendant neither acknowledges nor denies the claim; remains silent.
صلح مع انکار (ṣulḥ maʿa inkār): Settlement where the defendant denies the claim but agrees to pay something to end the dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, which type of sulh is prohibited?
A) Sulh with silence
B) Sulh with denial
C) Sulh that makes halal into haram or haram into halal
D) Sulh with acknowledgment involving a reduced amount

Key Takeaway
All three types of sulh are permissible, provided the settlement does not violate the boundaries of halal and haram.

Definition and Three Types of Sulh
Definition and types of sulh in financial disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sulh, differentiate its three types based on the defendant's stance, and apply the Quranic and prophetic evidence to argue its permissibility.

Core Idea
Sulh is a permissible contract that ends a dispute, whether the defendant admits, denies, or remains silent.

This passage opens the chapter on sulh (reconciliation) in financial disputes. It first clarifies the linguistic and technical meaning, then introduces three distinct scenarios based on how the defendant responds to a claim. The key ruling is that all three types are permissible (jā'iz) unless the settlement violates a clear divine command. The author supports this with Quranic and hadith evidence, providing a foundation for the Hanafi position on compromise.

Guided Path
1
Define sulh linguistically and technically
Examine the author's linguistic derivation from 'salah' (improvement/righteousness) and the technical definition: a contract that removes dispute and cuts off enmity. Identify the key terms: musalah ‘alayh (the subject of compromise), musalah ‘anhu (the right being relinquished), and musalah (the compromising party).
2
Identify the three types of sulh
The text states that in financial disputes, sulh is of three types: (1) with acknowledgment (iqrār) – the defendant admits and settles; (2) with silence (sukūt) – the defendant neither admits nor denies; (3) with denial (inkār) – the defendant denies the claim but pays to avoid an oath or further litigation. Note the characteristics and legal effect of each.
The author of Al-'Inayah argues these three are exhaustive because a defendant's response can only be affirmation, negation, or silence.
3
Cite the evidence for permissibility
The passage gives two proofs: the Quranic verse (4:128) 'wa al-sulhu khayr' (reconciliation is better) and the hadith 'kullu sulhin ja'iz...' (every settlement is permissible except one that makes halal haram or haram halal). Understand the Hanafi usul principle: absolute praise or permission indicates permissibility (ibāha).
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud, Ibn Hibban, and al-Hakim. Both proofs are general (ʿāmm), covering all three types.
4
Identify the exception to permissibility
The hadith explicitly excludes any sulh that violates the Shari'ah by allowing what is forbidden or forbidding what is allowed. This preserves the inviolability of divine rulings and serves as a universal condition for valid sulh.
This exception applies to all three types equally.
5
Note the broader categorization of sulh
The commentator expands by listing four contexts of sulh: (1) Muslims vs. warring non-Muslims, (2) between two warring Muslim factions, (3) between spouses fearing discord, and (4) financial disputes (the chapter's focus). This helps situate the three types within a wider framework.
The chapter only details the financial type, but the other contexts are mentioned to show the scope.

إِعْرَاضًا فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِمَا أَنْ يُصْلِحَا بَيْنَهُمَا صُلْحًا وَالصُّلْحُ خَيْرٌ} چوتھی نوع وہ صلح ہے جو اموال کے سلسلے میں اختلاف کنندگان کے درمیان واقع ہو۔ اس باب میں اسی نوع کا بیان ہے۔ بمنزلہ شراء برا قل ہوتی ہے۔ ۲۔ صلح مع انکار: یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ دعویٰ سے منکر ہو کر صلح کرنے پر آمادہ ہو۔ گویا اس پر جب بوجہ انکار قسم عائد ہوئی تو اس نے قسم کے عوض یہ مال دے کر صلح کری۔ ۳۔ صلح مع سکوت: صاحب کتاب نے خود ذکر کیا ہے کہ مدعی علیہ نہ اقرار کرے نہ انکار۔ صاحب عنایہ کہتے ہیں کہ صلح کا انواع ثلثہ مذکورہ میں منحصر ہونا ضروری ہے، اس لئے کہ خصم بوقت دعوی سکوت اختیار کرے گا یا کوئی جواب کیونکہ حق تعالیٰ کا ارشاد {وَالصُّلْحُ خَيْرٌ} مطلق ہے۔ نیز حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد ہے: «الصُّلْحُ جَائِزٌ بَيْنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ»
Book of Sulh. Translation: This book is about the explanation of Sulh. Commentary: His saying 'Book': The book of Sulh has been brought after the book of Iqrār. The reason of appropriateness is apparent because the denial of the confirmer is a cause of dispute, and the root of dispute is Sulh. Sulh linguistically: the name of the source meaning reconciliation, derived from Salah (righteousness) opposite of crookedness. So its linguistic meaning indicates its intrinsic goodness. In Shari'ah, Sulh is the contract that removes dispute and cuts off enmity. That is, the contract that eliminates quarrels is called Sulh. That upon which Sulh occurs is called Musalah ‘alayh, and that from which Sulh is made is called Musalah ‘anhu, and the one who makes Sulh is called Musalah (or Musalih). Example: Zayd claimed a house against Khalid. Khalid said: take one hundred dirhams from me and drop the claim of the house. So the one hundred dirhams is Musalah ‘alayh, the house is Musalah ‘anhu, and Khalid is Musalah. He said: Sulh is of three types: Sulh with acknowledgment, and Sulh with silence, and it is that the defendant neither acknowledges nor denies, and Sulh with denial. And all that is permissible due to the generality of His statement, Most High: {And reconciliation is better} and due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Every Sulh is permissible except a Sulh that makes lawful something forbidden or makes forbidden something lawful.' Translation: Sulh is of three types: Sulh with acknowledgment, Sulh with silence (which is that the defendant neither acknowledges nor denies), and Sulh with denial. And all these three are permissible because the word of Allah {And reconciliation is better} is absolute, and because the Prophet's statement that every Sulh among Muslims is permissible except a Sulh that makes lawful the unlawful or makes unlawful the lawful. Commentary: His statement 'on three types': Sulh, as known above, is the mutual contract through which reconciliation occurs between opponents. It has various types. One type is the Sulh that occurs between Muslims and people of war. Allah said: {And if they incline to peace, then incline to it and rely upon Allah}. Second type: the Sulh that occurs between people of justice and people of rebellion. Allah said: {And if two parties among the believers fight, then reconcile between them}. Third type: the Sulh that occurs between spouses at time of fear of discord. Allah said: {And if a woman fears from her husband aversion or turning away, there is no sin upon them if they make peace between them, and reconciliation is better}. Fourth type: the Sulh that occurs between disputants in matters of wealth. In this chapter is the explanation of this type. This type has three divisions: Sulh with acknowledgment, Sulh with silence, Sulh with denial. 1. Sulh with acknowledgment: It is that the defendant acknowledges the claim of the plaintiff and then makes a Sulh with him for some amount so that he drops his claim. This Sulh is like a purchase for a consideration. 2. Sulh with denial: It is that the defendant denies the claim and then agrees to make Sulh. It is as if when an oath is required from him due to his denial, he gives this wealth in exchange for the oath and makes Sulh. 3. Sulh with silence: The author himself has mentioned it: that the defendant neither acknowledges nor denies. The author of 'Inayah says that it is necessary that Sulh be confined to the three mentioned types because the opponent at the time of claim will either adopt silence or give a reply, and the reply will not be free from two states: either negative or affirmative. His statement: 'And all that is permissible': According to us, the three mentioned types of Sulh are permissible in light of the Quran and Hadith. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad also are of this view. Because Allah's statement {And reconciliation is better} is absolute, and also the Prophet's statement: 'Reconciliation is permissible among Muslims.'
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Sulh (Reconciliation/Compromise) from a commentary on Al-Hidayah. The author first establishes the placement of this book after the Book of Iqrār, noting the logical connection: denial causes dispute, and dispute leads to the need for sulh. He then provides a linguistic and technical definition of sulh: linguistically, it derives from 'salah' (righteousness), indicating its inherent goodness; technically in Shari'ah, it is a contract that eliminates conflict and enmity. The author gives a practical example: if Zayd claims a house from Khalid, and Khalid proposes to pay 100 dirhams in exchange for dropping the claim, the money is 'musalah alayh' (the subject of compromise), the house is 'musalah anhu' (the object from which compromise is made), and Khalid is 'musalah' (the one making the compromise). The core ruling then follows from the matn: Sulh is of three types in financial disputes—(1) with acknowledgment (iḥrār), where the defendant admits the claim and settles; (2) with silence (sukūt), where the defendant neither admits nor denies; and (3) with denial (inkār), where the defendant denies the claim but opts to settle. All three are permissible (jā'iz). The proof is from the absolute statement of the Quran 'Wa al-sulh khayr' (And reconciliation is better) and the general hadith 'Every sulh is permissible except a sulh that makes lawful the unlawful or makes unlawful the lawful' (reported by Abu Dawud, Ibn Hibban, Hakim, etc.). The commentator then expands by categorizing sulh into four types based on context: (1) between Muslims and warring non-Muslims, (2) between two warring Muslim factions, (3) between spouses fearing discord, and (4) between disputants over wealth, which is the focus of this chapter. For the financial type, the three subtypes are reiterated with details: sulh with acknowledgment is like a purchase (the defendant buys the cessation of the claim); sulh with denial is like a consideration paid to avoid an oath that would otherwise be required; sulh with silence keeps the situation open. The commentator also notes a view from the author of Al-'Inayah that the confinement to three types is exhaustive because the defendant's response to a claim can only be silence, denial, or acknowledgment. Finally, the passage affirms that these three types are valid in the Hanafi school, and also reports agreement from Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad, based on the absolute Quranic verse and the hadith. Importantly, the hadith provides a limit: any sulh that permits what is haram or forbids what is halal is not permissible, preserving the inviolability of divine rulings.

Key Terms
صُلْح (sulh): A contract that removes dispute and cuts off enmity; specifically in this financial context, a compromise between claimant and defendant.
مُصَالَحَة (musālaha): The verbal noun meaning the act of making peace/reconciliation, the source from which the term sulh is derived.
إِقْرَار (iqrār): Acknowledgment by the defendant of the claimant's right; in sulh ma'a al-iqrar, the defendant admits the claim and then settles.
إِنْكَار (inkār): Denial by the defendant of the claim; in sulh ma'a al-inkar, the defendant denies but pays to avoid an oath or further litigation.
سُكُوت (sukūt): Silence of the defendant, neither acknowledging nor denying the claim; this is a separate category because the legal status of the sulh may differ.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A defendant in a debt dispute remains silent when asked if he owes the amount. He then offers to pay a sum to settle. According to the Hanafi school, which type of sulh is this, and is it permissible?
A) Sulh ma'a al-inkar; it is permissible because the defendant can settle even if silent.
B) Sulh ma'a al-sukut; it is permissible because all three types are allowed.
C) Sulh ma'a al-iqrar; it is permissible only if the silence is interpreted as admission.
D) It is not a valid sulh because silence creates uncertainty.

Key Takeaway
All three types of financial sulh (with acknowledgment, silence, or denial) are permissible in the Hanafi school, based on the general Quranic and prophetic evidence, provided the settlement does not violate a clear divine ruling.

Defending the Hadith for Sulh Against Ibn Hazm
Defends the authenticity of the hadith for sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school defends the authenticity of the hadith 'Kullu sulhin ja'iz' and refutes Ibn Hazm's criticism using takhrij and narrator differentiation.

Core Idea
A hadith accused of having a weak narrator is defended by citing multiple chains and separating two similarly named narrators.

The hadith 'Kullu sulhin ja'iz' is a primary proof for the permissibility of sulh in the Hanafi school. However, some scholars, notably Ibn Hazm, challenged its authenticity due to an alleged weak narrator. In this passage, the author provides a detailed takhrij and refutes the criticism, demonstrating that the hadith remains a valid proof. Understanding this defense is crucial for appreciating how Hanafi scholars safeguard their legal evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its legal significance
The hadith 'Kullu sulhin ja'iz' is a general statement indicating the permissibility of settlements (sulh). It is a key proof for the Hanafi ruling that sulh is allowed in all matters except those explicitly prohibited.
Sulh is a broad concept covering compromise in disputes.
2
List the hadith compilers and chains
The author lists multiple compilers who recorded the hadith: Abu Dawud, Ibn Hibban, al-Hakim from Abu Hurairah; and Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, al-Hakim from Amr bin Awf. Tirmidhi declared it authentic.
Takhrij shows the hadith is well-attested.
3
Understand the criticism
Critics, including Ibn Hazm, claim the narrator Kathir bin Abdullah al-Muzani is accused of lying, making the hadith weak. Ibn Hazm asserts that this narrator is the same as Kathir bin Zaid, who is also weak.
Accusation of lying is a severe defect (jarh).
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The author presents two rebuttals: (1) Imam Bukhari himself used Kathir bin Abdullah's narration and deemed it hasan, showing he is not completely rejected. (2) The hadith has a separate chain via Kathir bin Zaid from Abu Hurairah, which is distinct from the chain via Kathir bin Abdullah.
Multiple chains strengthen the hadith (mutaba'at).
5
Evaluate the refutation of Ibn Hazm's conflation
The author dismisses Ibn Hazm's identification of the two Kathirs as pure conjecture. They share only the first name and the context of the hadith, but their lineages and chains differ, proving they are separate narrators.
This preserves the reliability of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: كل صلح جائز .... اس حدیث کی تخریج امام ابوداؤد، ابن حبان اور حاکم نے حضرت ابو ہریرہ سے اور امام ترمذی، ابن ماجہ اور حاکم نے حضرت عمرو بن عوف سے کی ہے اور امام ترمذی نے اس کی تصحیح کی ہے۔ اس پر بعض حضرات نے امام ترمذی کا تعاقب کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا راوی کثیر ابن عبد اللہ بن عمرہ بن عوف مزنی متہم بالکذب ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ امام بخاری نے الساعة التي ترجى يوم الجمعه میں کثیر بن عبد اللہ کی روایت کو حسن کہا ہے۔ (کمافی التہذیب) نیز امام ابوداؤد نے حدیث مذکور بطریق کثیر بن زید عن الولید بن رباح عن ابی ہریرہ روایت کی ہے۔ سوال ..... ابن حزم نے کہا ہے کہ کثیر بن عبداللہ ہی کثیر بن زید ہے اور بالاتفاق ساقط الاعتبار ہے۔ جواب یہ موصوف کا ظن محض ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ دو جدا جدا راوی ہیں جو نام اور سیاق متن حدیث میں مشترک اور نسب اور سند میں مختلف ہیں۔ اسی
His saying: 'Every sulh is permissible' ... The takhrij of this hadith: Imam Abu Dawud, Ibn Hibban, and Hakim narrated it from Abu Hurairah; and Imam Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and Hakim from Amr bin Awf; and Imam Tirmidhi declared it authentic. Some people have criticized Imam Tirmidhi because its narrator Kathir bin Abdullah bin Amr bin Awf al-Muzani is accused of lying. The answer is that Imam Bukhari has said in the hadith of 'the hour that is hoped for on Friday' that the narration of Kathir bin Abdullah is hasan (good). (As in al-Tahdhib). Also, Imam Abu Dawud narrated the aforementioned hadith through the chain of Kathir bin Zaid from al-Walid bin Riba' from Abu Hurairah. Objection: Ibn Hazm said that Kathir bin Abdullah is the same as Kathir bin Zaid, and by consensus, he is abandoned. Answer: This is pure conjecture from that person. Because these are two separate narrators who share only the name and the context of the hadith text, but their lineage and chain differ. So
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the proof for the permissibility of sulh. The author defends the hadith 'kullu sulhin ja'iz' against criticisms regarding its chain of transmission. The hadith has been recorded by multiple major hadith scholars: Abu Dawud, Ibn Hibban, and al-Hakim from Abu Hurairah; and Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and al-Hakim from Amr bin Awf. Imam Tirmidhi classified it as authentic (sahih). However, some critics challenged Tirmidhi's authentication because one narrator in the chain, Kathir bin Abdullah bin Amr bin Awf al-Muzani, is accused of lying. The author provides two rebuttals. First, Imam Bukhari himself—known for his strictness—has narrated from Kathir bin Abdullah in the hadith about 'the hour on Friday' and considered it hasan (good), as stated in al-Tahdhib. This indicates that Kathir is not completely unreliable. Second, the same hadith is narrated through a different chain: Kathir bin Zaid from al-Walid bin Riba' from Abu Hurairah, which is a separate, stronger chain. Then the author addresses a specific objection from Ibn Hazm (the Zahiri scholar), who claimed that Kathir bin Abdullah and Kathir bin Zaid are the same person, and that this narrator is unanimously abandoned. The author refutes this as mere conjecture: they are two different narrators who happen to share the same first name but have different patronymics and chains. Ibn Hazm's claim is baseless. This discussion is important for establishing the hadith as a reliable proof (hujjah) for the permissibility of sulh in the Hanafi school, since the opponents may try to weaken the evidence. The Hanafi scholars, by citing multiple chains, maintain the authority of the hadith, ensuring that the ruling of permissibility stands on solid ground.

Key Terms
تَخْرِيج (takhrij): The process of citing the sources and chains of transmission for a hadith; here, the author lists the hadith compilers who recorded this hadith.
مُتَّهَمٌ بِالْكَذِبِ (muttahamun bi al-kadhib): A narrator accused of lying; this is a serious jarh (defect) that typically renders a hadith very weak unless supported.
حَسَن (hasan): A hadith classification meaning 'good' – acceptable as proof, though not as strong as sahih. Used by Bukhari here.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the Hanafi commentator refute Ibn Hazm's claim that the narrator Kathir bin Abdullah is the same as Kathir bin Zaid?
A) He argues that both are trustworthy despite the accusation
B) He proves they are two different narrators with different lineages and chains
C) He admits the hadith is weak but uses the Quranic verse as the primary proof
D) He ignores Ibn Hazm's objection entirely

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'Kullu sulhin ja'iz' is defended as authentic through multiple chains and the separation of two narrators named Kathir, ensuring its validity as proof for the permissibility of sulh in the Hanafi school.

The Ruling on Sulh with Denial or Silence: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i's objection and the Hanafi response regarding sulh with denial or silence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on sulh with denial or silence and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Sulh with denial is valid because the hadith's exception applies only to inherently haram/halal items, not financial claims.

In this passage, the commentator presents Imam al-Shafi'i's objection to sulh (compromise) when the defendant denies the claim or remains silent, and the Hanafi school's robust response. The dispute centers on whether such a settlement constitutes a permissible exchange or falls under forbidden bribery. Understanding this disagreement clarifies the Hanafi principle of interpreting textual exceptions narrowly and recognizing legitimate motivations behind compromise.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that sulh (compromise) is valid even when the defendant denies the claim or remains silent. The claimant takes the money in exchange for his alleged right, and the defendant pays to cut off litigation.
2
Identify the opposing school's view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that such sulh is invalid because it either makes haram halal or vice versa and resembles bribery (rishwah).
The Shafi'i position is based on a hadith prohibiting sulh that changes the ruling of halal/haram.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Their proof is the hadith: 'Sulh is permissible among Muslims except a sulh that makes haram halal or halal haram.' They argue that in sulh with denial, the payment is haram for the receiver if the claim is false, or halal for the giver if the claim is true, thus reversing the ruling.
Also they analogize to bribery because the defendant pays to end the case.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis restrict the hadith's exception to objects that are inherently haram (e.g., wine) or inherently halal (e.g., right to intercourse with a co-wife), not to financial claims. The claimant's intention is to recover his right, and the defendant's payment to avoid litigation is legitimate, as wealth is a protection against harm.
The Hanafi response also cites the Quranic verse 'And reconciliation is good' (4:128) as general permission.
5
Determine the practical difference
In practice, Hanafis allow sulh without admission of the claim, while Shafi'is require the defendant to admit the claim for the sulh to be valid.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of the disagreement).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي لَا يَجُوزُ مَعَ إِنْكَارِ أَوْ سُكُوتٍ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَهَذَا بِهَذِهِ الصَّفَةِ لِاَنَّ الْبَدَلَ كَانَ حَلَالًا عَلَى الدَّافِعِ حَرَامًا عَلَى الْأَخِذِ فَيَنْقَلِبُ الْأَمْرُ وَ لاتَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ يَدْفَعُ الْمَالَ لِقَطْعِ الْخُصُومَةِ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ وَهَذَا رِشْوَةً

وَلَنَا مَا تَلَوْنَا وَاَوَّلُ مَا رَوَيْنَا وَتَاوِيلُ آخِرِهِ اَحَلَّ حَرَامًا لِعَيْنِهِ كَالْخَمْرِ اَوْ حَرَّمَ حَلَالًا لِعَيْنِهِ كَالصُّلْحِ عَلَى أَنْ يَطَأَ الضَّرَّةَ وَلِاَنَّ هَذَا صُلْحٌ بَعْدَ دَعْوى صَحِيْحَةٍ فَيُقَضِي بِجَوَازِهِ لِاَنَّ الْمُدَّعِى يَأْخُذُهُ عِوَضًا عَنْ حَقِهِ فِي زَعْمِهِ وَهَذَا مَشْرُوعٌ وَالْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ يَدْفَعُهُ لِدَفْعِ الْخُصُومَةِ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ وَهَذَا مَشْرُوعٌ أَيْضًا إِذِ الْمَالُ وِقَايَةً الْأَنفُسِ وَدَفْعُ الرِشْوَةِ لِدَفْعِ الظُّلْمِ أَمْرٌ جَائِزٌ
And al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible with denial or silence because of what we narrated, and this is of this description because the compensation was halal for the giver and haram for the receiver, so the matter is reversed, and the defendant gives money to cut off litigation from himself, and this is a bribe. And we have what we recited and the beginning of what we narrated, and the interpretation of its end: it made permissible something specifically haram like wine, or made haram something specifically permissible like sulh on condition of intercourse with a co-wife, and because this is a sulh after a valid claim, so it is ruled permissible because the claimant takes it in exchange for his right in his belief, and this is legislated, and the defendant gives it to repel litigation from himself, and this is also legislated since wealth is a protection of lives, and giving a bribe to repel oppression is permissible.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of sulh (compromise settlement) when it involves denial (inkar) or silence (sukut) of the claim. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that such sulh is not permissible, basing his view on a hadith that prohibits making permissible what is haram or vice versa. He argues that in sulh with denial, the compensation is halal for the giver (defendant) and haram for the receiver (claimant) if the claim was false, or vice versa if true, thus reversing the ruling. He also likens this to bribery (rishwah) since the defendant pays to end the dispute. The Hanafi school responds by citing the general Quranic verse 'And reconciliation is good' (al-sulhu khayr), which encompasses all types of sulh. They interpret the hadith's restriction as applying only to cases where the object is inherently haram (like wine) or inherently halal (like the right to intercourse with a co-wife), not to financial disputes. They further argue that the claimant takes the money as consideration for his claimed right (in his belief), which is legitimate, and the defendant pays to protect himself from litigation, which is also legitimate, likening it to giving money to repel oppression, which is permissible. This establishes the Hanafi position that sulh with denial or silence is valid, provided the claim is valid and there is no clear injustice.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A compromise or settlement between disputing parties to end litigation.
الصلح مع الإنكار (al-sulh ma'a al-inkar): A settlement where the defendant denies the claim but pays to end the dispute.
الصلح مع السكوت (al-sulh ma'a al-sukut): A settlement where the defendant remains silent about the claim.
رشوة (rishwah): Bribe; payment to influence a decision or end a case unjustly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is sulh with denial (ma'a al-inkar) considered valid despite the hadith warning against making haram halal?
A) Because the defendant's denial is presumed true.
B) Because the hadith's exception applies only to objects inherently haram or halal, not to financial claims.
C) Because the claimant is always truthful.
D) Because the payment is considered a gift, not compensation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates sulh with denial or silence by interpreting the hadith's prohibition narrowly and recognizing the legitimate motives of both parties, distinguishing it from bribery.

The Generality of Sulh Proofs: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Hanafi defense of sulh generality against Shafi'i objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the generality of sulh proofs (Quranic verse and hadith) and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding sulh ma'a al-inkar.

Core Idea
The Quranic 'wa-l-sulhu khayr' is general ('amm) and includes sulh with denial, as long as it does not change inherent rulings.

Sulh (settlement) is recommended in Islamic law, but its scope is disputed between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafi school holds that the primary proofs—the Quranic verse 'wa-l-sulhu khayr' and the hadith 'al-sulhu ja'iz bayna al-muslimin'—are general and apply to all types of sulh, including those where the defendant denies the claim (sulh ma'a al-inkar). The Shafi'is restrict these texts to cases with admission (iqrar). In this lesson, we will walk through the proofs, objections, and Hanafi responses as presented in Ashraf al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary proofs for sulh
The Quranic verse (4:128) 'wa-l-sulhu khayr' and the hadith 'al-sulhu ja'iz bayna al-muslimin'. Note the Hanafi claim that they are general ('amm) and cover all types of sulh.
The verse is used as a major premise: 'Every sulh (that does not involve inherent change) is good.'
2
Analyze the Shafi'i objections regarding context and generality
Shafi'is argue that the verse is contextually restricted to marital sulh (sulh al-zawjayn) and that the hadith's exception (except a sulh that makes halal haram) negates generality. Also, they claim sulh with denial is bribery.
Ibn Hazm denies any generality in the verse.
3
Trace the Hanafi responses to each objection
Hanafis respond: (1) The verse's cause (tahsil al-khayr) is general, not restricted to marital context. (2) The hadith's exception only excludes sulh that changes inherent rulings (like making wine halal). (3) Sulh with denial is not bribery because it ends a valid dispute.
The rational proof distinguishes sulh from bribery: the plaintiff takes money as his claimed right, the defendant gives to avoid litigation.
4
Examine the reliance on Zahir al-Riwayah
The Hanafi position is based on the authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah texts (Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Kafi, al-Hidayah). A contrary narration in ghayr al-Zahir al-Riwayah is not relied upon.
The Shafi'is exploit this weak narration in their objection.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Per Hanafis, sulh with denial is valid; the plaintiff becomes owner of the settlement amount, and the defendant is released from the claim. Per Shafi'is, the sulh is invalid; the plaintiff must return the money, and the claim remains.
This difference affects actual property rights and litigation outcomes.

Source Text

الْأَنفُسِ وَدَفْعُ الرِشْوَةِ لِدَفْعِ الظُّلْمِ أَمْرٌ جَائِزٌ
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل وہ آیت ہے جو ہم نے تلاوت کی اور آغاز اس حدیث کا جو ہم نے روایت کی اور اس کے آخر کی تاویل یہ ہے کہ جو حلال کرے حرام لعینہ کو جیسے شراب یا حرام کرے حلال لعینہ کو جیسے اس پر صلح کرنا کہ سوتن سے وہلی نہیں کرے گا اور اس لئے کہ یہ صلح صحیح دعوئی کے بعد ہے تو اس کے جواز کا حکم دیا جائے گا کیونکہ مدعی بزعم خود وہ مال اپنے حق کے عوض میں لے گا اور یہ مشروع ہے اور مدعی علیہ اپنی ذات سے دفع خصومت کے لئے دے گا اور یہ بھی مشروع ہے۔ کیونکہ مال تو جانوں کی حفاظت کے لئے ہے اور دفع ظلم کے لئے رشوت دے دینا جائز ہے۔

معہود مراد ہو تو عموم نہ رہا۔
جواب بقول صاحب اسرار یہ برائے تعطیل ہے۔ ای لا جناح عليها ان يصال حالان الصلح خیر “ پس یہ عام ہوئی۔ کیونکہ علت حکم کے اسی محل کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ہوتی جس میں علت ذکر کی گئی ہے بلکہ جہاں بھی وہ علت پائی جائے وہیں اس کا حکم لاگو ہوگا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ اگر جنس پر محمول کیا جائے تو اس میں معہود اور غیر معہود سب داخل ہوگا اور عہد کی صورت میں صرف معہود پر منحصر ہوگا۔ فـكـان حـمـلـه على الجنس احق كما في قوله تعالى " والله يعلم المفسد من المصلح اى جميع المفسدين والمصلحین۔ صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ قواعد اصول کے مناسب یہی تقریر ہے بلکہ قواعد معقول کے مطابق بھی یہی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں والصُّلْحُ خیر شکل اول کے کبری کی جگہ ہوگا۔ گویا یوں کہا گیا۔ فان هذا صلح خیر نے اور یہ معلوم ہے کہ شکل اول کے انتاج کے لئے کلیت کبری شرط ہے۔ سوال اگر جملہ مذکورہ برائے تعطیل ہوتا تو واؤ کے بجائے فاعلا کر فالصلح خیر کہا جاتا۔
