And if the substitute in sulh is, for example, a slave and a defect is found in him, then returning him is permissible. Also, if at the time of sulh he could not see the object of sulh, after seeing he can return it. Similarly, if in sulh one party wants to stipulate an option of three days for himself, he is entitled to it. Also, ignorance of the substitute in sulh invalidates the sulh, because it is like ignorance of the price in a sale, which invalidates the sale. Yes, ignorance of the subject of reconciliation (musalah 'anhu) does not harm the sulh, because it falls from the liability of the defendant, and ignorance of what is dropped does not lead to dispute. Also, ability to deliver the substitute is necessary. So if sulh is made upon a runaway slave, it is not valid.

But it should be clear that sulh with iqrar is property. It being in the meaning of sale when in exchange for property, as mentioned above, is when the sulh occurs upon a claim different from the subject of claim. If it occurs upon the same subject of claim, then three cases are possible: it is less than the claim, equal to it, or more. If less than the claim, it is reduction and remission (hatt wa ibra'). If equal to the claim, it is receipt and satisfaction (qabd wa istifa'). If more, it is surplus and gift (fadl wa hibah). This is explicitly stated in al-Tabyin and others.

Fa'idah: The author of 'Inayah wrote that the aforementioned ruling is not absolute but has detail: According to the two substitutes, sulh is of four types. Sulh of a known thing for a known thing: this is absolutely valid. Sulh of an unknown thing for an unknown thing: it has several forms. Either delivery is required or not. If delivery is not required, e.g., the plaintiff claimed his right in the defendant's house, and the defendant claimed his right in the land in the plaintiff's possession, and both made sulh on dropping their claims, this is valid. If delivery is required and they make sulh that one of them will give some property so that the other drops his claim, and that property is not specified, or they make sulh that the defendant will hand over the thing claimed, this sulh is not valid. Sulh of an unknown thing for a known thing where delivery is required: e.g., someone has a house in his possession, the plaintiff claims a right in it without specifying it, then they make sulh that the plaintiff will give a known property so that the defendant hands over the thing claimed, this is also not valid. If delivery is not required, as in the mentioned case if they make sulh that the plaintiff will drop his claim, this is valid. Fourth: Sulh of a known thing for an unknown thing. In this case, if delivery is required it is not valid, otherwise valid. In all these cases, the general principle is: any ignorance that leads to dispute and prevents delivery invalidates the sulh.

Tanbih: The author of Nata'ij says that the jurists stated a general principle regarding sulh: it is necessary to interpret the contract of sulh according to the closest contract (as will be explained later). The author of the book (i.e., al-Hidayah) gave a rule: sulh with iqrar, if property for property, is interpreted as a sale; if property for benefits, as ijarah. But this rule is incomplete because sulh with iqrar also occurs from benefits for property or from benefits for benefits. For example, someone bequeathed the dwelling of his house to a person for one year, then the testator died, and the legatee claimed the right of dwelling. The heirs made sulh with him in exchange for a specified amount or one month's service of a slave or riding an animal to Baghdad—all this is valid (as will come in a later chapter), yet this rule is not mentioned in the book (though it is in the meaning of ijarah). Also, sulh occurs from something that is neither property nor benefit, like sulh for intentional injury, which is valid and is like a marriage contract, such that anything that can be a dower in marriage can be a substitute in sulh, yet this is also not mentioned in the rule. Similarly, sulh from a claim of slavery in exchange for property is in the meaning of emancipation for property. And sometimes a husband's claim of marriage in exchange for property is in the meaning of divorce for ransom (khul'). All these are neither included in the mentioned rule nor understood from it.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the contract of sulh (settlement) when it involves acknowledgment (iqrar) by the defendant. The text begins by discussing practical aspects: if a slave given as substitute has a defect, it can be returned; a right of inspection and option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart) is recognized. The central point is that ignorance (jahl) regarding the substitute (badal) invalidates the sulh, by analogy to sale where ignorance of price invalidates. However, ignorance of what is being dropped (the claim itself) does not harm, as dropping obligations is not subject to dispute. The requirement of ability to deliver (tamkin al-taslim) is stressed, like a runaway slave. The passage then clarifies the legal nature: sulh with iqrar, when it concerns property for property, is treated like a sale (bay'). Three cases: if the substitute is less than the claim, it is remission (ibra'); if equal, it is receipt (qabd); if more, it is a gift (hibah). A fa'idah from Sahib 'Inayah expands: sulh is classified into four types based on knowledge/ignorance of the two substitutes (the thing given and the thing dropped). The guiding principle is that any ignorance that leads to dispute (mufdi ila al-niza') and prevents delivery invalidates sulh. The tanbih from Sahib Nata'ij critiques the general rule that sulh should be interpreted by the nearest contract, noting that the Hidayah's rule (sulh as sale or ijarah) is incomplete because sulh can also involve benefits for benefits, claims of slavery, intentional injury (like nikah), and claims of marriage (like khul'). Thus, the rule must be applied with nuance.

Key Terms
تنبیہ (tanbih): A critical note or refinement by a later commentator pointing out incompleteness or nuance.
اقرب عقود (aqrab al-'uqud): The nearest contract type that resembles the sulh in its essence, used to determine the applicable rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tanbih, sulh for intentional injury (janayat 'amd) is analogous to which contract?
A) Sale (bay')
B) Ijarah
C) Nikah (marriage)
D) Itq (emancipation)

Key Takeaway
The rule that sulh is interpreted by the nearest contract is broader than just sale and ijarah; it also includes nikah, itq, and khul', and a mufti must consider all possibilities.

Sulh for Benefits: Ijarah Analogy and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on sulh for benefits with intra-Hanafi dispute on death's effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf on whether sulh from property to benefits voids upon death, and distinguish the rulings for different types of benefits.

Core Idea
Sulh for benefits is like ijarah, but Abu Yusuf carves exceptions to preserve the contract's purpose: ending disputes.

This lesson delves into the ruling when a settlement (sulh) involves exchanging property for the use of benefits (manafi'), such as dwelling, riding, or service. While the general Hanafi principle treats such a sulh as analogous to an ijarah (lease) contract, the school's two great imams, Muhammad al-Shaybani and Abu Yusuf, differ on a crucial point: what happens when one party dies before the benefits are fully utilized? Understanding this dispute sharpens your appreciation for how the Hanafi school balances contract structure (ma'na) with contractual purpose (qat' al-munaza'ah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic rule
Recognize that sulh from property to benefits is treated like ijarah because the meaning of ijarah (tamlik al-manafi' bi mal) is present. Contracts are considered by their meanings, not names.
This is the general principle from the matn.
2
Understand the implications of the ijarah analogy
Like ijarah, this sulh requires specification of time (taqit) and becomes void upon death of either party, destruction of the subject matter, or any condition that contradicts ijarah.
These consequences flow from the analogy.
3
Locate the ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad applies the analogy absolutely: the sulh voids in all cases upon death or destruction. Imam Abu Yusuf distinguishes between types of benefits: dwelling and service (which are not entirely personal) vs. riding and wearing (which are personal).
The dispute is within the Hanafi school.
4
Examine Abu Yusuf's rationale
Abu Yusuf argues that the purpose of sulh is to cut off dispute (qat' al-munaza'ah). Voiding the contract upon death in dwelling and service would revive the dispute, defeating the purpose. For riding and wearing, the benefit is too personal for the heir to substitute.
Purpose overrides strict analogy in these cases.
5
Evaluate the practical outcome
Under Imam Muhammad, the claimant's original claim revives upon death or destruction. Under Abu Yusuf, for dwelling and service, the contract continues: the claimant receives the benefit from the estate, or the heir steps in.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: different results for the same scenario.

Source Text

مال سے منافع کے عوض صلح کا حکم
وَإِنْ وَقَعَ عَنْ مَالِ بِمَنَافِعِ يُعْتَبَرُ بِالْإِجَارَاتِ لِوُجُودِ مَعْنَى الْإِجَارَةِ وَهُوَ تَمْلِيْكُ الْمَنَافِعِ بِمَالٍ وَالْإِعْتِبَارُ فِي الْعُقُودِ لِمَعَانِيهَا فَيُشْتَرَطُ التَّوْقِيتُ فِيهَا وَيَبْطُلُ الصُّلْحُ بِمَوْتِ أَحَدِهِمَا فِي الْمُدَّةِ لِأَنَّهُ إِجَارَةً

ترجمہ اور اگر مال سے منافع کے عوض واقع ہو تو اعتبار کیا جائے گا اجازت کے ساتھ معنی اجارہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اور مال کے عوض منافع کا مالک کرنا ہے اور اعتبار عقود میں ان کے معنی کا ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس میں بیان مدت شرط ہوگا اور مدت میں کسی ایک کے مرنے سے صلح باطل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ یہ تو اجارہ ہے۔ تشريح ... قوله عن مال بمنافع الخ - اور اگر لح مع اقرار مال کی طرف سے منافع کے عوض واقع ہو تو اسکا اعتبار اجارہ سے کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس میں اجارہ کے معنی یعنی منافع کی تملیک بعوض مال موجود ہے اور اس میں کوئی اور اس میں کوئی شک ہی نہیں کہ عقود میں صرف معنی کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے چنانچہ ہبہ بشرط عوض بیع ہوتا ہے اور کفالہ بشرط براءت اصیل حوالہ ہوتا ہے اور حوالہ بشرط مطالبہ اصیل کفالہ ہوتا ہے۔ پس ہر وہ منفعت جس کا استحقاق عقد اجارہ سے ہوتا ہے اس کا استحقاق صلح سے بھی ہو گا و مالا فلا۔
......
پس اگر زید نے عمرو پر کسی چیز کادعویٰ کیا اور عمرو نے اس کا اقرار کر لیا پھر عمرو نے زید کے ساتھ ایک سال تک رہنے یا اپنی سواری پر سوار ہونے یا اپنا کپڑا پہنے یا اپنے غلام سے خدمت حاصل کرنے یا اپنی زمین کاشت کرنے پر صلح کرلی تو اس کا حکم اجارہ کے مانند ہے کہ جیسے اجارہ میں استیفاء منفعت کی مدت مقرر کرنا شرط ہے اس طرح اس میں شرط ہے اور جیسے اجارہ احد المتعاقدین کی موت ہے باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ ایسے ہی یہ بھی باطل ہو جائے گی۔ نیز اگر رہائش کی صورت میں ابد یا حتی یموت کی قید لگائی یا زراعت کی صورت میں مدت بیان نہیں کی تو صلح جائز نہ ہوگی۔ فائده صلح عن المال بالمنافع کا علی الاطلاق اجارہ کے معنی میں ہونا امام محمد کا قول ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ مدعی یا مدعلی علیہ کے مرنے سے اسی طرح محل منفعت کے تلف ہو جانے سے صلح فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ خواہ خود بخود تلف ہوا ہو یا کسی نے تلف کر دیا ہو۔ اب قیمت کا ضمان لازم ہو گا اگر اتلاف استیفاء منفعت سے قبل ہو اور مدگی اپنے دعوئی میں رجوع کرے گا۔ ہاں اگر کچھ منفعت حاصل کر چکا تو اس کے بقدر دعوی ختم ہو جائے گا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ امام محمد نے صلح کو بمنزلہ اجارہ قرار دیا ہے۔ اور اجارہ موجر و مستاجر کے مرنے اور محل منفعت کے ہلاک ہو جانے سے باطل ہو جاتا ہے تو ایسے ہی صلح بھی باطل ہو جائے گی۔ بخلاف امام ابو یوسف کے کہ ان کے نزدیک صلح مذکور من کل الوجود اجارہ کی طرح نہیں ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر مکان کا دعویٰ کیا پھر اس کی طرف سے مکان کی رہائش یا ایک سالہ خدمت عبد یا بغداد تک رکوب دا بہ یا ایک ماہ کپڑا پہنے پر صلح کی۔ پھر مدعی علیہ مر گیا۔یا قبل از استیفاء محل منفعت ہلاک ہو گیا تو از روئے قیاس صلح باطل ہو جائے گی۔ یہی امام محمد کا قول ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مدعی علیہ مرا تو صلح باطل نہ ہوگی بلکہ مدعی اس کو وصول کرے گا اور اگر مدعی مراتب بھی خدمت عبد اور مکان کی رہائش میں صلح باطل نہ ہوگی بلکہ مدعی اس کو وصول کرے گا اور اگر مدعی مراتب بھی خدمت عبداور مکان کی رہائش میں صلح باطل نہ ہوگی۔ بلکہ وارث اس کا قائم مقام ہوگا۔ ہاں رکوب دابہ اور بس ثوب کے مسئلہ میں باطل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ صلح قطع منازعت کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور ان میں سے کسی ایک کے مرنے سے صلح باطل کرنے میں منازعت کو واپس لانا ہے۔
اور رکوب ولبس میں لوگوں کا طریق استعمال چونکہ مختلف ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے وارث ان میں قائم مقام نہ ہوگا۔ (کفایہ)
Ruling on sulh from property for benefits: And if it occurs from property in exchange for benefits, it is treated according to ijarah due to the presence of the meaning of ijarah, which is the ownership of benefits in exchange for property, and consideration in contracts is given to their meanings. So specification of time is required in it, and the sulh becomes void upon the death of either party during the period because it is ijarah.

Translation: And if it occurs from property in exchange for benefits, it will be treated as ijarah because the meaning of ijarah is found, which is making the owner of benefits in exchange for property, and consideration in contracts is given to their meanings. So specifying the time is a condition, and upon the death of either during the period, the sulh becomes void because it is ijarah. Commentary: ... regarding his saying 'from property for benefits' — and if sulh with iqrar occurs from property in exchange for benefits, it will be treated as ijarah because the meaning of ijarah, i.e., ownership of benefits for property, is present, and there is no doubt that in contracts only meanings are considered, just as a gift with a condition of exchange becomes a sale, and a guarantee with a condition of the principal's discharge becomes a transfer (hawalah), and a transfer with a condition of recourse to the principal becomes a guarantee. So every benefit that is entitled through ijarah is also entitled through sulh, and so on.

So if Zayd claimed something from 'Amr and 'Amr acknowledged it, then 'Amr made sulh with Zayd for dwelling for one year, or riding his mount, or wearing his garment, or using his slave's service, or cultivating his land — the ruling is like ijarah: just as in ijarah it is a condition to specify the period of utilization, similarly here it is a condition; and just as ijarah becomes void upon the death of either contracting party, similarly this becomes void. Also, if in the case of dwelling the condition 'forever' or 'until death' is laid, or in cultivation the period is not specified, the sulh is not valid. Benefit: The opinion that sulh from property for benefits is absolutely in the meaning of ijarah is the saying of Imam Muhammad. So much so that upon the death of the claimant or defendant, and similarly upon the destruction of the subject of benefit, the sulh becomes invalid — whether it perished by itself or someone destroyed it. Then compensation (daman) for the value becomes due if the destruction occurs before utilization, and the claimant will revert to his claim. Yes, if he had already obtained some benefit, his claim is extinguished to that extent. The reason is that Imam Muhammad considered sulh as in the status of ijarah, and ijarah becomes void upon the death of the lessor or lessee and upon the destruction of the subject of benefit, so similarly sulh becomes void. Contrary to Imam Abu Yusuf, who holds that this sulh is not completely like ijarah. So if the claim was for a house, then a dwelling in that house for one year, or service of a slave for one year, or riding a mount to Baghdad, or wearing a garment for one month, was made as sulh, then the defendant died or the subject of benefit was destroyed before utilization — according to analogy, the sulh would be void; this is the saying of Imam Muhammad. Imam Abu Yusuf says: If the defendant dies, the sulh does not become void, rather the claimant will receive it (the benefit); and if the claimant dies, similarly in the cases of slave service and house dwelling, the sulh does not become void, but the heir takes his place. Yes, in the cases of riding an animal and wearing a garment, it does become void, because sulh is for cutting off dispute, and voiding it upon death brings back the dispute. And in riding and wearing, since people's way of using them differs, the heir cannot take his place. (Kifayah)
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage introduces the ruling that when sulh involves property (mal) in exchange for benefits (manafi'), it is treated like an ijarah (lease) contract. The reasoning is that contracts are classified by their underlying meaning (ma'na), not their name. Just as a gift with a condition of return becomes a sale, this sulh takes the legal rulings of ijarah. Therefore, specifying the duration (taqit) is a condition for validity, and the contract is voided by the death of either party during the term, by the destruction of the subject matter, and by any condition that contradicts ijarah. The text then highlights an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad holds that all such sulhs are completely equivalent to ijarah, so death or destruction invalidates them entirely. Imam Abu Yusuf distinguishes: In contracts of dwelling (sukna) and slave service (khidmat al-'abd), the sulh does not become void upon death because the purpose of ending the dispute (qat' al-munaza'ah) would be undermined; the heir can step in. However, in cases of riding a mount (rukoob al-dabbah) and wearing a garment (lubs al-thawb), the sulh does become void because those benefits are personal to the parties and cannot be transferred to heirs due to differences in usage. This dispute reflects deeper principles about the nature of sulh: it is primarily a contract of amicable settlement, not a pure ijarah, and its validity should be assessed with that aim in mind.

Key Terms
منافع (manafi'): Usufruct or benefits derived from a property, such as dwelling, riding, service, or wearing.
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract of lease or hire for the use of benefits in exchange for compensation.
تملیک المنافع (tamlik al-manafi'): Transfer of ownership of benefits, which is the core meaning of ijarah and this type of sulh.
قطع منازعت (qat' al-munaza'ah): The purpose of sulh: to end dispute, which influences its rulings according to Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, in which type of benefit does the death of the defendant NOT void the sulh?
A) Riding an animal
B) Wearing a garment
C) Dwelling in a house
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats sulh for benefits as ijarah, but Imam Abu Yusuf's exceptions show that the contract's purpose (ending disputes) can override strict analogy in some benefit types.

Sulh with Silence or Denial: Dual Nature and Effect on Shuf'ah
Explains that sulh with silence/denial is fidyah for defendant and mu'awadah for plaintiff, and its effect on shuf'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dual nature of sulh from silence/denial and apply the distinction between sulh 'an and sulh 'ala to determine whether shuf'ah is obligatory.

Core Idea
Sulh from denial is a fidyah for the defendant but an exchange for the plaintiff; the contract's effect differs per party.

This lesson explores a nuanced ruling from Al-Hidayah on the legal nature of sulh (compromise) when the defendant remains silent or denies the claim. The author, al-Marghinani, explains that such a sulh has a dual character: for the defendant it is a payment to avoid an oath and end litigation, while for the plaintiff it is an exchange. This duality directly impacts the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah), which applies only when the transaction is a true sale from the relevant party's perspective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios of sulh
Sulh when the defendant remains silent (sukut) or denies (inkar) the claim. Both are treated alike in Hanafi law.
Silence is ambiguous but does not constitute admission.
2
Analyze the dual legal nature
For the defendant, sulh is a fidyah (ransom) to avoid oath and end dispute. For the plaintiff, it is a mu'awadah (exchange) because he believes he is receiving compensation.
The contract has different rulings for different parties.
3
Examine the analogy with iqalah
Al-Marghinani compares this dual nature to iqalah (mutual rescission), which is a rescission for the original parties but a new sale for third parties.
Illustrates that a single contract can have multiple effects.
4
Apply the principle to shuf'ah
In sulh 'an dar (from a house) with denial or silence, shuf'ah is not wajib because the defendant retains the house as his original right. In sulh 'ala dar (on a house), shuf'ah is wajib because it is a true exchange from the plaintiff's perspective.
The plaintiff's belief does not bind the defendant.

Source Text

قَالَ وَالصُّلْحُ عَنِ السُّكُوتِ وَالْإِنْكَارِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ لِافْتِدَاءِ الْيَمِينِ وَقَطْعِ الْخُصُومَةِ وَفِي حَقِّ الْمُدَّعِي لِمَعْنَى الْمُعَاوَضَةِ لِمَا بَيَّنَا وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَخْتَلِفَ حُكْمُ الْعَقْدِ فِي حَقِّهِمَا كَمَا يَخْتَلِفُ حُكْمُ الْإِقَالَةِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُتَعَاقِدَيْنِ وَغَيْرِهِمَا وَهَذَا فِي الْإِنْكَارِ ظَاهِرٌ وَكَذَا فِي السُّكُوتِ لِأَنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ الْإِقْرَارَ وَالْجُحُودَ فَلَا يَثْبُتُ كَوْنُهُ عِوَضًا فِي حَقِّهِ بِالشَّكِّ. قَالَ وَإِذَا صَالَحَ عَنْ دَارٍ لَمْ يَجِبْ فِيهَا الشُّفْعَةُ قَالَ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا كَانَ عَنْ إِنْكَارٍ أَوْ سُكُوتٍ لِأَنَّهُ يَأْخُذُهَا عَلَى أَصْلِ حَقِّهِ وَيَدْفَعُ الْمَالَ دَفْعًا لِخُصُومَةِ الْمُدَّعِي وَزَعْمُ الْمُدَّعِي لَا يَلْزَمُهُ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا صَالَحَ عَلَى دَارٍ حَيْثُ يَجِبُ فِيهَا الشُّفْعَةُ لِأَنَّ الْمُدَّعِي يَأْخُذُهَا عِوَضًا عَنِ الْمَالِ فَكَانَ مُعَاوَضَةً فِي حَقِّهِ فَيَلْزَمُهُ الشُّفْعَةُ بِإِقْرَارِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ يُكَذِّبُهُ
ترجمہ: اور صلح مع سکوت و صلح مع انکار مدعی علیہ کے حق میں قسم کا فدیہ دینے اور جھگڑا مٹانے کے طور پر اور مدعی کے حق میں بدرجہ معاوضہ ہوتی ہے اسی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی اور یہ جائز ہے کہ ان کے حق میں عقد کا حکم مختلف ہو جائے۔ جیسے اقالہ کا حکم متعاقدین اور ان کے غیر کے حق میں مختلف ہوتا ہے اور یہ صلح مع انکار میں تو ظاہر ہے اور ایسے ہی صلح مع سکوت میں کیونکہ اس میں اقرار وانکار دونوں کا احتمال ہے تو اس کے حق میں عوض ہونا بوجہ شک کے ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ جب صلح کی گھر سے تو اس میں شفعہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ جب صلح مع انکار یا صلح مع سکوت ہو۔ کیونکہ مدعی علیہ اس کو اپنے اصلی حق پر لیتا ہے اور مدعی کی خصومت دفع ہونے کے لئے دیتا ہے۔ اور مدعی کا اعتقاد اس پر لازم نہیں۔ بخلاف اس کے جب صلح دار پر کی ہو کہ اس میں شفعہ واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مدعی اس کو مال کا عوض سمجھ کر لیتا ہے تو اس کے حق میں معاوضہ ہو گا۔ پس اس کے اقرار سے شفعہ لازم ہوگا۔ گو مدعی علیہ اس کو جھوٹا بتلاتا ہے۔
تشریح: قوله والصُّلْحُ عن السكوت - اگر صلح مدعی علیہ کے سکوت یا اس کے انکار سے ہو تو یہ مدعی کے حق میں معاوضہ اور مدعی علیہ کے حق میں نزاع اور قسم کا فدیہ ہوتا ہے۔ مدعی کے حق میں معاوضہ اس لئے ہے کہ وہ بزعم خود اپنے حق کا عوض لیتا ہے اور مدعی علیہ کے حق میں یمین کا فدیہ ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ اگر صلح واقع نہ ہوتی تو مدعی علیہ پر قسم لازم آتی اور جھگڑا مٹانے کی غرض سے دے رہا ہے۔ ممکن ہے کوئی یہ اعتراض کرے کہ عقد جب ایک صفت کے ساتھ متصف ہو چکا تو پھر وہ دوسری صفت کے ساتھ کیسے متصف ہوگا۔ ويجوز ان يختلف حكم العقد ... الخ - سے اس کا جواب دیتے ہیں کہ یہ بات ممکن ہے کہ اس صلح کا حکم دونوں کے حق میں مختلف ہو۔ یعنی مثلا مدعی کے حق میں صلح بمعنی بیع یا اجارہ ہو اور دوسرے کے حق میں نہ ہو۔ جیسے اقالہ کی صورت میں ہوتا ہے کہ اقالہ متعاقدین کے حق میں تو فسخ ہوتا ہے اور دوسروں کے حق میں بیع جدید ہوتا ہے۔ ایسے ہی عقد نکاح ہے کہ اس کا حکم اپنی بیوی کے حق میں حلت ہے اور اس کی ماں کے حق میں حرمت مؤبدة ہے۔ تنبیہ: سکوت یا انکار کی صورت میں صلح کا مدعی کے حق میں علی الاطلاق معاوضہ کے معنی میں ہونا غیر مسلم ہے اس لئے کہ اگر مدعی نے مدعی علیہ کو بطریق صلح کوئی چیز دے کر عین شئی لے لی تو یہ صلح جائز ہے۔ جیسا کہ فقہاء نے تصریح کی ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ مدعی کے حق میں معاوضہ کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مدعی کا زعم تو یہ ہے کہ جس معین کا دعویٰ اس نے کیا ہے وہ اس کا حق ہے ولا يتصور ان يعارض انسان ملك نفسه. بلکہ اس صورت
He said: Sulh from silence and denial is, with respect to the defendant, for redeeming the oath and cutting off the dispute, and with respect to the plaintiff, for the meaning of exchange (mu'awadah) for the reason we have stated. And it is permissible that the ruling of the contract differs in respect to them, just as the ruling of iqalah differs in respect to the two contracting parties and others. This is obvious in the case of denial, and similarly in silence because it carries the possibility of admission and denial, so its being a compensation (iwad) in his right is not established due to doubt. He said: And when he makes sulh from a house (sulh 'an dar), pre-emption (shuf'ah) is not obligatory in it. He (the commentator) said: Its meaning is when it is from denial or silence, because he takes it as his original right and pays the money to ward off the plaintiff's dispute, and the plaintiff's belief does not bind him. Contrary to when he makes sulh on a house (sulh 'ala dar), where pre-emption is obligatory, because the plaintiff takes it as compensation for property, so it is an exchange in his right, and thus pre-emption becomes binding upon him due to his affirmation (iqrar), even if the defendant denies it.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses sulh (compromise) in cases where the defendant either remains silent (sukūt) or denies (inkār) the plaintiff's claim. The author explains that such a sulh has a dual legal nature: from the defendant's perspective, it is a payment to avoid taking an oath (iftidā' al-yamīn) and to end the dispute; from the plaintiff's perspective, it is an exchange (mu'āwaḍah) because he believes he is receiving compensation for what he considers his right. The ruling can differ for the two parties, like the case of iqālah (mutual rescission) which is a rescission for the original parties but a new sale for third parties. The passage then applies this principle to the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah). If a person makes a sulh 'an dār (from a house) — meaning he settles a claim related to the house by paying money but the house remains with him — then shuf'ah is not obligatory on him as a seller because he is not selling the house; he is retaining it as his own and paying to stop the dispute. However, if the sulh is 'alā dār (on a house) — meaning the plaintiff takes the house as compensation for property — then shuf'ah is obligatory because it is treated as a sale from the plaintiff's perspective. The commentary elaborates on the logical possibility of a single contract having different rulings for different parties, citing examples from iqālah and marriage. A further note (tanbīh) clarifies that the plaintiff's belief that he is receiving his own right does not make the sulh a pure exchange; for instance, if the plaintiff gives something to the defendant and takes the very item he claims, the sulh is valid even though it is not an exchange in reality because one cannot exchange one's own property with oneself.

Key Terms
صلح عن السكوت (ṣulḥ ʿan al-sukūt): A compromise made when the defendant remains silent on the claim, without admission or denial.
صلح عن الإنكار (ṣulḥ ʿan al-inkār): A compromise made when the defendant denies the claim.
شفعة (shufʿah): Pre-emption; the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase property sold to an outsider.
إقالة (iqālah): Mutual rescission of a sale contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sulh 'an dar (from a house) with denial, is shuf'ah (pre-emption) obligatory on the defendant?
A) Yes, because the house is transferred.
B) No, because the defendant retains the house as his original right and pays to avoid the oath.
C) Yes, if the plaintiff believes it is a sale.
D) No, only if the defendant admits the claim.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, sulh from denial or silence is not a sale from the defendant's perspective, so it does not trigger shuf'ah; only sulh 'ala dar (on a house as compensation) does.

Sulh from Silence or Denial: Dual Nature for Parties
States ruling on sulh from silence/denial with dual legal nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the dual legal nature of sulh from silence/denial for plaintiff and defendant, and explain why shuf'ah does not apply.

Core Idea
Sulh from silence/denial is a ransom for defendant, an exchange for plaintiff.

This passage addresses a subtle point in Hanafi contract law: a single sulh (compromise) agreement can have different legal effects for each party when the defendant either denies the claim or remains silent. The commentator resolves the apparent paradox by analogy to iqalah (rescission of sale), showing that the contract's nature can vary depending on the party's perspective. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying shuf'ah (pre-emption) rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its dual categorization
The passage states that sulh from silence/denial is, for the defendant, a ransom to avoid taking an oath and to end the dispute. For the plaintiff, it is a compensation for his claimed right. This is the core ruling.
Note the asymmetry: the same contract has a different legal nature for each party.
2
Analyze the proof: analogy to iqalah
The commentator argues that a contract can have different rulings for different parties, citing iqalah (rescission) as an example: for the original parties it is a rescission, for a third party it is a new sale. This proves that a single contract can have dual effects.
This is a qiyas (analogical reasoning) based on an established ruling in sales.
3
Apply to silence vs. denial
The rule applies to both denial and silence. In denial, the defendant's position is clear. In silence, since it may imply either acknowledgment or denial, doubt prevents considering it as a compensation (mu'awadah) for the defendant.
Hanafis treat silence as ambiguous, not as admission.
4
Contrast with sulh by acknowledgment
If the plaintiff instead makes a sulh where he explicitly takes a property in exchange for dropping his claim (i.e., an acknowledged right), then shuf'ah applies because it is a pure exchange.
This distinction shows the practical consequence: shuf'ah turns on whether the defendant is 'selling' or 'ransoming'.
5
Derive the shuf'ah consequence
From the dual nature, the passage concludes that shuf'ah does not apply in sulh from silence/denial. The defendant is not selling the property; he is paying to end the plaintiff's claim. The plaintiff's belief does not alter the contract's objective nature.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical outcome) that differs from other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَالصُّلْحُ عَنِ السُّكُوتِ وَالْإِنْكَارِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ لِافْتِدَاءِ الْيَمِينِ وَقَطْعِ الْحُصُومَةِ وَفِي حَقِ الْمُدَّعَى لِمَعْنَى الْمُعَاوَضَةِ لِمَا بَيَّنَا وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَخْتَلِفَ حُكْمُ الْعَقْدِ فِي حَقِهِمَا كَمَا يَخْتَلِفُ حُكْمُ الْإِقَالَةِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُتَعَاقِدَيْنِ وَغَيْرِهِمَا وَهَذَا فِي الْإِنْكَارِ ظَاهِرٌ وَكَذَا فِي السُّكُوتِ لِأَنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ الْإِقْرَارَ وَالْجُحُودُ فَلَا يَثْبُتُ كَوْنُهُ عِوَضًا فِي حَقِهِ بِالشَّكِ. قَالَ وَإِذَا صَالَحَ عَنْ دَارٍ لَمْ يَجِبْ فِيهَا الشُّفْعَةُ قَالَ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا كَانَ عَنْ اِنْكَارٍ أَوْ سُكُوتٍ لِأَنَّهُ يَأْخُذُهَا عَلَى أَصْلِ حَقِّهِ وَيَدْفَعُ الْمَالَ دَفْعًا لِحُصُومَةِ الْمُدَّعَى وَزَعِمَ الْمُدَّعَى لَا يَلْزَمُه بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا صَالَحَ عَلَى دَارٍ حَيْثُ يَجِبُ فِيهَا الشُّفْعَةُ لِاَنَّ الْمُدَّعَى يَأْخُذْهَا عِوَضًا عَنِ الْمَالِ فَكَانَ مُعَاوَضَةً فِي حَقِّهِ فَيَلْزَمُهُ الشُّفْعَةُ بِإِقْزَارِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ يُكَذِّبُهُ
He said: Sulh from silence and denial is, in the right of the defendant, for ransoming the oath and cutting off the dispute, and in the right of the plaintiff, for the meaning of compensation, as we have explained. And it is permissible that the ruling of the contract differs in their right, just as the ruling of iqalah differs in the right of the two contracting parties and others. And this is apparent in denial, and similarly in silence, because it admits of both acknowledgment and denial, so its being a compensation in his right is not established due to doubt. He said: When one makes sulh regarding a house, shuf'ah is not obligatory in it. He said: Its meaning is when it is from denial or silence, because he takes it on the basis of his original right, and pays the money to repel the plaintiff's dispute, and the plaintiff's belief is not binding upon him. Contrary to when he makes sulh upon a house, where shuf'ah is obligatory, because the plaintiff takes it as compensation for the property, so it is a mu'awadah in his right, so shuf'ah becomes obligatory by his acknowledgment, even if the defendant denies him.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Hidayah, expanded by the commentator. It clarifies that sulh (compromise) when the defendant remains silent or denies the claim has a dual legal nature. For the defendant, it is a ransom to avoid taking an oath and to end the dispute; for the plaintiff, it is a compensation for his claimed right. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: how can a single contract have two different natures? He answers by analogy with iqalah (rescission of sale), which is a rescission for the parties but a new sale for others. Similarly, sulh from silence/denial is a mu'awadah (exchange) for the plaintiff but a fidya (ransom) for the defendant. In the case of silence, it is not clear whether it implies acknowledgment or denial; since doubt exists, it is not considered a compensation in the defendant's right. The passage then applies this to shuf'ah (pre-emption): if sulh is from silence/denial, no shuf'ah is due because the defendant is not selling but simply paying to end the dispute. However, if the sulh is structured as an exchange (e.g., plaintiff gives up his claim in return for a house), then shuf'ah applies because it is a sale-like transaction.

Key Terms
الصلح (al-sulh): A contract to end a dispute by mutual consent, with or without compensation.
السكوت (al-sukut): Defendant's silence in response to a claim, which may imply either acknowledgment or denial.
الإنكار (al-inkar): Defendant's explicit denial of the claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, why is shuf'ah not wajib in sulh from silence or denial?
A) Because the defendant is not selling the property.
B) Because the plaintiff has no right to shuf'ah.
C) Because the sulh is void.
D) Because the property is not owned by the defendant.

Key Takeaway
Sulh from silence/denial is a ransom for the defendant and compensation for the plaintiff; shuf'ah does not apply.

Istihqaq After Sulh: Acknowledgment vs. Silence/Denial
Ruling on istihqaq after sulh with distinction between acknowledgment and denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on istihqaq after a sulh based on whether the sulh was with acknowledgment or with silence/denial, and apply the proportional refund rule.

Core Idea
Sulh with acknowledgment is an exchange; sulh from denial ends a dispute—istihqaq unravels them differently.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi distinction: what happens when a third party proves ownership of property that was the subject of a sulh (compromise). The ruling hinges on the nature of the sulh—whether it was based on the defendant's acknowledgment of the claim (considered an absolute exchange, mu'awadah) or on silence/denial (a payment to end the dispute). Understanding this distinction is critical for correctly applying the rules of istihqaq in mu'awadat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of sulh
The passage distinguishes sulh 'an iqrar (from acknowledgment) and sulh 'an sukun aw inkar (from silence or denial). In the first, the defendant admits the claim; in the second, he pays to end the dispute without admitting liability.
This classification determines the legal effect of subsequent istihqaq.
2
Apply the qiyas to sale
Sulh with acknowledgment is an absolute exchange (mu'awadah mutlaqah), analogous to a sale. Therefore, istihqaq operates like in a sale: the defendant gets a proportional refund of the compensation (if part of the subject matter is claimed).
The illa (effective cause) is that both are pure exchanges.
3
Analyze the effect for sulh from denial
Since the defendant paid only to stop the dispute, if the entire disputed property is claimed by a third party, he gets back the full compensation because the purpose (ending the dispute) is defeated. If part is claimed, he gets back a proportional refund and may resume the dispute over that part.
The underlying principle: the compensation was for dropping the claim, which becomes meaningless if the claimant had no right.
4
Distinguish from a sale made under denial
The passage contrasts: if a defendant sells something to the plaintiff while denying the claim, that sale itself is an acknowledgment of the right. Not so with sulh, which may occur solely to end the dispute.
This shows the specificity of sulh's purpose.
5
Consider the case where the substitute perishes
If the compensation perishes before delivery, the same rules apply as in istihqaq for both types of sulh.
The ruling remains consistent with the underlying legal nature.

قَالَ وَإِذَا كَانَ الصُّلْحُ عَنْ إِقْرَارِ وَاسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَ الْمَصَالِحٍ عَنْهُ رَجَعَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ بِحِصَّتِةِ ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْعِوَضِ لِأَنَّهُ مُعَاوَضَةٌ مُطْلَقَةٌ كَالْبَيْعِ وَحُكْمُ الْاِسْتِحْقَاقِ فِى الْبَيْعِ هَذَا وَإِنْ وَقَعَ الصُّلْحُ عَنْ سُكُوتٍ أَوْ إِنْكَارِ فَاسْتَحَقَّ الْمُتَنَازَعَ فِيْهِ رَجَعَ الْمُدَّعَى بِالْخُصُومَةِ وَرَدَّ الْعِوَضَ لِاَنَّ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ مَا بَذَلَ الْعِوَضَ إِلَّا لِيَدْفَعَ الْحُصُوْمَةَ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ فَإِذَا ظَهَرَ الْإِسْتِحْقَاقُ تَبِيَّنَ أَنْ لَا خُصُومَةَ لَهُ فَيَبْقَى الْعِوَضُ فِي يَدِهِ غَيْرِ مُشْتَمِلٍ عَلَى غَرْضِهِ فَيَسْتَرِدُّهُ وَإِنِ اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَ ذَلِكَ رَدَّ حِصَّتَهُ وَ رَجَعَ بِالْحُصُومَةِ فِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ خَلَا الْعِوَضُ فِي هَذَا الْقَدْرِ عَنِ الْعَرْضِ وَلَوِ اسْتَحَقَّ الْمَصَالِحَ عَلَيْهِ عَنْ إِقْرَارٍ رَجَعَ بِكُلِّ الْمَصَالِحَ عَنْهُ لِأَنَّهُ مُبَادَلَةٌ وَإِنِ اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَهُ رَجَعَ بِحِمَّتِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ الصُّلْحُ عَنْ اِنْكَارِ أَوْ سُكُوتٍ رَجَعَ إِلَى الدَّعُوىٰ فِي كُلِّهِ أَوْ بِقَدْرِ الْمُسْتَحَقَّ إِذَا اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَهُ لِاَنَّ الْمُبْدَلَ فِيهِ هُوَ الدَّعْوَى وَهَذَا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا بَاعَ مِنْهُ عَلَى الْإِنْكَارِ شَيْئًا حَيْثُ يَرْجِعُ بِالْمُدَّعِي لَأَنَّ الْاِقْدَامَ عَلَى الْبَيْعِ إِقْرَارٌ مِنْهُ بِالْحَقِّ لَهُ وَلَا كَذلِكَ الصُّلْحُ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ يَقَعُ لِدَفْعِ الْحُصُومَةِ وَلَوْ هَلَكَ بَدَلُ الصُّلْحُ قَبْلَ التَّسْلِيمِ فَالْجَوَابُ فِيهِ كَالْجَوَابِ فِي الْإِسْتِحْقَاقِ فِي الْفَصْلَيْنِ
He said: When the sulh is from acknowledgment and part of the sulh subject matter is claimed (by a third party), the defendant takes back that share of the compensation, because it is an absolute exchange like a sale, and the ruling of istihqaq in sale is this. And if the sulh occurs from silence or denial, and the disputed item is claimed, the plaintiff returns the dispute and gives back the compensation, because the defendant only gave the compensation to repel the dispute from himself. So when the entitlement is revealed, it becomes clear that he has no dispute, so the compensation remains in his hand without achieving his purpose, so he takes it back. And if part of that is claimed, he returns its share and returns to the dispute over it, because the compensation is devoid of the purpose to that extent. And if the sulh subject matter is claimed (when it is) from acknowledgment, he takes back the entire subject matter because it is an exchange. And if part of it is claimed, he takes back its share. And if the sulh is from denial or silence, he returns to the claim in its entirety or to the extent of what is claimed, if part is claimed, because what is exchanged is the claim. And this is contrary to when he sells something from him upon denial, where he returns (the sale) with the plaintiff? because undertaking the sale is an acknowledgment from him of the right for him. Not so with sulh, because it may occur to repel the dispute. And if the substitute of the sulh perishes before delivery, the answer in it is like the answer in istihqaq in the two cases.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on istihqaq (a third party proving ownership) after a sulh. It distinguishes between two types of sulh: with acknowledgment (iqrar) and with silence/denial. When the sulh is based on the defendant's acknowledgment of the claim, it is considered a pure exchange (mu'awadah mutlaqah), akin to a sale. Therefore, if a third party proves ownership of part of the sulh subject matter, the defendant is entitled to a proportional refund of the compensation he paid. This is analogous to istihqaq in a sale. On the other hand, if the sulh was from silence or denial, the defendant's payment was only to end the dispute. If the entire disputed property is claimed by another, the defendant gets back the entire compensation because the purpose (ending the dispute) is defeated. If only part is claimed, he gets back a corresponding portion and may renew the dispute over that part. The passage also contrasts sulh with a sale made under denial: if a defendant sells something while denying the claim, that sale itself is an acknowledgment of the plaintiff's right, so the ruling differs. Finally, it states that if the sulh substitute (the compensation) perishes before delivery, the same rules apply as in istihqaq.

Key Terms
الاستحقاق (al-istihqaq): A third party proving ownership of the property that is the subject of the sulh or the compensation.
المعاوضة المطلقة (al-mu'awadah al-mutlaqah): An absolute exchange where each party gives something in return for something else without any additional consideration.
الصلح عن إقرار (al-sulh 'an iqrar): A compromise based on the defendant's acknowledgment of the claim.
الصلح عن سكوت أو إنكار (al-sulh 'an sukun aw inkar): A compromise made while the defendant remains silent or denies the claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a third party proves ownership of the entire disputed property after a sulh from denial, what does the defendant get?
A) He keeps the compensation and the dispute ends.
B) He gets back the full compensation and resumes the dispute.
C) He gets nothing because he denied the claim.
D) He gets back half the compensation.

Key Takeaway
The effect of istihqaq after sulh depends on whether the sulh was with acknowledgment (exchange) or from denial (dispute termination), leading to proportional refund in the former and full refund in the latter.

Shuf'a Not Obligatory in Sulh with Denial or Silence
Ruling that shuf'a is not established in sulh when the defendant denies or remains silent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shuf'a in sulh transactions and apply the principle that the defendant's perspective as non-purchaser prevents shuf'a from being established against him.

Core Idea
In sulh with denial or silence, the defendant is not buying—he retains his original right; therefore shuf'a is not established against him.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling: when a property dispute is settled via sulh (compromise), whether the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) applies depends entirely on the role of the party. For the defendant who gives consideration to end the dispute, he is not purchasing the property but rather redeeming his own claim—so no shuf'a. For the plaintiff who receives property, he is receiving compensation, which is treated like a purchase, so shuf'a may apply. Understanding these perspectives is essential to correctly applying the rules of shuf'a.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Parties' Legal Positions
The passage describes a dispute where one person claims a house from another. The defendant either denies the claim or remains silent. The plaintiff asserts ownership.
Sulh with denial or silence is distinct from sulh with acknowledgment (iqrar).
2
Determine the Nature of the Sulh for Each Party
For the defendant, the sulh is a means to retain what he already considers his own property; he is not buying it from the plaintiff. For the plaintiff, the sulh is a compensation for his claimed right—he considers it a purchase.
The defendant 'redeems his oath' (fidyat yamin) while the plaintiff receives 'compensation' (mu'awada).
3
Apply the Principle 'A Person is Held to His Own Belief'
The plaintiff's belief that the property belongs to him does not bind the defendant. The defendant's own belief that it is his original right governs the transaction for him.
Arabic: 'al-mar'u innama yu'khadhu bima yaz'umuhu wa la yalzimuhu zannu ghayrihi.'
4
Differentiate the Two Scenarios
If the defendant gives a house to settle a property claim, from his perspective it is not a sale, so no shuf'a. If the plaintiff receives a house via sulh, it is compensation for him, so shuf'a is established.
The ruling distinguishes based on who is receiving property in the sulh.
5
Analogize to a Claim of Purchase
The passage provides an analogy: if a person claims to have bought a house, even if the seller denies, the pre-emptor can take it. This supports the principle that a claim is evidence for the claimant himself.
This qiyas (analogy) reinforces that the plaintiff's assertion makes the sulh a purchase in his regard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله لم يحب فيها الشفعة مدعی کے حق میں صلح ذکور کے معاوضہ ہونے اور مدعلی علیہ کے حق میں فدیہ یمین ہوئے پر متفرع ہے۔ مسئلہ اور کی توضیح یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے دوسرے پر گھر کا دعویٰ کیا۔ اور مدعلی علیہ نے اس کا انکار کیا یا وہ خاموش رہا۔ پھر اس نے کچھ دے کر گھر کے معاملہ میں صلح کر لی تو اس گھر میں شفعہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مدعی علیہ اس کو اپنے اصلی حق کی بنا پر لے رہا ہے نہ یہ کہ وہ اس سے خرید رہا ہے۔ البتہ مدعی ضرور اس کو اپنے اعتقاد میں معاوضہ سمجھتا ہے مگر مدعی کا یہ اعتقاد علی علیه پرلازم نہیں لان المرء انما يو أخذ بمانی زعمه ولا يلزمه زعم غيره اور اگر مدعی نے مال کا دعویٰ کیا اور مدعی علیہ نے ایک گھر دے کر صلح کرلی تو اس میں شفعہ واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مدعی اس کو اپنے مال کا عوض سمجھ کر لے رہا ہے تو یہ اس کے حق میں معاوضہ ہوا لہذا شفعہ واجب ہوگا۔ اگر چہ مدعلی علیہ اس کو جھوٹا بتلاتا ہے۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر کوئی شخص یہ کہے کہ میں نے یہ مکان فلاں سے خریدا ہے اور فلاں منکر ہے تو شفیع اس کو شفعہ میں لے سکتا ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر یہ دعوی کیا کہ اس نے اپنا مکان فلاں کے ہاتھ فروخت کیا ہے اور وہ انکار کر لے تب بھی شفعہ میں لے سکتا ہے۔ لان زعمه حجة في حق نفسه
His statement: 'Shuf'a is not obligatory in it' is subsidiary to the fact that sulh is a compensation for the plaintiff and a redemption of oath for the defendant. Explanation of the issue: A person claims a house from another. The defendant denies or remains silent. Then he gives something and settles regarding the house. In this, shuf'a is not obligatory because the defendant is taking it based on his original right, not that he is buying it from him. However, the plaintiff certainly considers it as compensation in his belief, but the plaintiff's belief is not binding upon the defendant, because a person is only held to what he believes [on his own], and the belief of another is not binding on him. And if the plaintiff claimed property and the defendant gave a house and settled, then shuf'a is obligatory therein. Because the plaintiff is taking it as compensation for his property, so it is compensation for him; therefore shuf'a is obligatory. Even if the defendant claims he is lying. Do you not see that if a person says, 'I bought this house from so-and-so' and the other denies it, the pre-emptor can take it in pre-emption? Similarly, if he claimed that he sold his house to so-and-so and he denies it, even then he can take it in pre-emption. Because his claim is evidence for himself.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage addresses the application of shuf'a (pre-emption) in sulh settlements. The ruling distinguishes between the perspective of the defendant and the plaintiff. When the defendant gives something to settle a claim, from his perspective he is not purchasing the property but rather retaining what he already claims as his own. Therefore, shuf'a does not become obligatory against him. However, from the plaintiff's perspective, he is receiving the property as compensation for his claimed right, so if the plaintiff receives property via sulh, it is considered a purchase in his regard, and shuf'a applies. The passage then analogizes: if someone claims to have bought a house, even if the seller denies, the claim is evidence for the claimant's own right, so shuf'a may apply. This is based on the principle that a person is held to his own assertion, not to the assertion of another.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): The right of pre-emption enabling a co-owner or neighbor to purchase property sold to a third party.
الصلح (al-sulh): A settlement agreement between disputing parties, often involving a consideration (iwad) to end the dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sulh where the defendant gives a house to the plaintiff to settle a property claim, is shuf'a obligatory against the defendant?
A) Yes, because it is like a sale.
B) No, because the defendant retains the property as his original right.
C) Yes, but only if the plaintiff asserts ownership.
D) No, because shuf'a only applies to land.

Key Takeaway
Shuf'a is not established against a defendant who settles a claim via sulh, but may be established for a plaintiff who receives property as compensation.

Istihqaq in Sulh: Effects on Consideration and Claim
Rulings on recovery of consideration when the subject matter is claimed by a third party.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the effects of istihqaq in sulh with acknowledgment versus sulh with silence/denial, and apply the appropriate ruling to recover consideration or resume the original claim.

Core Idea
In sulh, the effect of a third-party claim depends on the nature of the settlement: exchange or litigation avoidance.

When a settlement (sulh) is made and later a third party proves ownership of the disputed property or the consideration, the legal consequences hinge on whether the defendant acknowledged the claim (iqrar) or remained silent/denied (sukt/inkar). This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rules for recovering consideration and resuming disputes, based on the foundational text of Al-Hidayah and its commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Type of Sulh
Determine whether the sulh was based on acknowledgment (iqrar) or on silence/denial (sukt/inkar). This classification dictates the legal nature of the transaction.
Sulh 'an iqrar is a commutative exchange (mu'awada); sulh 'an sukt/inkar is a payment to end litigation.
2
Determine What Is Claimed by a Third Party
Is the third-party claim over the subject matter (musalih 'anhu) or the consideration (musalih 'alayh)? The ruling differs accordingly.
The subject matter is what the dispute was about; the consideration is what the defendant paid.
3
Apply the Ruling for Subject Matter Claim
If the subject matter (or part) is claimed: in iqrar, the defendant recovers proportionate consideration; in sukt/inkar, the plaintiff returns the full (or proportional) consideration and the defendant resumes the claim.
The rationale: in iqrar, it's an exchange; in sukt/inkar, the consideration was to avoid litigation, which failed.
4
Apply the Ruling for Consideration Claim
If the consideration (or part) is claimed: in iqrar, the plaintiff returns the subject matter (or proportional) and resumes the claim; in sukt/inkar, the plaintiff returns to the claim entirely or proportionally.
Here the substitute (badal) is the claim itself in sukt/inkar.
5
Distinguish from Sale
In a sale made despite denial (inkar), the sale itself implies acknowledgment, so the seller cannot resume the claim if the price is claimed. In sulh, this reasoning does not apply because sulh can be purely to end litigation.
This contrast highlights the unique nature of sulh.

صلح مع اقرار ہوئی پھر مصالح عنہ کا کوئی مستحق نکل آیا تو مدعی علیہ اس حصہ کے بقدر اپنا عوض واپس لے گا
قَالَ وَإِذَا كَانَ الصُّلْحُ عَنْ إِقْرَارِ وَاسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَ الْمَصَالِحٍ عَنْهُ رَجَعَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ بِحِصَّتِةِ ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْعِوَضِ لِأَنَّهُ مُعَاوَضَةٌ مُطْلَقَةٌ كَالْبَيْعِ وَحُكْمُ الْاِسْتِحْقَاقِ فِى الْبَيْعِ هَذَا وَإِنْ وَقَعَ الصُّلْحُ عَنْ سُكُوتٍ أَوْ إِنْكَارِ فَاسْتَحَقَّ الْمُتَنَازَعَ فِيْهِ رَجَعَ الْمُدَّعَى بِالْخُصُومَةِ وَرَدَّ الْعِوَضَ لِاَنَّ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ مَا بَذَلَ الْعِوَضَ إِلَّا لِيَدْفَعَ الْحُصُوْمَةَ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ فَإِذَا ظَهَرَ الْإِسْتِحْقَاقُ تَبِيَّنَ أَنْ لَا خُصُومَةَ لَهُ فَيَبْقَى الْعِوَضُ فِي يَدِهِ غَيْرِ مُشْتَمِلٍ عَلَى غَرْضِهِ فَيَسْتَرِدُّهُ وَإِنِ اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَ ذَلِكَ رَدَّ حِصَّتَهُ وَ رَجَعَ بِالْحُصُومَةِ فِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ خَلَا الْعِوَضُ فِي هَذَا الْقَدْرِ عَنِ الْعَرْضِ وَلَوِ اسْتَحَقَّ الْمَصَالِحَ عَلَيْهِ عَنْ إِقْرَارٍ رَجَعَ بِكُلِّ الْمَصَالِحَ عَنْهُ لِأَنَّهُ مُبَادَلَةٌ وَإِنِ اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَهُ رَجَعَ بِحِمَّتِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ الصُّلْحُ عَنْ اِنْكَارِ أَوْ سُكُوتٍ رَجَعَ إِلَى الدَّعُوىٰ فِي كُلِّهِ أَوْ بِقَدْرِ الْمُسْتَحَقَّ إِذَا اسْتَحَقَّ بَعْضَهُ لِاَنَّ الْمُبْدَلَ فِيهِ هُوَ الدَّعْوَى وَهَذَا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا بَاعَ مِنْهُ عَلَى الْإِنْكَارِ شَيْئًا حَيْثُ يَرْجِعُ بِالْمُدَّعِي لَأَنَّ الْاِقْدَامَ عَلَى الْبَيْعِ إِقْرَارٌ مِنْهُ بِالْحَقِّ لَهُ وَلَا كَذلِكَ الصُّلْحُ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ يَقَعُ لِدَفْعِ الْحُصُومَةِ وَلَوْ هَلَكَ بَدَلُ الصُّلْحُ قَبْلَ التَّسْلِيمِ فَالْجَوَابُ فِيهِ كَالْجَوَابِ فِي الْإِسْتِحْقَاقِ فِي الْفَصْلَيْنِ ترجمہ جب صلح مع اقرار ہو اور کچھ مصالح عنہ کسی اور کا ثابت ہو تو مد علی علیہ اس کے بقدر عوض امیں سے واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو بیع کی طرح مطلق معاوضہ ہے اور بیع می استحقاق کا حکم یہی ہے اور اگر واقع ہو صلح مع سکوت یا مع انکار پھر متنازع فیہ کا حقدار نکل آئے تو مدعی مقدار سے جھگڑے اور عوض واپس کرے۔ کیونکہ مدعلی علیہ نے مال نہیں دیا مگر اس لئے تا کہ اپنی ذات سے خصومت دور کرے اور جب استحقاق ظاہر ہوا تو یہ واضح ہو گیا که حق خصومت نہیں تھا۔ پس مدعی کے قبضہ میں عوض باقی علیہ کی غرض کو شامل نہیں ہے۔ لہذا واپس لے لے اور اگر بعض حصّہ کا حقدار نکل آیا تو اس کے بقدر واپس کر کے اس میں جی مقدار میں غرض سے خالی ہے اور اگر صلح مع اقرار میں مصالح علیہ کسی کا نکل آئے تو کل مصالح عنہ واپس لے۔ کیونکہ یہ تو مبادلہ تھا اور اگر بعض حصہ مستحق نکلا تو اسی کے بقدر واپس لے اور اگر صلح مع انکار یا مع سکوت ہو تو مدعی پورے یا بقدر مستحق دعوی کی طرف رجوع کرے کیونکہ مبدل اس میں دعوئی ہے اور یہ اس کے خلاف ہے جب مدعی نے اس کے ہاتھ کوئی چیز انکار کے باو بود فروخت کی کی اس میں مدعا واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ بیع پر اقدام کرنا اس کی طرف سے اقرار ہے مدعی کے لئے حق ہونے کا اور صلح میں یہ بات نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ صلح کبھی دفع خصومت کی غرض سے ہوتی تو کل مصالح عنہ کا دعوی کرے اور بعض ہو تو بعض کا کیونکہ مدعی نے جو اپنے دعوئی کو ترک کیا ہے وہ اس لئے کیا ہے تا کہ اس کے قبضہ میں بدل صلح صحیح سالم آئے۔ اور جب وہ دوسرے کا ٹھہرا تو وہ مبدل یعنی دعوئی کی طرف رجوع کرلے گا۔ مگر یہ اس وقت ہے جب بدل صلح مال میں ہو اور سحق نے صلح کو جائز نہ کھا ہو۔ اور اگر ا نے صلح کو جائز نہ بکا کانال بین مدعی کے حوا۔ ۔ کرے اور مستحق مدعی علیہ پر اس کی قیمت میں رجوع کرے اگر وہ ذات القیم میں سے ہو اور اگر بدل صلح دین ہو۔ جیسے درا ہم ودنا نیر اور تکمیل موزوان (بغیر اعیانہا ) تو استحقاق کی وجہ سے صلح باطل نہ ہوگی۔ لیکن اس کے مثل کے ساتھ رجوع کرلے گا۔ کیونکہ استحقاق کی وجہ سے صلح باطل نہ ہوگی۔ لیکن اس کے مثل کے ساتھ رجوع کرے گا۔ کیونکہ استحقاق کی وجہ سے استیفاء باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس گویا اس نے ابھی پورا حق وصول ہی نہیں کیا۔ کذافي شرح الطحاوی (کفایه) قوله وهذا بخلاف ما ... حکم کی مذکورہ تفصیل اس وقت ہے جب عقد صلح میں لفظ بیج کا نظلم نہ ہو اوراگر اس میں بیج کا تنکم ہو۔ مثلا کسی نے
When sulh is with acknowledgment and part of the subject matter (musalih 'anhu) is claimed (by a third party), the defendant recovers his share of the consideration because it is an absolute exchange like sale, and the ruling of istihqaq in sale is this. And if the sulh occurs with silence or denial and then the disputed item is claimed, the plaintiff resumes the dispute and returns the consideration, because the defendant only gave the consideration to remove litigation from himself. So when the claim appears, it becomes clear that there was no litigation for him, thus the consideration remains in his hand not fulfilling his purpose, so he takes it back. And if part of that is claimed, he returns its share and resumes dispute over it because the consideration for this portion is void of purpose. And if the consideration (musalih 'alayh) is claimed in a sulh with acknowledgment, he returns all of the subject matter because it is an exchange. And if part of it is claimed, he returns its share. And if the sulh was with denial or silence, he returns to the claim in whole or to the extent of what is claimed, because the substitute here is the claim. This is contrary to the case where he sells something to him despite denial, where the plaintiff returns [the price] because proceeding to sell is an acknowledgment from him of the right of the other; not so in sulh, because it may occur to remove litigation. And if the consideration of sulh perishes before delivery, the answer in it is like the answer in istihqaq in both sections. Translation: When sulh is with acknowledgment and part of the subject matter is proven to belong to someone else, the defendant recovers the proportion of the consideration. Because this is an absolute exchange like sale, and the ruling of istihqaq in sale is this. And if sulh occurs with silence or denial, then the rightful owner of the disputed item appears, the plaintiff [who received consideration] returns it and disputes with the rightful owner. Because the defendant only gave the consideration to remove litigation from himself, and when istihqaq appears, it becomes clear that the right to litigation did not exist. So the consideration remaining with the plaintiff does not fulfill the defendant's purpose. Therefore he takes it back. And if part of it is claimed, he returns its proportion and resumes dispute over that portion because the consideration for that portion is devoid of purpose. And if in sulh with acknowledgment the consideration (musalih 'alayh) is claimed, the plaintiff returns all of the subject matter because it was an exchange. And if part is claimed, he returns its share. And if sulh was with denial or silence, the plaintiff returns to the claim in whole or to the extent claimed, because the substitute here is the claim. This is contrary to the case where he sold something to him despite denial, where the plaintiff [the seller] takes back the sold item because proceeding to sell is an acknowledgment of the right of the buyer; not so in sulh because sulh may occur for removing litigation. And if the consideration perishes before delivery, the ruling is the same as in istihqaq in both sections. Elaboration: His statement: 'When sulh is with acknowledgment' – if the defendant acknowledged the claim and then made sulh, and then part of the subject matter (the thing regarding which sulh was made) is proven to belong to a third party and taken from the defendant, the defendant recovers from the plaintiff the proportion of the consideration. Because sulh with acknowledgment is in reality an absolute exchange like sale, and the ruling of exchange is that upon istihqaq, one recovers proportionally. Example: Zayd claims a house in 'Amr's possession, and after acknowledgment 'Amr settles with Zayd for one hundred dirhams; then half the house is proven to belong to someone else. 'Amr recovers fifty dirhams from Zayd. His statement: 'And if sulh occurs with silence...' – And if sulh with silence or denial, then the disputed item appears to belong to someone else. Example: 'Amr has a house; Zayd claims it as his; 'Amr denies or remains silent; then he gives one hundred dirhams and settles. Thereafter the house is proven to belong to someone else. Then Zayd returns the one hundred dirhams to 'Amr and disputes with the rightful owner. Because 'Amr gave the dirhams to eliminate the quarrel and keep the subject matter without dispute; when it appears to be owned by another, his purpose is not achieved, also it becomes clear that Zayd's claim against 'Amr was baseless. So he takes back the dirhams, and Zayd disputes with the rightful owner as he now stands in place of the defendant. If part of the disputed item is claimed, he returns proportion of the consideration and the claimant disputes over that portion because the defendant's purpose is not met for that portion. His statement: 'And if the consideration (musalih 'alayh) is claimed in sulh with acknowledgment' – if the consideration (badal al-sulh) is proven to belong to someone else, the plaintiff returns to his claim, i.e., re-files the lawsuit. If the entire consideration is proven to be another's, he claims the entire subject matter; if part, he claims that part. Because the plaintiff abandoned his claim only so that he would receive the consideration soundly. When it turns out to be another's, he returns to the substitute, i.e., the claim. But this is when the consideration is property ('ayn) and the sulh is not void. And if the sulh is not void? [Unclear] He may return... and the rightful owner may claim its value from the defendant if it is an item of value. And if the consideration is debt like dirhams and dinars and complete weight (without specific coins), then istihqaq does not void the sulh, but he recovers its equivalent because istihqaq voids the receipt (isti'fa'), so it is as if he has not yet received his full right. (Kifayah from Sharh al-Tahawi) His statement: 'This is contrary to...' The detailed ruling mentioned is when the word 'sale' is not employed in the sulh contract. If the word 'sale' is used, e.g., someone... [incomplete]
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rulings on the consequences of istihqaq (a third party proving ownership) in the context of sulh. It distinguishes between three types of sulh: with acknowledgment (iqrar), with silence (sukt), and with denial (inkar). In sulh with acknowledgment, the transaction is treated as an exchange (mu'awadah) like a sale. Therefore, if part of the subject matter (musalih 'anhu) is taken by a rightful owner, the defendant can recover the proportionate consideration. In sulh with silence or denial, the consideration is seen as a payment to avoid litigation. If the disputed item is claimed by another, the plaintiff must return the full consideration to the defendant and resume the claim against the rightful owner, because the defendant's purpose (ending the dispute) was not achieved. The passage also covers the situation where the consideration itself (musalih 'alayh) is claimed: in sulh with acknowledgment, the plaintiff returns the subject matter and resumes his original claim; in sulh with denial/silence, he returns to the claim entirely or proportionally. A key distinction is made with sale: if someone sells a item to a person despite denying that person's claim, the sale itself is an acknowledgment, so the seller cannot later claim the item back if it is taken; but in sulh, because the aim is to remove litigation, the intention is not necessarily acknowledgment. Finally, if the consideration perishes before delivery, the same istihqaq rulings apply as if the consideration had been claimed.

Key Terms
الاستحقاق (al-istihqaq): A third party proving ownership of property that is the subject of a sulh or sale, leading to recovery or adjustment of the transaction.
المصالح عنه (al-musalih 'anhu): The property or right that is the subject matter of the sulh; what the dispute was about.
المصالح عليه (al-musalih 'alayh): The consideration (iwad) given by the defendant to the plaintiff in a sulh.
معاوضة (mu'awadah): A commutative transaction where one thing is exchanged for another, like a sale.
خصومة (khusumah): Litigation or dispute; in sulh 'an inkar/sukt, the payment is made to end the khusumah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In sulh with acknowledgment (iqrar), if half of the disputed property is later proven to belong to a third party, what happens?
A) The sulh becomes void entirely and the claim is resumed.
B) The defendant recovers half the consideration he paid.
C) The plaintiff keeps the entire consideration.
D) The third party must give permission for the sulh.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between sulh with acknowledgment (proportional recovery) and sulh with silence/denial (full recovery and resumption of claim) when a third party proves ownership, because the nature of the payment differs.

Proportional Refund in Sulh with Acknowledgment
Explains ruling when part of the settled property is claimed by another after sulh with acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on proportional refund in sulh with acknowledgment when part of the subject matter is taken, and explain the qiyas on sale that justifies it.

Core Idea
In sulh with acknowledgment, the defendant gets proportional refund for taken property because it is a pure exchange like sale.

When a defendant acknowledges a claim and then settles, the Hanafi school treats this sulh as an exchange contract (mu'awadah). This means that if part of the settled property is later proven to belong to a third party, the defendant can reclaim a proportional part of the consideration. The following passage from al-Hidayah explains the ruling and its proof through analogy to sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The defendant takes back a proportional part of the badal (consideration) when part of the maslah 'anhu (subject matter) is taken by a mustahiq (rightful owner).
This only applies to sulh with iqrar (acknowledgment).
2
Understand the Reasoning (Ta'lil)
The reason (sabab) is that sulh with acknowledgment is a pure exchange (mu'awadah mutlaqah), like a sale.
The Hanafi school emphasizes the exchange nature over the idea of release (ibra').
3
Apply the Analogy (Qiyas) to Sale
In a sale, if part of the sold item is taken, the buyer recovers a proportional part of the price. The same principle applies here because both are exchange contracts.
The common illa (effective cause) is the exchange of specific property for specific consideration.
4
Consider the Example
Zayd claims a house from 'Amr. 'Amr acknowledges and pays 100 dirhams in sulh. Half the house is later proven to belong to Khalid. 'Amr recovers 50 dirhams from Zayd.
This illustrates the proportional refund rule clearly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح قوله اذا كان الصُّلْحُ عن اقرار اگر مدعی علیہ نے مدعی کے دعوے کا اقرار کر کے صلح کی پھر مصالح عنہ یعنی جس چیز کی طرف سے صلح کی تھی اس میں سے کچھ حصہ کسی نے اپنا استحقاق ثابت کر کے مدعی علیہ سے لے لیا تو مدعلی علیہ اس حصہ کے بقدر اپنا عوض واپس لے گا۔ اس لئے کہ صلح باقرار در حقیقت بیع کی طرح معاوضہ مطلقہ ہے اور معاوضہ کا حکم یہی ہے کہ بوقت استحقاق رجوع بقدر مستحق ہوتا ہے۔ اس کی مثال یوں سمجھو کہ زید نے ایک مکان کا دعوی کیا جو عمرو کے قبضہ میں ہے اور عمرو نے اقرار کے بعد زید سے ایک سو درہم پر صلح کر لی پھر نصف مکان کسی دوسرے کا نکل آیا تو عمرو زید سے پچاس درہم واپس لے لے گا۔
Explanation of his statement: When the sulh is with acknowledgment: If the defendant acknowledged the plaintiff's claim and made sulh, then some part of the maslah ‘anhu (the thing for which sulh was made) was proven to belong to another and he took it from the defendant, then the defendant shall take back his consideration (badal) proportional to that part. This is because sulh with acknowledgment is in reality an absolute exchange like a sale, and the rule of an exchange is that at the time of istihqaq, recourse is proportional to what was taken. An example: Zayd claimed a house in the possession of ‘Amr, and ‘Amr after acknowledgment made sulh with Zayd for one hundred dirhams; then half the house turned out to belong to someone else; so ‘Amr will take back fifty dirhams from Zayd.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof: it states the Hanafi rule for sulh with acknowledgment (iqrar) when part of the subject matter (maslah ‘anhu) is later proven to belong to a third party. The key principle is that sulh with iqrar is treated as a pure exchange (mu‘awadah mutlaqah), exactly like a sale (bay‘). Therefore, if the defendant paid consideration (badal) for the subject matter, and part of it is taken away by a rightful owner (mustahiq), the defendant can reclaim a proportional part of the consideration back from the plaintiff. The reasoning (ta‘lil) is qiyas on sale: in a sale, if part of the sold item is subject to istihqaq, the buyer recovers part of the price. The example illustrates: Zayd claims a house, ‘Amr acknowledges and gives 100 dirhams in sulh; if half the house is proven for another, ‘Amr gets back 50 dirhams. This ruling is within the Hanafi madhhab and is consistent with the principle of 'recourse proportional to the right'.

Key Terms
صلح عن اقرار (ṣulḥ ‘an iqrār): A compromise (sulh) made after the defendant acknowledges the plaintiff's claim; it is treated as an exchange (mu‘awadah) like a sale.
مصالح عنه (muṣālaḥ ‘anhu): The subject matter of the compromise – the property or right over which the dispute is settled.
بدل صلح (badal ṣulḥ): The consideration given by the defendant to the plaintiff in exchange for settling the claim.
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): The proven right of a third party to the property, causing it to be taken from the possessor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If Zayd claims a house from ‘Amr, ‘Amr acknowledges and makes sulh for 100 dirhams, then half the house is proven to belong to Khalid, what is the ruling?
A) ‘Amr gets back 100 dirhams
B) ‘Amr gets back 50 dirhams
C) ‘Amr gets nothing back
D) ‘Amr must pay another 50 dirhams to Zayd

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, sulh with acknowledgment is a pure exchange, so partial istihqaq of the subject matter entitles the defendant to proportional refund of the consideration.

Sulh with Silence/Denial: Effect of Istihqaq on Consideration
Ruling with ta'lil on consequence of istihqaq in sulh with silence/denial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the disputed property is taken from the defendant after sulh with silence or denial, and explain the reasoning based on the purpose of the contract.

Core Idea
In sulh with silence/denial, if the subject matter is owned by another, the consideration must be returned because the defendant's purpose (peaceful possession) failed.

You are already familiar with sulh (compromise) as a contract to end a dispute. But what happens when the property that was the subject of the dispute turns out to belong to someone else? In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling for sulh made with silence or denial—where the defendant does not acknowledge the claim. Unlike sulh with acknowledgment, here the consideration is not earned by the plaintiff if the property is taken by the rightful owner. Let us follow the reasoning of the Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Start by recognizing the specific scenario: sulh is made with either silence (sukut) or denial (inkar) from the defendant, and then the entire disputed property (mutanaza' fih) is proven to belong to a third party.
The ruling differs from sulh with acknowledgment (iqrar).
2
Understand the purpose (maqsad) of the sulh
The purpose of this sulh is not a true exchange (mu'awadah) but an agreement to end the dispute, allowing the defendant to keep the property without further litigation. The consideration (badal) is given to secure peace.
This purpose is central to the ruling.
3
Apply the reasoning when the entire property is taken
When the property turns out to belong to a third party, the defendant's purpose of peaceful possession is completely defeated. Moreover, the plaintiff's claim against the defendant is revealed as baseless. Therefore, the plaintiff must return the full consideration to the defendant and then contest with the rightful owner (mustahiq) as a substitute for the original defendant.
The plaintiff stands in place of the defendant (qa'im maqam) against the mustahiq.
4
Distinguish the partial istihqaq case
If only part of the disputed property is taken by the mustahiq, the refund is proportional to that part. The plaintiff returns that portion of the consideration and may contest only for the part taken, because the defendant's purpose failed only for that fraction.
The refund is calculated by proportion (bi-qadrihi).

Source Text

قوله وان وقع الصُّلْحُ عن سكوت ..... اور اگر صلح بسکوت یا با نکار ہوئی پھر متنازع فیہ کسی اور کی نکل آئی۔ مثلا عمرو کے قبضہ میں ایک مکان ہے۔ زید نے اس کا دعویٰ کیا کہ یہ میرا ہے۔ عمرو نے اس کا انکار کیا یا وہ خاموش رہا۔ پھر اس نے ایک سو درہم دے کر صلح کر لی۔ اس کے بعد وہ مکان کسی اور کا نکل آیا۔ تو زید نے عمرہ سے جو ایک سو درہم لئے تھے وہ اس کو واپس کر کے مستحق سے خصومت کرے۔ کیونکہ عمرو نے زید کو ایک سو درہم اس لئے دئے تھے تا کہ جھگڑا مٹ جائے اور اس کے پاس مصالح عنہ بلا خصومت باقی رہے اور جب وہ دوسرے کا مملوک نکل آیا تو اس کا مقصد حاصل نہ ہوا نیز یہ بھی ظاہر ہو گیا کہ عمرو کے ساتھ زید کی خصومت بے جاتھی۔ لہذا وہ ایک سو درہم واپس لے گا۔ اور زید مستحق سے جھگڑے گا۔ کیونکہ اب وہ مدعی علیہ کے قائم مقام ہے اور اگر متنازع فیہ کا کچھ حصہ مستحق نکلا تو عوض صلح میں ہے اس کے بقدر واپس دے کر مدعی اتنے ہی میں مستحق سے خصومت کرے کیونکہ اتنے حصہ میں مدعلی علیہ کی غرض حاصل نہیں ہوئی۔
His statement: 'And if the sulh was with silence or denial' – And if the sulh occurred with silence or denial, then the disputed item (mutanaza‘ fih) turned out to belong to someone else. For example, there is a house in possession of ‘Amr. Zayd claimed it saying 'It is mine.' ‘Amr denied it or remained silent. Then he made sulh by giving 100 dirhams. Afterwards, the house turned out to belong to someone else. So Zayd will return the 100 dirhams he took from ‘Amr, and then contest with the rightful owner (mustahiq). Because ‘Amr gave 100 dirhams to Zayd to end the dispute and keep the sulh property without litigation; when it turned out to be owned by another, his purpose was not achieved. It also became clear that Zayd's dispute with ‘Amr was baseless. Therefore, he will take back the 100 dirhams, and Zayd will contest with the mustahiq, because he now stands in place of the defendant. And if only part of the disputed item is taken by the mustahiq, then the plaintiff will return a proportional part of the consideration and contest for that part, because the defendant's objective was not achieved for that part.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with ta‘lil (reasoning) for sulh made when the defendant either denies the claim or remains silent (i.e., does not acknowledge). The rule is different from sulh with acknowledgment. Here, the sulh is not a pure exchange; rather, its purpose is to end the dispute and allow the defendant to keep the property without further litigation. Therefore, if the entire disputed property is later proven to belong to a third party, the plaintiff must return the full consideration to the defendant. The defendant's purpose (sakinah, peaceful possession) is defeated because the property is not his to keep. Additionally, the plaintiff's claim is shown to be baseless against the defendant, so he has no right to retain the consideration. The plaintiff then steps into the defendant's shoes (qaim maqam) to contest with the mustahiq. If only part is taken, the refund is proportional, and the plaintiff may contest for that part only. The reasoning is that the consideration was given to secure peace for the defendant's possession; partial loss means partial failure.

Key Terms
صلح عن سكوت (ṣulḥ ‘an sukūt): A compromise where the defendant remains silent, neither acknowledging nor denying the claim; it is treated as a contract to end dispute, not an exchange.
صلح عن إنكار (ṣulḥ ‘an inkār): A compromise where the defendant denies the claim; same ruling as with silence.
متنازع فيه (mutanāza‘ fīh): The property or right that is the subject of the dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In sulh with denial (inkar), if only part of the disputed property is taken by a third party, what is the correct action?
A) The plaintiff returns the entire consideration and contests for the whole property.
B) The plaintiff returns a proportional part of the consideration and contests for the taken part.
C) The plaintiff keeps the consideration and contests only for the taken part.
D) The plaintiff returns the consideration and does not contest.

Key Takeaway
In sulh with silence/denial, if the subject matter is owned by another, the consideration must be returned proportionally because the purpose of ending the dispute regarding that property was not achieved.
